# CTOX Harness Hardening — Backlog

> Generated from a two-pass, adversarially-verified multi-agent sweep of the harness hot path (126 agents, 87 confirmed findings, 17 rejected by the verifier). Companion to [`harness-hardening-constraints.md`](harness-hardening-constraints.md) — the constraints every fix below must obey.

**How to use:** each entry is a self-contained ticket — anchors, the grounded problem, the fix, its Prüfsatz mapping, and the adversarial verifier's implementation guidance (read it: it often corrects the original finding). For `revise` tickets, the stale original Fix/Change-sketch fields were removed in the re-audit cleanup; the executable scope is the **Canonical scope** + **Verifier guidance**. Tick the box when done.

**Production-ready issue contract:** every ticket now has the fields needed to be worked independently. `keep` tickets use `Fix` + `Change sketch` + `Prüfsatz` as the implementation body. `revise` tickets use `Canonical scope` + `Canonical verification` + `Verifier guidance` as the implementation body (the stale original Fix/Change-sketch fields were removed in the re-audit cleanup).

**Anchors are `file::symbol` or `file:line` as of the sweep (2026-06-13). Line numbers drift — re-grep the symbol before editing.**

**Legend:** 🟠 high impact · 🟡 medium · ⚪ low. Effort S/M/L. `kind` (Pass 2 only): bug · concurrency · design-pattern · architecture · migration-safety · dead-code · missing-test.

**Verifier verdict (per ticket):** `keep` = the fix is accepted as-is (37 of 87). `revise` = the *problem* is real but the **Change sketch** is wrong, too broad, or under-specified → do not execute from the original sketch until it has been normalized against the **Verifier guidance** line (50 of 87). Every ticket is self-rated *high confidence*, which is an LLM judgement, **not** calibrated proof — re-verify against live code before each fix. These `keep`/`revise` badges are the prior sweep; where they disagree with the per-ticket `🔎 Live re-audit` line, the re-audit line wins.

**Definition of done (per ticket):** ① re-grep the anchor (line numbers drift) ② read the live code and confirm the problem still exists ③ for `revise`, take the corrected scope from *Verifier guidance*, not *Change sketch* ④ write the failing test that pins the invariant — Prüfsatz Q10, the test *is* the verification ⑤ make the minimal fix ⑥ `cargo check` + the targeted test ⑦ atomic commit. A ticket is not done until a test pins the invariant.

⚠️ **Coordination:** most P0 fixes touch `src/core/service/service.rs` and `src/core/mission/channels.rs`, where a parallel Codex agent works on `main`. Commit atomically, re-grep anchors before each edit, and do not ride mid-flight core changes.

---

## P0 — recommended triage order (highest leverage first; re-check each scope)

P0 is not a blanket "no-new-mechanism" list. Most items reuse existing idioms; a few high-leverage items require structured plumbing. Re-read the ticket guidance before treating any P0 item as low-risk.

1. [ ] `egress-idempotency · EGRESS-1` — emit `Sending→Sent` on successful founder send (symmetric to the existing failure path)
2. [ ] `failmode-patterns · x2-2` + `x2-1` — stop swallowing the `defer_mission_for_reason` kill-switch and the success-path lease acks (audit currently lies / work silently re-leased)
3. [ ] `concurrency-isolation · X2-1` — make the lease UPDATE a check-and-set inside `BEGIN IMMEDIATE` (stop silent lease theft); idiom exists at `channels.rs:5517`
4. [ ] `concurrency-isolation · X2-3` — close the spawn-budget TOCTOU: count+insert in one IMMEDIATE txn
5. [ ] `compaction-internals · lcm-x1/lcm-x2/lcm-x3` — atomic message persist + propagate count errors instead of `unwrap_or(0/1)`
6. [ ] `queue-lifecycle · queue-2` — idempotent create on a caller-supplied hard key (mirror `tickets.rs:4603`)
7. [ ] `persistence-migration · X2-01` — wrap the destructive `ticket_self_work_items` migration in a txn with row-count verify
8. [ ] `review-outcome · review-1` — gate the terminal no-send close on the structured `ReviewDisposition`, not scraped text
9. [ ] `model-runtime-robustness · gateway-1` — classify local-backend readiness failure as `InfraError` → hold+cooldown
10. [ ] `egress-idempotency · EGRESS-2` — provider idempotency key + durable `draft_pending_send` (no double-send on crash)
11. [ ] `arch-godfiles · X2-01` — add structured Skill-contract plumbing and move the hardcoded `intersolar` deliverable guard out of the router
12. [ ] `turn-loop-context · turnloop-6` — stop swallowing DB errors as 'no boundary' in `detect_durable_state_transition`

The body below is now grouped by the **live re-audit verdict** — work the ✅ DO section first, then ⚠️ REVISE (Verifier-guidance scope only); 🔵 DEFER and ⬜ DROP are audit/cosmetic.

- ⚠️ **REVISE — real, but the original sketch would regress; only the Verifier-guidance scope is safe: 16.**

## ✅ DO — real stability wins (42) — work these first

### `arch-godfiles` · `X2-01` — Single-customer deliverable contract hardcoded as a deterministic FAIL gate in the dispatch/review layer

🏷 Pass 2 · impact **high** · effort **M** · kind **bug** · verifier **keep**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** ✅ **DO — real stability win** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **clear** — Every load-bearing claim is verified in live code. A hardcoded single-customer string ("intersolar") plus magic thresholds (<200 data rows, "PLZ" header) deterministically override the model review verdict as a hard ReviewVerdict::Fail a...

- [ ] **open**
- **Anchors:** `src/core/service/service.rs::spreadsheet_attachment_guard_outcome (6576-6637)`, `src/core/service/service.rs::spreadsheet_guard_failure_outcome (6639)`, `src/core/service/service.rs::inferred_skill_from_message_content (10099) + looks_like_web_extraction_task (10123)`, `src/core/mission/review.rs::CompletionReviewRequest.required_deliverables (139)`, `src/core/skills/skill_store.rs::parse_skill_catalog_metadata`
- **Problem:** spreadsheet_attachment_guard_outcome is wired into review_completion_for_job (service.rs:5125) as a hard ReviewVerdict::Fail gate, but its trigger and pass/fail rule are a hardcoded single-customer contract: the artifact text must contain `intersolar` AND one of `alle aussteller`/`alle unternehmen`/`vollstaendig`, and the attached .xlsx must have `>=200` data rows AND a `PLZ` header. This is a business-semantic decision ('is THIS varying input the special complete-list case, and is the deliverable production-ready?') resolved deterministically by fuzzy keyword scan in the serial router — exactly what the determinism-split forbids (deterministic only for hard facts; never for 'is a varying input a special case' or 'fuzzy work production-ready'). `required_deliverables` exists today only as free text for the reviewer prompt, so the fix needs real structured Skill-contract plumbing rather than a flip of an existing wire. The same anti-pattern recurs in inferred_skill_from_message_content/looks_like_web_extraction_task, which keyword-assign a skill in-router.
- **Fix:** Add structured Skill deliverable-contract fields (e.g. min_rows, required_columns) and propagate them into the review request / guard thresholds. The deterministic guard should check only Skill-declared, explicit required_evidence rather than a literal company name. If a Skill declares a spreadsheet deliverable but omits the required contract, fail closed.
- **Change sketch:** 1) Extend Skill metadata/frontmatter parsing with explicit required-evidence fields (e.g. required_columns, min_data_rows). 2) Propagate the bound Skill's contract into review::CompletionReviewRequest / guard input. 3) Replace the `intersolar`/`alle aussteller` trigger in spreadsheet_attachment_guard_outcome with 'guard fires when the bound skill declares a spreadsheet deliverable contract', and replace `<200`/`PLZ` literals with the skill-declared thresholds. 4) Keep spreadsheet_guard_failure_outcome and inspect_xlsx_attachment as-is. 5) Keep verdict semantics identical so existing review wiring is untouched.
- **Prüfsatz:** Hardens spreadsheet_attachment_guard_outcome and review::CompletionReviewRequest.required_deliverables. route_external_messages stays the dispatch hot path (unchanged). Work still flows through Queue/Ticket/Internal Work (only the guard's trigger source changes). All status changes still flow through the state machine (guard still emits a ReviewOutcome consumed by the existing path). No new spawns. Review-rework stays on the same work item. Semantic equality is NOT assumed — the guard moves from a fuzzy keyword match to explicit Skill-declared hard keys (required_columns/min_rows). Skills become the source of the repeatable deliverable contract. Evidence: the guard still writes a Fail ReviewOutcome + slice assurance. Test: a Skill declaring min_rows/required_columns must FAIL a short/missing-column workbook and PASS a complete one, with NO 'intersolar' literal in the assertion.
- **Risk:** Skill-contract plumbing must reach review::CompletionReviewRequest before the guard runs; if a skill omits the contract the guard must fail-closed for declared spreadsheet deliverables, not fail-open. Behavior for the current single customer must be preserved by a fixture skill during migration.
- **Verifier guidance:** Keep. The finding is grounded and the strongest constraint backing it — the determinism split — is unambiguously violated today: a per-input "is this the special complete-list case / is it production-ready" judgement is resolved by a deterministic fuzzy keyword scan over a hardcoded customer name, wired as a hard ReviewVerdict::Fail at the review hot path (service.rs:5125 -> 6588-6620). The proposed fix is constraint-compliant and behavior-preserving. Two corrections to fold into the writeup so it isn't over-claimed: (1) changeSketch step 4 is wrong — channels.rs:9823 is a test fixture, not a production seed; drop that step, the only production literal to relocate is inside spreadsheet_attachment_guard_outcome itself. (2) required_deliverables is currently free-text-into-LLM-prompt only and is sourced from founder commitments, and no skill frontmatter contract field exists (skill_store.rs), so the effort is genuinely M-and-real new plumbing: add structured frontmatter contract fields (required_columns/min_data_rows) + parser in skill_store.rs, propagate suggested_skill's contract into CompletionReviewRequest, and have the guard read skill-declared thresholds with a fail-CLOSED default for any skill that declares a spreadsheet deliverable but omits the contract. Keep the determinism-split as the primary justification rather than the weaker "feature-placement says contracts belong in Skills" argument — architecture.md:157-168 actually places verification/communication in CTOX core, so that line of reasoning is softer; the determinism split is the decisive one.
- **Grounding caveat:** Verified in-tree. spreadsheet_attachment_guard_outcome (service.rs:6576-6637) hardcodes the single-customer trigger `haystack.contains("intersolar") && (alle aussteller|alle unternehmen|vollstaendig|...)` (6588-6593) and the literal pass/fail rule `row_count-1 < 200 || !has_plz` (6616), emitting a hard ReviewVerdict::Fail (spreadsheet_guard_failure_outcome 6639-6677). It is wired at the review hot path (service.rs:5125, inside review_completion_for_job) and overrides the model review outcome. This is a per-input business-semantic decision ("is THIS varying input the special complete-list case, and is the deliverable production-ready?") resolved by deterministic fuzzy keyword scan — exactly what the determinism split forbids ("never deterministic for: special-case input? / fuzzy work production-ready?"). inferred_skill_from_message_content (10099) + looks_like_web_extraction_task (10123) confirm the same in-router keyword-classification anti-pattern. TWO anchor caveats: (a) channels.rs:9823 is NOT a production seed — it is a test fixture string inside `#[test] teams_work_ack_requires_review_even_with_queue_backing` (channels.rs:9810); grep confirms every non-test `intersolar` occurrence lives only inside spreadsheet_attachment_guard_outcome itself, so changeSketch step 4 is misdescribed. (b) The claim "review.rs already has a required_deliverables channel for exactly this" overstates readiness: required_deliverables (review.rs:139) is today consumed ONLY as free text into the LLM reviewer prompt (review.rs:910-913,1029) and is populated from founder_required_deliverables (service.rs:5004-5023) — there is no structured min_rows/required_columns deterministic path, and no skill frontmatter contract field exists (skill_store.rs parse_skill_catalog_metadata only knows class/state/cluster/description). So the fix needs net-new plumbing (skill frontmatter schema -> propagate suggested_skill contract -> CompletionReviewRequest -> guard), not a flip of an existing wire. Core weakness is nonetheless real and live.


### `compaction-internals` · `lcm-x1` — Non-atomic message persist orphans the row; persist-retry duplicates it

🏷 Pass 2 · impact **high** · effort **S** · kind **bug** · verifier **keep**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** ✅ **DO — real stability win** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **clear** — Every anchor resolves to live code (drifted line numbers only): add_message_with_outcome (1087-1144), persist_lcm_message_with_retry (752-779), insert_summary SAVEPOINT (2889/2915). The atomicity hole is real and demonstrable: three sepa...

- [x] **shipped**
- **Anchors:** `lcm.rs::add_message_with_outcome (1087-1144)`, `turn_loop.rs::persist_lcm_message_with_retry (752-779)`, `lcm.rs::insert_summary SAVEPOINT (2940-2995)`
- **Problem:** Three autocommit INSERTs (messages, fts, context_items) with no transaction; if context_items fails the committed messages row is invisible to compaction (context_entries joins context_items 3018) and render, and the 4x persist-retry inserts a duplicate while the first is orphaned; insert_summary already uses a SAVEPOINT.
- **Fix:** Wrap the body in unchecked_transaction() and commit, like continuity_apply_diff (1497-1504).
- **Change sketch:** let tx=unchecked_transaction()?; inserts on tx; commit; keep continuity_init outside.
- **Prüfsatz:** Hardens add_message_with_outcome and the persist hot path; route_external_messages untouched; no new spawn/status; no semantic equality; test asserts one message+context_items row after injected failure; LCM SQLite only.
- **Verifier guidance:** Real, grounded, constraint-clean, behavior-preserving. One refinement to the proposed test: assert after an injected context_items failure that there is (a) NO orphan messages row AND (b) NO orphan messages_fts row — the FTS insert at lcm.rs:1124 also commits before context_items and is part of the same atomicity hole, so a tx that only covers messages+context_items but not fts would still leak FTS rows; the fix must wrap all three inserts (messages, messages_fts, context_items) in the single tx and the test should cover the FTS row too. Also assert that the 4x retry produces exactly one final message row (no duplicate) after the first attempt's transient failure rolls back cleanly.
- **Grounding caveat:** All three anchors resolve exactly. add_message_with_outcome (lcm.rs:1110/1124/1129) runs three autocommit inserts (messages, messages_fts, context_items) with no transaction. context_entries (lcm.rs:3029) and context_token_count (3059) both drive FROM context_items LEFT JOIN messages, so a messages row with no context_items row is invisible to render/compaction AND uncounted in tokens, while still polluting messages_fts (1124) and bumping seq (1099). persist_lcm_message_with_retry (turn_loop.rs:760-773) retries 4x via run_add_message (lcm.rs:3859, fresh Connection in autocommit), so a context_items failure on attempt 1 orphans the message and attempt 2 inserts a duplicate message+context_items. insert_summary already wraps its multi-insert body in SAVEPOINT (lcm.rs:2889/2915), confirming the cited asymmetry. The connection uses WAL+busy_timeout (lcm.rs:731) and multiple openers exist (run_add_message harness, run_add_assistant_turn service.rs:3431, channels.rs:10887), so a SQLITE_BUSY mid-sequence is a realistic partial-failure window — the very existence of the retry helper proves transient failure is expected, which the non-atomic body converts into permanent orphan+duplicate.


### `concurrency-isolation` · `X2-1` — Message/queue lease UPDATE is unconditional last-writer-wins, not check-and-set: concurrent owners silently steal each other's lease

🏷 Pass 2 · impact **high** · effort **M** · kind **concurrency** · verifier **revise**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** ✅ **DO — real stability win** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **clear** — Not a hallucination — this is the rare well-researched entry. Every anchor, symbol, and behavioral claim resolves to live code (only line numbers drifted, which is permitted). The check-then-act lease window is real: SELECT eligibility r...

> ⚠️ **Canonical issue:** implement the **Canonical scope** + **Verifier guidance** below. (The stale original Fix/Change-sketch fields were removed in the live re-audit cleanup.)

- [x] **shipped**
- **Canonical scope:** Implement the corrected scope in **Verifier guidance**. Treat the superseded original fix/sketch/test mapping as historical context, not instructions.
- **Canonical verification:** Use the Q10/test instructions in **Verifier guidance**; if they conflict with any superseded original field, Verifier guidance wins.
- **Anchors:** `src/core/mission/channels.rs::take_messages (lines 6754-6798, SELECT outside txn then unconditional ON CONFLICT DO UPDATE SET lease_owner=excluded.lease_owner)`, `src/core/mission/channels.rs::lease_queue_task (lines 2650-2678, no transaction at all, unconditional lease UPDATE)`, `src/core/service/core_transition_guard.rs::evaluate_core_transition (line 163 validates only request.from_state, never reads persisted current state)`, `src/core/mission/channels.rs::update_pending_send_to_accepted (line 5509, the correct CAS precedent already in this file)`
- **Problem:** take_messages SELECTs eligible (pending/leased-by-me) rows OUTSIDE any transaction (line 6754), drops the statement, then opens a separate unchecked_transaction and applies an unconditional INSERT...ON CONFLICT(message_key) DO UPDATE SET route_status='leased', lease_owner=excluded.lease_owner (line 6783). lease_queue_task is worse: no transaction at all. Each lease caller opens its own connection via open_channel_db. Between one caller's SELECT and its UPDATE, a second caller (parallel agent / service loop) on a different connection can lease the same message_key; both UPDATEs succeed and the second overwrites the first's lease_owner. The core transition guard does NOT prevent this — evaluate_core_transition validates the caller-claimed request.from_state ('pending'/'leased') against the catalog, it never reads the row's actual persisted lease_owner/route_status, so a stale 'pending'->'leased' edge from each racer is accepted. Result: two workers believe they exclusively own the same inbound message or queue task. This is the lease check-then-act window the concern names; Pass-1 only flagged it as an untested mapping, not as a missing CAS guard.
- **Risk:** Low–medium: BEGIN IMMEDIATE raises busy_timeout contention slightly; the rows-affected==0 branch must be threaded through the returned Vec so a losing caller does not return a message it failed to lease. No schema or persistence change — same table, same columns.
- **Verifier guidance:** Keep the finding — it is real, precisely grounded, and constraint-compliant. One refinement to the changeSketch is required for audit correctness: in take_messages the enforce_queue_route_status_transition call currently runs at line 6769 BEFORE the lease UPDATE (6777). If you only add a CAS WHERE clause to the UPDATE but leave enforce running unconditionally first, a LOSING racer will write a core-transition proof for a lease that then fails the CAS (rows-affected==0) and never actually flipped — a phantom audit proof. So the order must be: (1) open the write txn with TransactionBehavior::Immediate BEFORE the eligibility SELECT; (2) run the guarded CAS UPDATE; (3) only if rows-affected==1, call enforce_queue_route_status_transition and push to `taken`; (4) on rows-affected==0, skip both the proof and the push. The finding's prose 'it still records the proof for the rows that actually flipped' is the right intent but the sketch leaves the pre-UPDATE enforce call in place, which contradicts it — gate the enforce/proof on CAS success. Same ordering fix applies to lease_queue_task (move enforce after the guarded UPDATE; if rows-affected==0, return a 'lease lost / already owned' error rather than loading a task it doesn't own, since that fn returns a single QueueTaskView not a Vec). The proposed CAS predicate `(lease_owner IS NULL OR lease_owner='' OR lease_owner=? OR route_status='pending')` correctly mirrors the eligibility predicate at lines 6707-6712, so it is consistent. Everything else (BEGIN IMMEDIATE, rows-affected check, concurrent-lease test asserting the second caller gets rows-affected==0, no schema change) is sound and should be kept.
- **Grounding caveat:** All four anchors verified at the exact cited lines. take_messages: SELECT runs outside any txn (channels.rs:6754-6763), statement dropped (6764), then a DEFERRED unchecked_transaction (6765), then an unconditional INSERT...ON CONFLICT(message_key) DO UPDATE SET lease_owner=excluded.lease_owner (6783-6788) with no WHERE guard on current owner. lease_queue_task (2639-2681) is worse: fresh open_channel_db connection (2650), reads previous_route_status outside any transaction (2655), then the same unconditional lease UPDATE (2664-2678) with NO transaction at all. evaluate_core_transition (core_transition_guard.rs:163) calls csm::validate_transition, which I confirmed (core_state_machine.rs:370-401) is a PURE function over the in-memory request — it never opens the conn to read persisted route_status/lease_owner, so two racers each claiming from_state='pending'->'leased' both pass the catalog check; the guard cannot serialize the lease. update_pending_send_to_accepted (5509-5527) is a genuine CAS precedent in the same file: UPDATE ... WHERE message_key=? AND status='draft_pending_send' plus `if updated==0 { bail }`. Callers open a fresh connection per invocation (1771, 2014, 2650), so the cross-connection multi-writer scenario is real (parallel agent / service loop). open_channel_db sets journal_mode=WAL + 30s busy_timeout (persistence.rs:34): WAL serializes the physical writes but the unconditional UPDATE means the second writer simply BLOCKS on busy_timeout then SILENTLY overwrites the first's lease_owner — a classic lost update. No BEGIN IMMEDIATE exists anywhere in channels.rs (all txns are unchecked_transaction/DEFERRED). The weakness is real right now.


### `concurrency-isolation` · `X2-3` — Spawn-budget gate has a TOCTOU: count-then-insert across two connections lets concurrent spawners exceed the finite budget

🏷 Pass 2 · impact **high** · effort **M** · kind **concurrency** · verifier **keep**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** ✅ **DO — real stability win** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **clear** — Every anchor and behavioral claim verified against live code. The count-then-insert is genuinely non-atomic: validate_core_spawn does a COUNT(*) read (699) that excludes the current edge_id (edge_id <> ?2, 862), and the INSERT is a separ...

- [x] **shipped**
- **Anchors:** `src/core/service/core_transition_guard.rs::validate_core_spawn (lines 695-704, reads accepted_spawn_budget_count then returns)`, `src/core/service/core_transition_guard.rs::evaluate_core_spawn (lines 438-478, INSERTs the edge AFTER validation, no enclosing transaction)`, `src/core/service/core_transition_guard.rs::accepted_spawn_budget_count (referenced at line 699; COUNT(*) over accepted edges by budget_key)`, `docs/harness-operating-model.md (Finite Budget liveness argument, budget<=64 contracts)`
- **Problem:** evaluate_core_spawn validates the spawn by calling validate_core_spawn, which checks `accepted_spawn_budget_count(conn, budget_key, edge_id) >= max_attempts` (line 699-700) to enforce the finite budget that the operating model relies on for liveness. It then INSERTs the new edge into ctox_core_spawn_edges (line 446) — but the count and the insert are NOT wrapped in a single write transaction, and callers pass their own per-call connection. Two concurrent spawners sharing a budget_key both read existing=max-1 (both under the cap), both pass validation, and both insert distinct edge_ids (edge_id is deterministic over request_json, so different children do NOT collide on the ON CONFLICT). The accepted-edge count now exceeds max_attempts. This violates the 'every accepted spawn path has a finite budget' invariant that harness-operating-model.md treats as a release-blocking contract. Distinct from Pass-1's 'spawn-budget values untested' (a value-correctness gap): this is the budget enforcement itself racing.
- **Fix:** The fix is to make the budget read and the edge insert atomic so the second racer observes the first's committed edge. SQLite gives this for free with a BEGIN IMMEDIATE write transaction around validate+insert on a single connection; busy_timeout then serializes the two spawners and the loser correctly sees existing==max and is rejected with spawn_budget_exhausted.
- **Change sketch:** In evaluate_core_spawn, open `conn.transaction_with_behavior(TransactionBehavior::Immediate)` (or unchecked_transaction with an explicit BEGIN IMMEDIATE) BEFORE calling validate_core_spawn, perform the accepted_spawn_budget_count read and the INSERT inside it, and commit. No change to validate_core_spawn's logic. enforce_core_spawn/check_core_spawn semantics unchanged. Add an index-friendly re-count is unnecessary; the IMMEDIATE lock is sufficient because both racers contend on the same DB write lock.
- **Prüfsatz:** Hardens existing fn evaluate_core_spawn and table ctox_core_spawn_edges (the Core Spawn Guard itself); no second scheduler; route_external_messages untouched; spawns still flow exclusively through this guard (that is the point — it is made race-safe); status SM untouched; review-rework untouched; semantic equality is on the hard deterministic edge_id/budget_key, never fuzzy; Skills untouched; ctox_core_spawn_edges remains the process-mining audit evidence; deterministic invariant (spawn budget) gets a new test: N concurrent enforce_core_spawn calls with the same budget_key and max_attempts=K accept at most K.
- **Risk:** Medium: must confirm all callers pass a writable (not read-only) connection into evaluate_core_spawn; check_core_spawn (read-only preview) must stay outside the IMMEDIATE txn. Slight increase in writer contention under spawn bursts, bounded by busy_timeout. No schema or persistence change.
- **Verifier guidance:** Keep as-is. The fix sketch is correct and the finding already names the right guards in its risk section: open conn.transaction_with_behavior(TransactionBehavior::Immediate) on the SAME passed-in connection, do the accepted_spawn_budget_count read and the INSERT inside it, commit; leave check_core_spawn (read-only preview) outside any IMMEDIATE txn. One caller-side check to add to the test/PR: confirm every evaluate_core_spawn/enforce_core_spawn caller passes a writable connection (all observed callers use open_channel_db, which is writable — the read-only path is open_channel_db_read_only and is not used for spawns). New invariant test: N threads call enforce_core_spawn with identical budget_key and distinct child_entity_ids at max_attempts=K; assert at most K accepted edges land. Severity is real but partly workload-gated (needs concurrent same-budget_key contention), so 'high' impact is defensible given it is a release-blocking liveness contract per harness-operating-model.md.
- **Grounding caveat:** Verified in src/core/service/core_transition_guard.rs: evaluate_core_spawn (432-486) calls validate_core_spawn -> accepted_spawn_budget_count COUNT(*) read (699, 855-868) then a SEPARATE INSERT (446-478) with NO enclosing transaction. accepted_spawn_budget_count excludes the current edge_id (edge_id <> ?2), and edge_id is deterministic over request_json, so two distinct concurrent children with the same budget_key do NOT collide on ON CONFLICT(edge_id) and both can insert -> count exceeds max_attempts. Multi-writer is real: each caller opens its own Connection via channels.rs::open_channel_db (6059-6070); DB is WAL + busy_timeout (6066, 6117-6118); SharedState mutex is NOT held across route_external_messages (service.rs 9044+ locks per push_event only), so it does not serialize spawn-guard writes; callers run on independent background threads (channel router, mission maintenance, IoT conditions.rs:1074, tickets.rs:2907). Existing budget test core_spawn_allows_only_finite_budgeted_cycles (1409-1428) is strictly sequential on one in-memory conn, so the concurrent over-budget race is untested. Minor: worst case needs two distinct child_ids sharing one budget_key racing simultaneously (workload-dependent), but the enforcement primitive is genuinely non-atomic.


### `egress-idempotency` · `EGRESS-1` — Successful founder send never emits Sending->Sent; entity stranded in non-terminal Sending, success never witnessed by the kernel

🏷 Pass 2 · impact **high** · effort **S** · kind **bug** · verifier **keep**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** ✅ **DO — real stability win** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **clear** — Conclusively grounded. The entity-lifecycle asymmetry is real: every reviewed founder send is driven Approved->Sending before the provider call, the failure outcome emits Sending->SendFailed through the kernel, but the success outcome em...

- [x] **shipped**
- **Anchors:** `src/core/mission/channels.rs::send_email_message (4117-4213)`, `src/core/mission/channels.rs::enforce_reviewed_founder_send_core_transition (5425)`, `src/core/mission/channels.rs::emit_reviewed_founder_send_failed_transition (5613-5659)`, `src/core/mission/channels.rs::mark_founder_reply_review_sent (5083)`, `src/core/service/core_state_machine.rs::allowed_transition_catalog (1160 (Sending,Sent))`, `src/core/service/core_state_machine.rs::is_outcome_terminal_transition (526-531)`
- **Problem:** The egress path drives the FounderCommunication entity Approved->Sending before the provider call and Sending->SendFailed on failure, but on SUCCESS no code emits the catalog-legal (Sending,Sent) transition. grep over all of src/core finds exactly one from_state:CoreState::Sending emitter and it is the failure path (channels.rs:5643); the only other CoreState::Sent reference is a reverse-mapping table in process_mining.rs:4815, not an emitter. Consequence: every successfully sent founder/owner mail leaves its entity permanently in the non-terminal Sending state. Failure is witnessed by the kernel; success is not. Because the outcome-witness terminal gate (is_outcome_terminal_transition) only fires for Completed/Closed/Sent/Done, the strongest validation never runs for the highest-blast-radius case, and process-mining/liveness see successful sends as perpetually in-flight. mark_founder_reply_review_sent only updates the review table, bypassing the Core State Machine for the success outcome.
- **Fix:** Make the success outcome flow through the same kernel the failure outcome already does: after mark_outbound_send_accepted succeeds, emit the Sending->Sent core transition with the same CoreEvidenceRefs (review_audit_key + body/recipient hashes) already assembled for the Approved->Sending edge, symmetric to enforce_reviewed_founder_send_failed_core_transition. This hardens an existing function on the existing serial path; no new runner.
- **Change sketch:** Add emit_reviewed_founder_send_succeeded_transition(conn, entity_id, approval_key, request, pending_message_key) mirroring emit_reviewed_founder_send_failed_transition but from_state=Sending, to_state=Sent, event=CoreEvent::Send/Confirm. Call it in send_email_message immediately after mark_outbound_send_accepted (line 4199) when reviewed_context.is_some(), threading entity_id like the failure branch already does at 4182-4191. Carry the same approved/outgoing hash refs so require_reviewed_outbound still passes.
- **Prüfsatz:** (1) hardens send_email_message + the FounderCommunication entity lifecycle; (2) route_external_messages stays the dispatch hot path - this is downstream of it; (3) no new work item, reuses the existing entity; (4) YES - this is the missing success status change that must flow through the Core State Machine, fixing the bypass; (5) no new spawn; (6) rework stays bound to the same FounderCommunication entity_id; (7) hard keys only (sha256 hashes, approval_key); (8) skills unaffected; (9) ADDS the missing kernel witness/audit row for send success; (10) test: assert a successful reviewed founder send produces a Sending->Sent core_transition row for the same entity_id (no such test exists today).
- **Risk:** Low; behavior-preserving for delivery (mail already sent), additive kernel witness on a path that already emits the failure twin. Must reuse identical evidence refs so the founder_send_body_hash_mismatch gate does not reject the new edge.
- **Verifier guidance:** Solid, grounded, constraint-compliant bug. One wording nuance worth flagging (not a revision-blocker): the 'strongest validation never runs' impact via validate_outcome_witness (core_state_machine.rs:489-516) is conditional - that gate early-returns unless evidence.expected_artifact_refs is non-empty (493-494). So emitting Sending->Sent only triggers the outcome-witness gate if artifact refs are actually supplied on the new edge. The load-bearing defect (non-terminal stranding in Sending + success unwitnessed by the kernel + process-mining/liveness seeing perpetual in-flight) is real and independent of that gate. Recommend the implementer either populate expected/delivered_artifact_refs on the new Sent edge so the witness gate engages, or scope the claim to 'no terminal witness at all' rather than 'strongest validation skipped'.
- **Grounding caveat:** Verified at channels.rs:4117-4213 (send_email_message: failure branch emits Sending->SendFailed at 4183; success branch at 4199 calls only mark_outbound_send_accepted, a bare communication_messages UPDATE at 4367-4394 with NO enforce_core_transition). grep over src/core confirms exactly ONE from_state:CoreState::Sending emitter and it is the failure path (channels.rs:5643); zero to_state:CoreState::Sent emitters exist (all CoreState::Sent hits are process_mining reverse-map/normalizers or gate predicates at core_state_machine.rs:529/553). mark_founder_reply_review_sent (5083) updates only communication_founder_reply_reviews, bypassing the SM. Catalog has (Sending,Sent) legal at core_state_machine.rs:1160. Test phase1_emit_send_failed_transition_records_kernel_proof (11527) asserts the SendFailed proof; no symmetric Sent test exists. Entity is genuinely stranded in non-terminal Sending on success and the kernel never witnesses success.


### `egress-idempotency` · `EGRESS-2` — Crash between provider-accept and accepted-mark re-sends founder mail: no provider idempotency key, draft_pending_send not treated as durable

🏷 Pass 2 · impact **high** · effort **M** · kind **bug** · verifier **keep**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** ✅ **DO — real stability win** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **clear** — Independently verified every load-bearing claim against current code; the ticket's grounding caveat matched live source in all eight checks. The double-send crash window is real and present on a P0 founder-egress path: record_outbound_pe...

- [x] **shipped**
- **Anchors:** `src/core/mission/channels.rs::send_email_message (4161-4199)`, `src/core/mission/channels.rs::record_outbound_pending_send (4221-4301)`, `src/core/mission/channels.rs::existing_durable_outbound_send_result (4309-4348)`, `src/core/mission/channels.rs::is_durable_outbound_send_state (4350-4365)`, `src/core/communication/adapters.rs::EmailAdapter::send_cli (225-232)`
- **Problem:** Re-send idempotency depends solely on the durable communication_messages row. The pending row is written as (status=draft_pending_send, folder_hint=outbox); adapter.send_cli physically sends; then mark_outbound_send_accepted flips folder_hint to sent. is_durable_outbound_send_state requires folder_hint=='sent' AND status not in the failed set, so a draft_pending_send row is explicitly NOT durable (channels.rs:4356). If the process dies (or the conn errors) after send_cli returns Ok but before mark_outbound_send_accepted commits, the row stays (draft_pending_send, outbox). On the next attempt record_outbound_pending_send re-finds the same deterministic key, existing_durable_outbound_send_result returns None, and send_cli is called a SECOND time. EmailSendCommandRequest carries no idempotency key / deterministic Message-ID derived from message_key (adapters.rs:71, send_cli at 225 just forwards), so the provider cannot dedupe either. The in-process acquire_reviewed_founder_send_lock does not survive a crash and is not even held on the send_reviewed_email_communication_request branch (channels.rs:3322).
- **Fix:** Tighten the existing durability check + provider request rather than add a runner. Pass a deterministic idempotency token (the existing pending_send_message_key/body_sha256) into EmailSendCommandRequest so a re-attempt is suppressed provider-side, and/or treat a draft_pending_send row whose provider call was already initiated as a hold-then-verify rather than a blind re-send. Both harden existing functions on the existing serial path.
- **Change sketch:** Add idempotency_key: &str to EmailSendCommandRequest set to pending_send_message_key; native send maps it to a stable Message-ID / provider dedup header. In send_email_message, before re-calling send_cli on an existing draft_pending_send row, record an attempt marker (e.g. metadata send_attempt_started_at) so a recovered process can distinguish 'never sent' from 'maybe sent' and require a delivery re-check instead of an unconditional resend.
- **Prüfsatz:** (1) hardens record_outbound_pending_send/is_durable_outbound_send_state/EmailSendCommandRequest; (2) hot path unchanged - downstream of route_external_messages; (3) reuses the existing communication_messages durable row, no new work item; (4) pairs with EGRESS-1 so the status change is kernel-witnessed; (5) no new spawn; (6) same entity; (7) idempotency keyed only on hard keys (account|thread|recipient_set_sha256|body_sha256), no semantic similarity; (8) skills unaffected; (9) the attempt marker is the audit evidence of the crash window; (10) test: simulate send_cli Ok then crash-before-accepted; assert a second send_email_message does NOT re-invoke the provider (currently it does).
- **Risk:** Medium; the duplicate-suppression must not swallow a genuine retry of a never-sent message. The attempt marker plus a delivery re-check (not blind suppression) is the safe shape; provider Message-ID support varies by backend so the key must degrade gracefully.
- **Verifier guidance:** Keep. Refinement for the fix author: the load-bearing half is the LOCAL attempt-marker (e.g. metadata send_attempt_started_at written before send_cli) plus a delivery re-check on recovery so a recovered process distinguishes 'never sent' from 'maybe sent' and does NOT blind-resend a draft_pending_send row whose provider call was already initiated. The provider-side-dedup half (stable deterministic Message-ID into EmailSendCommandRequest) is best-effort only: most SMTP servers do not dedupe on Message-ID, and today generated_message_id at email_native.rs:1529 is timestamp-salted so even an unchanged re-send currently gets a fresh ID. So the idempotency-token change is worth doing (make the Message-ID deterministic = derive from pending_send_message_key/body_sha256, degrade gracefully per backend) but must not be relied on as the suppression mechanism. The test in item (10) is the correct invariant proof: simulate send_cli Ok then crash-before-accepted, assert the second send_email_message does NOT re-invoke the provider (it does today). Also: the same crash window exists on the non-reviewed branch (channels.rs:3333) which never holds the lock either, so the durability fix must live in send_email_message/record_outbound_pending_send (shared path), not in the lock.
- **Grounding caveat:** All anchors verified. send_email_message ordering confirmed: record_outbound_pending_send (writes status=draft_pending_send, folder_hint=outbox; channels.rs:4262) -> adapter.send_cli physically sends (4161-4178) -> mark_outbound_send_accepted flips folder_hint='sent' (4199, 4377). is_durable_outbound_send_state requires folder_hint=='sent' AND status not in {draft_pending_send,send_failed,failed,cancelled} (channels.rs:4351-4357), so a stranded (draft_pending_send, outbox) row is explicitly NOT durable; existing_durable_outbound_send_result returns None for it (4336-4337). EmailSendCommandRequest (adapters.rs:71-83) carries NO idempotency key/Message-ID; send_cli just forwards (adapters.rs:225-232). Crucially, the generated Message-ID is non-deterministic: email_native.rs:1529 salts the digest with now_iso_string(), so a re-send produces a NEW Message-ID and the provider cannot dedupe. I also checked the key counter-argument: the core SM does NOT act as a crash-survival idempotency gate. enforce_reviewed_founder_send_core_transition hardcodes from_state=Approved->to_state=Sending (channels.rs:5445-5446); evaluate_core_transition (core_transition_guard.rs:137) and validate_transition (core_state_machine.rs:370-401) never load the entity's persisted state - they validate only the caller-supplied from/to against the allowed-transition catalog - so a recovery re-attempt is re-accepted. Confirmed no separate reconciliation sweep flips a stranded draft_pending_send row based on provider state. Lock claims verified: send_reviewed_email_communication_request (5380) does NOT acquire_reviewed_founder_send_lock before send_email_message (5394), and the lock (5463) is an in-process Mutex that does not survive a crash. pending_send_message_key is deterministic on hard keys account|thread|recipient_set_sha256|body_sha256 (channels.rs:5474-5485). Real weakness, present right now.


### `failmode-patterns` · `x2-1` — Success-path lease acks are fully silent `let _ =`, asymmetric with the recording failure branch — a failed `handled` ack re-leases work invisibly

🏷 Pass 2 · impact **high** · effort **S** · kind **bug** · verifier **keep**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** ✅ **DO — real stability win** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **clear** — Every anchor and behavioral claim verifies against live code (line numbers drifted only ~1-6 lines). The four success/terminal acks at service.rs:4081/4095/4170/4189 are bare `let _ =`, while the immediately adjacent message-retry else-b...

- [x] **shipped** — the four worker-completion success acks (handled/cancelled queue, handled/retry ticket-event) now route through `record_ack_failure_locked(&mut shared, <ack>, "<what>")` instead of bare `let _ =`, so a swallowed success ack surfaces a distinct feed event (e.g. "Failed to ack handled queue lease(s): …") and a stuck `leased` row is diagnosable instead of silently re-leased. Behavior-preserving (the ack still runs; never aborts the worker). Test `swallowed_success_ack_failure_is_recorded` pins Err→one event / Ok→none. (Landed on main inside the parallel agent's whole-file `service.rs` commit `426cb45f` due to shared-checkout co-editing; post-hoc adversarial review = 2 SHIP. Defer-side defer-key collision spun off separately.)
- **Anchors:** `src/core/service/service.rs:4081 (ack_leased_messages "handled")`, `src/core/service/service.rs:4094 (ack "cancelled")`, `src/core/service/service.rs:4170 (ack_leased_ticket_events "handled")`, `src/core/service/service.rs:4189 (ticket retry ack)`, `src/core/service/service.rs:4159 (the adjacent else-branch that DOES record ack failure)`, `src/core/mission/channels.rs:2185 (ack_leased_messages: opens DB, runs guard_founder_handled_ack + ack_messages, all fallible)`
- **Problem:** The worker-completion block records ack failures only in its pending/failed else-branch (service.rs:4159 pushes an event on Err). The success transitions — `handled` for queue messages (4081) and ticket events (4170), and `cancelled`/retry (4094, 4189) — use bare `let _ =`. `ack_leased_messages` runs `guard_founder_handled_ack` and a status transition through `ack_messages`; under DB lock contention or a guard rejection these return Err. When the success ack silently fails, the message keeps `route_status='leased'` with no event, no governance record, no failure_reason. The serial router's `active_agent_loop_in_progress` / queue-pressure logic then re-leases the same message on a later tick, causing duplicate processing of work that already completed (and, for founder/owner lanes, a duplicate outbound), or the stuck lease blocks the single CHANNEL_ROUTER_SERIAL_LEASE_LIMIT slot. The bug is invisible precisely because the success path is the one without recording.
- **Fix:** Make the success ack as auditable as the failure ack it sits next to. This hardens the EXISTING ack/lease-transition path (channels::ack_leased_messages / tickets::ack_leased_ticket_events) and keeps route_external_messages the hot path; no new mechanism.
- **Change sketch:** Replace the four `let _ = channels::ack_leased_messages(...)` / `tickets::ack_leased_ticket_events(...)` success calls with `if let Err(e) = ... { push_event_locked(&mut shared, format!("Failed to ack <handled|cancelled> lease(s) after completion: {}", clip_text(&e.to_string(),180))); }`, reusing the exact pattern already at 4159-4167. No control-flow change (still best-effort, never aborts the worker), just record the swallow so a regression surfaces in the feed/governance and the stuck lease is diagnosable.
- **Prüfsatz:** 1) hardens channels::ack_leased_messages + tickets::ack_leased_ticket_events callsites in the worker completion path. 2) route_external_messages stays the dispatch hot path (only adds an event on Err). 3) work still flows through Queue/Ticket — no new path. 4) status changes still flow through ack_messages → enforce_queue_route_status_transition. 5) no new spawn. 6) review-rework unchanged. 7) acks key on explicit message_key/ticket_event_key only. 8) skills untouched. 9) ADDS evidence where there is currently none. 10) test: lease a message, stub the ack DB to fail, assert an event/governance record is emitted and the lease is not silently dropped.
- **Risk:** Minimal — behavior-preserving; only adds an event on the error branch that is currently empty.
- **Verifier guidance:** Keep as-is. Real, grounded, well-scoped, constraint-compliant observability hardening. Optional tightening for the author: soften the 'duplicate outbound (founder/owner lanes)' phrasing — founder_reply_sent_after_review/guard_founder_handled_ack give partial downstream protection against a re-run actually re-sending to a founder; the unconditionally-true harms are (a) duplicate processing of non-founder lanes and (b) a silent stuck 'leased' row consuming the single CHANNEL_ROUTER_SERIAL_LEASE_LIMIT=1 slot with no event/governance/failure_reason. That nuance does not change the fix.
- **Grounding caveat:** Verified all anchors. service.rs:4081/4095/4170/4189 are bare `let _ =` success acks; the adjacent else-branch at 4159-4167 DOES record the error via push_event_locked — asymmetry is real. channels.rs:2185 ack_leased_messages is genuinely fallible: runs guard_founder_handled_ack (which anyhow::bail!s at 5219 for a protected founder inbound marked handled without a reviewed reply) and ack_messages (DB + status transition, fallible under lock contention). Re-lease harm is grounded: dispatch eligibility query (channels.rs:6701/6607) selects route_status IN ('pending','leased'); re-acquire filter (6707/6613) matches self-owner; lease owner is the FIXED constant CHANNEL_ROUTER_LEASE_OWNER="ctox-service" (service.rs:111). So a stuck 'leased' row is re-picked next tick → duplicate processing, and it occupies the single CHANNEL_ROUTER_SERIAL_LEASE_LIMIT=1 slot. route_status is the only 'handled' signal at dispatch, so a swallowed ack leaves zero idempotency record. Minor: for the founder lane specifically, founder_reply_sent_after_review/guard_founder_handled_ack give partial downstream protection against a literal duplicate outbound on re-run, so the strongest 'duplicate outbound' wording is slightly optimistic there; the non-founder duplicate-processing and the silent-stuck-lease-blocks-the-one-slot harms are fully intact.


### `failmode-patterns` · `x2-2` — Retry-loop kill-switch `defer_mission_for_reason` is swallowed while the governance event hardcodes success — a failed defer keeps the runaway loop running and the audit lies

🏷 Pass 2 · impact **high** · effort **S** · kind **bug** · verifier **keep**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** ✅ **DO — real stability win** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **clear** — Every anchor verified at or within a few lines of the cited locations, and the described behavior exists exactly as stated. The safety/kill-switch action (defer_mission_for_reason, which flips is_open=false to stop the runaway retry loop...

- [x] **shipped** — the threshold defer is no longer `let _ =`: `record_agent_failure_threshold_outcome` ties the governance audit to the real defer `Result`. On `Ok` it records the byte-identical success event ("deferred mission and stopped automatic retry loop"); on `Err` it pushes a feed event AND records an error event "defer_mission FAILED — automatic retry loop NOT stopped" with a distinct idempotence-key prefix and the `defer_error` in details, so a swallowed safety action (is_open stayed true) no longer ships as a false success. Test pins both branches, the detail fields, and that a same-`{conversation,count}` Ok-vs-Err pair yields two distinct rows. Deterministic threshold logic untouched.
- **Anchors:** `src/core/service/service.rs:3447 (let _ = engine.defer_mission_for_reason(...))`, `src/core/service/service.rs:3451 (record_event action_taken: "deferred mission and stopped automatic retry loop")`, `src/core/service/service.rs:3475 (the sibling Err arm of increment_mission_agent_failure_count that DOES push_event)`, `src/core/context/lcm.rs:1897 (defer_mission_for_reason: persist_mission_state, fallible, sets is_open=false)`
- **Problem:** When agent failures reach the threshold the harness defers the mission to stop the automatic retry loop (the actual safety action) and then records a governance event whose action_taken literally states "deferred mission and stopped automatic retry loop". The defer call is `let _ =` (3447): `defer_mission_for_reason` runs `persist_mission_state`, which is guarded and fallible (clobber guard + DB write). If it fails, `mission_status` is NOT set to deferred, `is_open` stays true, the retry loop is NOT broken, the agent keeps burning turns — and the governance row at 3451 unconditionally asserts the loop was stopped. The author clearly knows how to record here (the matching Err arm at 3475 for the count bump pushes an event), making the swallow on the more-critical action an oversight. This is the fail-open-on-safety-action variant of the swallow class: control action dropped, audit claims success regardless.
- **Fix:** Tie the governance record to the actual outcome of the defer and surface failure. Hardens the existing agent-failure-threshold control path and the governance audit truthfulness; no new scheduler/terminal path.
- **Change sketch:** `match engine.defer_mission_for_reason(conversation_id, "agent_failure_threshold") { Ok(_) => { record_event(... action "deferred mission and stopped automatic retry loop" ...) } Err(e) => { push_event(&state, format!("agent_failure_threshold reached but defer FAILED for {}: {}", conversation_id, e)); record_event(... severity "error", action "defer_mission FAILED — retry loop NOT stopped" ...) } }`. Keeps both branches durable; never panics; the audit now matches reality.
- **Prüfsatz:** 1) hardens engine.defer_mission_for_reason + governance::record_event truthfulness. 2) route_external_messages stays hot path. 3) no new work item. 4) mission status change still flows through persist_mission_state (the guarded path). 5) no new spawn. 6) review-rework unchanged. 7) no semantic equality. 8) skills untouched. 9) FIXES a false audit and adds a real failure event. 10) test: force persist_mission_state to fail, assert mission stays the loop-stopping intent is recorded as FAILED (not as success) and an error event is emitted.
- **Risk:** Low — the only behavioral change is recording the real outcome; the deterministic threshold logic is untouched.
- **Verifier guidance:** Real fail-open-on-safety-action + false-audit bug, fully grounded and constraint-compliant. Minor cosmetic flaw only: pruefsatz item 10 has a garbled sentence ("assert mission stays the loop-stopping intent is recorded as FAILED"), but the changeSketch is unambiguous and correct — match on the defer Result, record success on Ok, and on Err emit both a push_event and an error-severity governance event reflecting that the retry loop was NOT stopped. Keep as-is with that wording cleaned up. No behavioral overreach: the deterministic threshold logic is untouched.
- **Grounding caveat:** All anchors verified. service.rs:3447 `let _ = engine.defer_mission_for_reason(conversation_id, "agent_failure_threshold")` discards a fallible Result. service.rs:3451-3459 `record_event` unconditionally records action_taken "deferred mission and stopped automatic retry loop" regardless of defer outcome. service.rs:3475 sibling Err arm of increment_mission_agent_failure_count DOES push_event, proving the author knows the pattern. lcm.rs:1897-1909 defer_mission_for_reason returns Result, calls persist_mission_state(&record)? and sets mission_status="deferred"/is_open=false/allow_idle=true (the actual loop-stopping action). persist_mission_state_with (lcm.rs:4400+) does a fallible clobber-guard read (load_mission_state_with(...)?) AND a fallible conn.execute INSERT — so the Err is real at runtime, not theoretical. is_open gates mission continuation (service.rs:1019). Existing test (service.rs:24992-25001) covers ONLY the happy path (asserts !is_open/allow_idle after a successful defer); no test for the failure-path false audit, so the proposed test is a genuine new invariant.


### `governance-recovery` · `govrec-1` — Mission failure threshold and timeout retry flag read raw std::env::var instead of the runtime store

🏷 Pass 1 · impact **high** · effort **S** · verifier **revise**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** ✅ **DO — real stability win** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **clear** — Every anchor, symbol, constant, and line-number claim verifies against live code (only line numbers drifted ~88 lines, e.g. 8510→8598). The two governance knobs that gate mission defer/failure decisions and timeout auto-retry read std::e...

> ⚠️ **Canonical issue:** implement the **Canonical scope** + **Verifier guidance** below. (The stale original Fix/Change-sketch fields were removed in the live re-audit cleanup.)

- [x] **shipped**
- **Canonical scope:** Implement the corrected scope in **Verifier guidance**. Treat the superseded original fix/sketch/test mapping as historical context, not instructions.
- **Canonical verification:** Use the Q10/test instructions in **Verifier guidance**; if they conflict with any superseded original field, Verifier guidance wins.
- **Anchors:** `src/core/service/service.rs::mission_agent_failure_threshold`, `src/core/service/service.rs::timeout_auto_retry_enabled`, `src/core/execution/models/runtime_env.rs::env_or_config`, `src/core/execution/models/runtime_env.rs::config_flag`
- **Problem:** The two high-signal governance knobs — mission_agent_failure_threshold (service.rs:8510, CTOX_MISSION_AGENT_FAILURE_THRESHOLD) and timeout_auto_retry_enabled (service.rs:8520, CTOX_TIMEOUT_AUTO_RETRY) — read process env directly via std::env::var. CLAUDE.md hard rule forbids process-env toggles for runtime/governance behavior; everything must flow through runtime_env::env_or_config / config_flag. Review/rework thresholds have the same env-var smell but are tracked canonically in `review-outcome · review-2`.
- **Risk:** Low. Behavior identical when no override present; only the override source changes. Must keep the >0 and MAX_ clamps to preserve the safety ceiling.
- **Verifier guidance:** Real, grounded, compliant — keep the core change but tighten scope. The observable knobs here are mission_agent_failure_threshold (DEFAULT 2/MAX 6) and the boolean timeout flag. The review thresholds are deliberately handled in `review-outcome · review-2` so this ticket does not become a duplicate. Scope precisely: a 2-function signature change plus call-site/test thread-through; swap std::env::var → runtime_env::env_or_config(root,...) for the integer threshold and config_flag for the bool, preserving exact clamp/default behavior. Do NOT touch defer/failed/requeue transition logic.
- **Grounding caveat:** Re-opened all anchors. service.rs:8510 mission_agent_failure_threshold() reads std::env::var("CTOX_MISSION_AGENT_FAILURE_THRESHOLD") raw; 8520 timeout_auto_retry_enabled() reads CTOX_TIMEOUT_AUTO_RETRY raw. runtime_env::env_or_config(root,key) exists (runtime_env.rs:80) and config_flag (runtime_env.rs:149); both already used in this file (705, 730, 2783, 2785). ### `internal-work-workflow` · `workflow-1` — Predecessor satisfaction can be asserted via raw metadata write, bypassing the core state machine

🏷 Pass 1 · impact **high** · effort **M** · verifier **revise**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** ✅ **DO — real stability win** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **clear** — Every anchor and behavioral claim verified against live code (line numbers drifted only slightly: service.rs 9046->9134, test 12445/12417 exact). The integrity gap is real and exploitable: a single `ctox ticket workflow-apply-delta` call...

> ⚠️ **Canonical issue:** implement the **Canonical scope** + **Verifier guidance** below. (The stale original Fix/Change-sketch fields were removed in the live re-audit cleanup.)

- [ ] **open**
- **Canonical scope:** Implement the corrected scope in **Verifier guidance**. Treat the superseded original fix/sketch/test mapping as historical context, not instructions.
- **Canonical verification:** Use the Q10/test instructions in **Verifier guidance**; if they conflict with any superseded original field, Verifier guidance wins.
- **Anchors:** `src/core/mission/tickets.rs::workflow_step_satisfied`, `src/core/mission/tickets.rs::apply_ticket_workflow_delta`, `src/core/mission/tickets.rs::merge_ticket_self_work_metadata`, `src/core/mission/tickets.rs::enforce_ticket_self_work_state_transition`, `src/core/mission/tickets.rs:3555`
- **Problem:** `workflow_step_satisfied` (4019) treats a step as a satisfied predecessor when its `workflow_step_status` metadata is `verified|passed|satisfied|closed|done|completed`, EVEN IF the durable `state` never crossed a terminal core state. `apply_ticket_workflow_delta`'s `update_steps` path writes that status through `merge_ticket_self_work_metadata` (3968), a raw `UPDATE ... SET metadata_json` that never calls `enforce_ticket_self_work_state_transition`/`enforce_core_transition`. So a reducer turn can declare any predecessor `verified` with one CLI call, unblocking downstream materialization (service.rs:9046) without the core state machine, review, or terminal-success proof ever being consulted. The existing test (tickets.rs:12445) bakes this in as the happy path.
- **Risk:** Must keep the leaf/reducer flow working: any place that legitimately relies on metadata-only `workflow_step_status` to express in-progress states must still be allowed; only the satisfying values reroute. Migration: existing rows already gate on state too, so backcompat is preserved.
- **Verifier guidance:** Real, well-grounded, compliant — but the proposed change as written leaves a residual hole, so tighten it. `ticket_self_work_core_state` (tickets.rs:4382) maps "verified" -> CoreState::Verified, and `enforce_ticket_self_work_state_transition` (4292) only demands `work_item_has_terminal_success_proof` for CoreState::Closed, NOT for Verified. So merely rerouting a satisfying status through the guard would still let "verified" pass without terminal-success proof; it would only newly require a *legal* csm transition (csm::validate_transition, core_transition_guard.rs:163) from the current durable state — strictly stronger than today's any-state raw metadata write, but not a full close. Corrected, tighter version: (1) make `workflow_step_satisfied` (4019) derive the satisfied predicate from the durable `state` ONLY (drop the metadata-status branch at 4024-4026); (2) in `apply_ticket_workflow_delta`'s update loop (3549-3566), when the normalized `workflow_step_status` is a *satisfying* value, drive the durable `state` through `set_ticket_self_work_state_internal`/`transition_ticket_self_work_item` (which run `enforce_ticket_self_work_state_transition`), keeping non-satisfying values (e.g. in_progress) on the metadata path; and (3) ensure the satisfying gating state actually carries proof — i.e. gate predecessor-satisfaction on a state that requires terminal-success proof (treat the gating signal as Closed/verified-with-proof, not bare Verified), or extend the 4292 proof requirement to cover the Verified gating state so "satisfied for gating" == "closed/verified under the core state machine with a proof in ctox_core_transition_proofs." Add the negative test the finding describes (successor does NOT materialize when predecessor status is metadata-only without a guarded, proof-bearing transition) and update the existing happy-path test at 12417 to drive the predecessor through the guarded transition. Scope caveat to honor: leaf/reducer in-progress metadata expression must keep working; only the satisfying values reroute, and backcompat holds because existing rows already gate on `state` too.
- **Grounding caveat:** All five anchors exist and the weakness is real. tickets.rs:4019-4027 `workflow_step_satisfied` returns true when metadata `workflow_step_status` is in {verified|passed|satisfied|closed|done|completed} regardless of durable `state`. tickets.rs:3549-3566 in `apply_ticket_workflow_delta` writes that status via `merge_ticket_self_work_metadata` (3566). tickets.rs:3968-4009 `merge_ticket_self_work_metadata` is a raw `UPDATE ... SET metadata_json` (3986) that records only a `self_work_metadata_updated` audit and never calls `enforce_ticket_self_work_state_transition`/`enforce_core_transition`. The materialization gate `workflow_step_ready_internal` (3936-3957) gates a successor on `workflow_step_satisfied(predecessor)` at 3944/3953, and this is reached in live dispatch at service.rs:9046 via `materialize_ready_workflow_steps`, with the agent-facing CLI entry `ctox ticket workflow-apply-delta` at tickets.rs:1173-1187. The guarded path is asymmetric: `set_ticket_self_work_state_internal` (4416) -> `enforce_ticket_self_work_state_transition` (4281) -> `enforce_core_transition`, which for Closed requires `work_item_has_terminal_success_proof` (4292). The test at 12417/12445 bakes the metadata-only `verified` -> successor-materializes flow as the happy path. So one CLI call can declare a predecessor satisfied and unblock downstream materialization without any core transition or proof.

- [ ] **open**
- **Anchors:** `src/core/mission/tickets.rs::apply_ticket_workflow_delta`, `src/core/mission/tickets.rs:3557`, `src/core/mission/tickets.rs::WorkflowDeltaUpdateStep`, `src/core/mission/tickets.rs:3486`

A delta can set `workflow_step_status:"verified"` with `evidence: null` and the step satisfies predecessors. The step's `workflow_exit_gate` (written at 3486, rendered into the prompt at service.rs:12549) is never compared to anything at flip time. Determinism-split fit: requiring that evidence be PRESENT for a satisfying flip is a hard harness fact; judging whether the evidence is good stays model/review work.
- **Fix:** Make the deterministic apply-path refuse a satisfying status flip that carries no `workflow_step_evidence`, tightening the existing delta validator rather than adding a new mechanism. This rides the same per-update loop that already rejects empty create prompts (3586).
- **Change sketch:** In `apply_ticket_workflow_delta` update loop: if the normalized `update.workflow_step_status` is in the satisfying set AND `update.evidence.is_null()` AND no `workflow_step_evidence` already exists on the row, `anyhow::bail!` with a message pointing at the step's `workflow_exit_gate`. Persist the evidence (already done at 3558) so the audit row at `merge_ticket_self_work_metadata` (3990) carries it. Pair with workflow-1 so the guarded transition also records the evidence ref.
- **Prüfsatz:** Q1 hardens `apply_ticket_workflow_delta` update validation. Q3/Q4 unchanged. Q7 keyed on explicit step id. Q9 evidence becomes a required, audited artifact for phase satisfaction (feeds process-mining by skill/phase). Q10 add a test: a delta marking a step `verified` with null evidence is rejected; with evidence it succeeds. Determinism-split honored: presence-of-evidence is deterministic, quality stays review.
- **Risk:** Low. Only blocks evidence-free satisfying flips. Reducer prompts already instruct 'only after evidence supports the delta' (service.rs:12573), so this enforces existing intent.
- **Verifier guidance:** Valid as written. One implementation refinement for the change sketch: the "no workflow_step_evidence already exists on the row" carve-out must inspect the LOADED row metadata (the `item` from locate_workflow_step / a fresh load_ticket_self_work_item_raw read), NOT the freshly-built metadata_update which does not yet reflect prior state — otherwise a legitimate re-flip on a step that already carries evidence could be wrongly rejected. With that, the precise guard is: in the update loop, after locating `item`, if normalize_token(update.workflow_step_status) is in the satisfying set {verified,passed,satisfied,closed,done,completed} AND update.evidence.is_null() AND metadata_string_value(&item.metadata, "workflow_step_evidence").is_none(), then anyhow::bail! citing the step's workflow_exit_gate. Test: extend the 12418 fixture style with a second case marking phase-0-reducer "verified" with evidence:null expecting an Err, and the existing non-null case expecting Ok.
- **Grounding caveat:** All anchors verified in real code. WorkflowDeltaUpdateStep.evidence is #[serde(default)] Value at tickets.rs:638; stored only if !update.evidence.is_null() at 3557. workflow_step_satisfied (4019-4027) keys ONLY on the status string set "verified|passed|satisfied|closed|done|completed" (4024-4025) with zero evidence consultation, so a {workflow_step_status:"verified"} delta with null evidence satisfies predecessors. workflow_exit_gate is written at 3486-3492 and rendered to the reducer prompt at service.rs:12549, but grep of every exit_gate reference confirms it is never compared at flip time. The existing test at 12418/12445 only ever passes non-null evidence, leaving the null-evidence path unguarded and untested.

Add a unit test asserting hard_runtime_blocker_retry_cooldown_secs and runtime_error_is_transient_api_failure both return retryable for an err string like "failed to ensure local chat backend before direct session: chat backend for Qwen3.5-27B did not become ready within 180s", and that failed_worker_route_status(false,false,true) == "pending".
- **Grounding caveat:** All four anchors exist and the weakness is real. Supervisor emits exactly the three cited readiness-failure strings: supervisor.rs:1943 ("did not become healthy while waiting for existing startup"), 2422/2449 ("exited before becoming ready"), 2461 ("did not become ready within {}s"). ensure_chat_backend_ready (supervisor.rs:437) failures propagate via turn_loop.rs:403 wrapped with .context("failed to ensure local chat backend before direct session"). Neither classifier matches any of these: summarize_known_infra_error (turn_loop.rs:1273-1342) and hard_runtime_blocker_retry_cooldown_secs (turn_loop.rs:1194-1254) only carry the local-infra phrase "chat backend could not start on this host" (lines 1249, 1322-1338), which the supervisor never emits. A grep of both turn_loop.rs and service.rs for the supervisor phrasings returns zero matches except the .context wrapper at turn_loop.rs:403. The burn path is confirmed: service.rs:4324-4342 gates retry on runtime_error_is_transient_api_failure, which returns false (cooldown None, service.rs:11442-11444) for these strings, so retry_not_before is None and the item is NOT held. runtime_blocker_backoff_remaining_secs (actual line 14801, finding cited 14763 — minor line drift, function is real) also yields None. Anchor line for that function is slightly off but not invented.

The migration genuinely runs RENAME/CREATE/INSERT/DROP as a single un-transacted execute_batch under WAL+autocommit on a fresh connection, so a crash between CREATE and INS...

- [x] **shipped**
- **Anchors:** `tickets.rs::migrate_ticket_self_work_items_schema (10440-10489)`, `rxdb_peer.rs::sync_ticket_state_with_database (3983)`
- **Problem:** Legacy DBs run RENAME/CREATE/INSERT/DROP as one execute_batch with no BEGIN/COMMIT while daemon (3s projection), TUI, CLIs share the file; a kill mid-migration leaves the canonical table missing and replicates a truncated ctox_ticket_self_work_items over WebRTC. Probe re-runs on all 90 open sites.
- **Fix:** Wrap in conn.unchecked_transaction and gate behind the persistence.rs::initialized_paths/governance.rs once-guard; 1:1 copy unchanged.
- **Change sketch:** tx=conn.unchecked_transaction; tx.execute_batch(SQL); tx.commit. Tickets-local OnceLock once-guard in open_ticket_db.

- **Verifier guidance:** KEEP with two refinements to the fix framing. (1) The transaction wrap (conn.unchecked_transaction; tx.execute_batch(SQL); tx.commit()) is the load-bearing, crash-safety fix and matches existing precedent at tickets.rs:4862/4899 — keep this. (2) Do NOT oversell the once-guard: persistence.rs::initialized_paths (173) is a per-PROCESS in-memory HashSet<PathBuf>, not cross-process and not crash-safe, so it must be presented as a minor redundant-probe optimization, not the safety mechanism. The atomic transaction is what closes the corruption window. (3) Optional hardening worth noting in the change: the early-return guard at 10448-10453 means recovery after a partial run is impossible because the new empty table no longer contains `UNIQUE(source_system, kind)`; keeping the legacy table around (don't DROP until after a verified row-count match, all inside the same tx) makes recovery and post-commit verification possible and gives the audit/verification evidence the Pruefsatz asks for. The early-return guard at 10448-10453 (returns Ok if table missing or no `UNIQUE(source_system, kind)`) means a subsequent open does NOT re-copy from the legacy table -> data effectively lost. Migration is reached on EVERY open_ticket_db -> ensure_schema (9971) -> ensure_ticket_event_routing_rows (10405/10436), including the projection path business_os_ticket_projection_documents (7199). ctox_ticket_self_work_items IS a replicated WebRTC collection (BUSINESS_OS_TICKET_COLLECTIONS, tickets.rs:664) projected from this exact table via sync_ticket_state_with_database (rxdb_peer.rs:3983), so a truncated/empty table replicates over WebRTC. Real now. conn.unchecked_transaction() is already the established atomicity pattern in this same file (4862, 4899).


### `process-mining-audit` · `pm-1` — Confirmed findings are silently stale-dropped on a single missed audit tick

🏷 Pass 1 · impact **high** · effort **S** · verifier **keep**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** ✅ **DO — real stability win** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **clear** — Real liveness/correctness defect, fully grounded in live code. The resolution UPDATE (findings.rs:170-179) stales a confirmed finding after a single missed observation, while promotion requires two consecutive ticks (record_or_confirm fi...

- [x] **shipped**
- **Anchors:** `src/core/service/harness_mining/findings.rs::mark_unseen_stale`, `src/core/service/harness_mining/findings.rs::run_audit_tick`, `src/core/mission/queue.rs::render_confirmed_harness_findings_block`
- **Problem:** mark_unseen_stale fires `UPDATE ... SET status='stale' WHERE status IN ('detected','confirmed') AND last_seen_at < tick_started_at`. Staling a `detected` finding is the intended 2-tick gate. But it ALSO stales a `confirmed` finding the instant it is not re-observed at one tick. The underlying algorithms are window-bounded (conformance `--window 1000`, stuck/sojourn over recent rows): a transient gap — a breach event aging just out of the 1000-row window, a sub-table query erroring inside `run_or_error`, or a single failed tick — flips a confirmed, operator-relevant finding straight to `stale` with resolved_by='audit-tick:no-longer-observed', WITHOUT ever passing acknowledge/mitigate/verify. Once stale, `render_confirmed_harness_findings_block` (which lists only status='confirmed') stops injecting it into the queue-repair prompt, so the recovery agent loses the signal. The downgrade is indistinguishable from a genuine resolution.
- **Fix:** Tighten the existing stale predicate so a *confirmed* finding requires N consecutive unseen ticks (symmetric with the 2-tick gate that promoted it), instead of one. This hardens the exact UPDATE that is the gate's resolution half, keeping detected→stale at one tick but making confirmed→stale require sustained absence — preserving the durable signal the repair prompt depends on.
- **Change sketch:** In mark_unseen_stale, split the single UPDATE: keep detected→stale at `last_seen_at < tick_started_at`; for confirmed, gate on a `last_seen_at` older than a small grace (e.g. one extra tick window already represented in the row's last_seen_at vs a passed `confirmed_grace_before` arg derived by the caller as the second-to-last tick start). No new table — reuse last_seen_at and confirmed_at already on the row. run_audit_tick passes both the current tick start and the prior tick start (it already owns started_at; persist last tick start in ctox_hm_audit_runs which already exists).
- **Prüfsatz:** Q1 hardens findings.rs::mark_unseen_stale + the 2-tick gate. Q4: all status moves still go through findings.rs guarded UPDATEs, no new state path. Q7: identity stays the explicit `signature` hard key (kind|entity_type|entity_id|lane) — no semantic matching added. Q9: makes the audit trail truthful (stale means really gone, not flickered). Q10: pin with a test 'confirmed survives one missed tick, stales after two' alongside existing third_observation_does_not_re_confirm.
- **Risk:** Low — change is confined to one UPDATE and one caller; back-compat preserved because detected behavior is unchanged. Slight risk of keeping a genuinely-resolved finding one tick longer, which is the safer direction.
- **Verifier guidance:** Real and worth keeping, with two corrections to tighten it. (1) Drop the 'single failed tick' trigger from the problem statement — it is false: a fully failed brief takes run_audit_tick's Err branch (findings.rs:412) and never calls mark_unseen_stale. Keep the two valid triggers: a run_or_error-swallowed sub-algorithm error (brief.rs:226-231 + the .unwrap_or(true)/.unwrap_or(0) defaults at brief.rs:93/83) and an event aging out of the conformance/drift window=1000 (conformance.rs:35). (2) Simplify the muddled changeSketch. Cleanest deterministic form: split mark_unseen_stale's single UPDATE into two. Keep detected->stale at `last_seen_at < tick_started_at`. For confirmed->stale, require absence across the prior tick too: pass run_audit_tick the previous run's started_at (already queryable from ctox_hm_audit_runs ORDER BY started_at DESC LIMIT 1 OFFSET 1, index idx_ctox_hm_audit_runs_started) and gate confirmed on `last_seen_at < prev_tick_started_at` so a confirmed finding only stales after TWO consecutive ticks of non-observation — symmetric with the 2-tick promotion gate. If no prior run exists, do not stale confirmed (safe direction). Test to add alongside third_observation_does_not_re_confirm: confirm a finding, run a tick where it is not re-observed -> assert still 'confirmed'; run a second unseen tick -> assert 'stale'. Cost is one finding lingering at most one extra tick, the safer direction.
- **Grounding caveat:** All three anchors verified. findings.rs:169-181 mark_unseen_stale UPDATEs status IN ('detected','confirmed') AND last_seen_at < tick_started_at with resolved_by COALESCE 'audit-tick:no-longer-observed' — matches the quote exactly. run_audit_tick (findings.rs:335-427) calls mark_unseen_stale only on the Ok branch. render_confirmed_harness_findings_block (queue.rs:1207-1274) lists ONLY status='confirmed' (line 1229), so a staled finding is dropped from the repair prompt. The 2-tick promotion gate is real (record_or_confirm detected->confirmed, findings.rs:103-112) but the resolution side is asymmetric at 1 tick, with no grace/consecutive-miss counter anywhere. Mechanism confirmed: brief::synthesize uses run_or_error (brief.rs:226-231) which swallows a sub-algorithm error into the errors[] array and defaults the metric to its healthy value (conformance_ok .unwrap_or(true) line 93; stuck_count .unwrap_or(0) line 83), so the brief still returns Ok and the finding is simply not re-emitted -> mark_unseen_stale flips the confirmed finding. Conformance/drift are window-bounded (window=1000, conformance.rs:35-36), so an event aging out of the recent window also drops the finding. Re-detection later creates a brand-new 'detected' row (record_or_confirm lookup excludes stale, findings.rs:94), so the signal must re-climb the 2-tick gate. ONE inaccuracy in the finding: the 'single failed tick' trigger is wrong — a fully failed brief takes the Err branch (findings.rs:412) and SKIPS mark_unseen_stale. But the two other triggers (run_or_error-swallowed sub-table error; window aging) are valid and independent, so the weakness is real.
