The defect is demonstrable in live code: run_audit_tick writes status='failed'/error_text and only returns Err; the w...

> ⚠️ **Canonical issue:** implement the **Canonical scope** + **Verifier guidance** below. (The stale original Fix/Change-sketch fields were removed in the live re-audit cleanup.)

- [x] **shipped**
- **Canonical scope:** Implement the corrected scope in **Verifier guidance**. Treat the superseded original fix/sketch/test mapping as historical context, not instructions.
- **Canonical verification:** Use the Q10/test instructions in **Verifier guidance**; if they conflict with any superseded original field, Verifier guidance wins.
- **Anchors:** `src/core/service/harness_mining/findings.rs::run_audit_tick`, `src/core/service/service.rs::start_harness_audit_watcher`, `src/core/service/process_mining.rs::diagnose_harness_findings`, `src/core/service/harness_mining/mod.rs::ui_snapshot`
- **Problem:** run_audit_tick wraps the brief in a transaction and on error writes `UPDATE ctox_hm_audit_runs SET status='failed', error_text=...`. But NOTHING reads those failed rows: diagnose_harness_findings reads only ctox_hm_findings, ui_snapshot recomputes algorithms live and never touches audit_runs, and the watcher's only signal is a transient `push_event("Harness audit tick failed")` log line that scrolls out of the TUI feed. If the 300s tick fails persistently (DB lock contention during the boot burst the code itself warns about, a corrupt sub-table, a panic in one algorithm), findings silently stop being recorded/confirmed and the queue-repair prompt silently stops receiving them — the harness believes it is healthy because no findings means 'no signal' and a dead audit means 'no findings'. This is a Pruefsatz Q9 hole: the evidence pipeline can die without evidence of its own death.
- **Risk:** Low — additive read in an existing diagnose function; cannot affect runtime state.
- **Verifier guidance:** KEEP the substance — the finding is grounded, compliant, and unhandled. One required tightening for the change + test, otherwise it does not compile against the real schema:

1) Real-schema awareness. The live ctox_hm_audit_runs schema is defined in findings.rs:56-66: columns run_id (PK), started_at, finished_at, status, brief_json, findings_recorded/confirmed/marked_stale, error_text. The change must query 'SELECT status, error_text, started_at FROM ctox_hm_audit_runs ORDER BY started_at DESC LIMIT 1'. Note the existing process_mining self-diagnose test fixture (process_mining.rs:6613) creates a STRIPPED MOCK ctox_hm_audit_runs (audit_id, status) lacking started_at/error_text — so the new read will fail against that fixture. The new test MUST create/seed the real columns (run_id, started_at, status, error_text), not reuse the stripped mock, and the table_exists guard in diagnose_harness_findings currently checks only ctox_hm_findings, so the audit-runs read needs its own table_exists guard (use unwrap_or to stay non-fatal on deployments where the table is absent).

2) Tighten the stale threshold to a deterministic, env-free constant. HARNESS_AUDIT_TICK_SECS=300 lives in service.rs (service.rs:110); diagnose lives in process_mining.rs and must NOT read process-env. Hard-code or share the 300s*3 bound as a module const in process_mining.rs (or pass it in) rather than reading any env/config — staleness is a deterministic fact, so a fixed multiplier is fine and keeps it env-free per the guardrails.

3) Severity discipline: emit 'critical' only for status='failed' on the latest run; emit 'warning' for stale (newest started_at older than ~3x tick). Do not escalate a single stale gap to critical, since a freshly-booted deployment (first tick offset is 60s, service.rs:8926) will legitimately have no recent run for the first minute — guard the stale branch so a never-run deployment (no rows) stays 'ok', matching the existing table_exists==0 'ok' path at process_mining.rs:2596-2604.

With those three adjustments the finding is a clean keep-quality hardening.
- **Grounding caveat:** All four anchors exist and the problem is real. findings.rs:412-425 (run_audit_tick) writes status='failed', error_text on the Err branch and only returns Err. service.rs:8940-8942 (start_harness_audit_watcher) handles that error with a transient push_event("Harness audit tick failed: {err}") only. process_mining.rs:2583-2620 (diagnose_harness_findings) reads ONLY ctox_hm_findings, never ctox_hm_audit_runs. mod.rs:244-300 (ui_snapshot) recomputes algorithms live and never reads ctox_hm_audit_runs. I grepped all of src/: the ONLY non-write reference to ctox_hm_audit_runs outside findings.rs is the telemetry event-mapping rule at process_mining.rs:3925 which records the write as a process-mining activity, NOT a consumer of failed/stale run status. The meta-evidence gap (Pruefsatz Q9: the audit pipeline can die without evidence of its own death) is genuine.

- [x] **shipped**

- **Problem:** The strongest conformance signal — a SQLite table mutation with NO mapping rule (`ctox_pm_unmapped_events`) — is the literal 'a decision happened that the state machine cannot see'. process_mining.rs surfaces it only as an ephemeral CLI finding via findings_for_mapping ('unmapped_sqlite_events', severity critical) inside the mapping/diagnose report. brief::synthesize, the ONLY input to run_audit_tick, builds findings from 5 algorithms and never reads unmapped_events or the rejected rows of ctox_core_spawn_edges. So the most important coverage gaps never enter ctox_hm_findings, never get the 2-tick confirmation, never reach the queue-repair prompt, and never get a lifecycle. A persistent coverage hole is invisible to every automated consumer.
- **Fix:** Add an `unmapped_coverage` finding kind to the SAME brief::synthesize ranking that already feeds the 2-tick gate, sourced from the counts process_mining already computes. This rides the existing brief→audit-tick→findings pipeline; no new scanner, no new table — it just promotes an already-recorded signal into the durable findings lifecycle.
- **Change sketch:** In brief::synthesize, add a read of `SELECT COUNT(*) FROM ctox_pm_unmapped_events WHERE scanned_at >= <recent>` (table already exists, guarded by table-exists like the others) and a read of rejected ctox_core_spawn_edges count. If >0, push a finding `{kind:'unmapped_coverage'|'spawn_rejected', severity:'critical'}`. extract_anchor in findings.rs already pulls entity anchors generically. The audit-tick then confirms/stales it identically to conformance_breach.
- **Prüfsatz:** Q1 hardens brief::synthesize + run_audit_tick coverage. Q5: rejected spawn edges (enforce_core_spawn output) finally get durable audit evidence. Q7: keyed on the same explicit signature, no semantic dedupe. Q9: closes the biggest Q9 coverage gap — the state machine's own blind spots become tracked findings. Q10: test that seeding an unmapped_events row makes audit-tick record a confirmed 'unmapped_coverage' finding after two ticks.
- **Risk:** Medium — must guard for the table not existing on older deployments (other reads already do via run_or_error); risk of finding noise if scan window is too wide, so scope to recent scanned_at.
- **Verifier guidance:** Solid finding; keep as-is with one implementation precision. extract_anchor (findings.rs:432) only inspects worst_case/top_breach/state/top_driver keys, so a coverage-count finding has no per-entity anchor and will get signature 'unmapped_coverage|-|-|-' (one durable finding per kind). That is acceptable and matches the keyed-signature intent, but the Q10 test must assert on kind/signature and the confirmed status after two ticks, NOT on an entity anchor. Also recommend two distinct kinds as the sketch suggests ('unmapped_coverage' for ctox_pm_unmapped_events, 'spawn_rejected' for accepted=0 spawn edges) since they map to different guards (mapping coverage vs Core Spawn Guard). Scope both COUNT(*) reads to a recent scanned_at/updated_at window and wrap them in run_or_error so older deployments without the table degrade gracefully (the brief already swallows per-source errors that way rather than via explicit table_exists).
- **Grounding caveat:** All four anchors exist and the weakness is real. findings_for_mapping (process_mining.rs:2687) emits the critical 'unmapped_sqlite_events' code only into an ephemeral diagnose-report Value via push_subsystem (line 2351); it is never persisted to ctox_hm_findings. record_unmapped_event (process_mining.rs:4355) DOES durably persist the signal to ctox_pm_unmapped_events at scan time (called at lines 4456 and 4511), with a scanned_at index (lines 274,297) — so the signal genuinely exists but is never consumed. brief::synthesize (brief.rs:42, imports at line 18) sources only 5 algorithms (stuck_cases, conformance, drift, sojourn, variants) and reads neither ctox_pm_unmapped_events nor rejected spawn edges; grep confirms nothing in harness_mining/ touches either. run_audit_tick (findings.rs:335) builds findings exclusively from brief['findings']. ctox_core_spawn_edges has accepted INTEGER NOT NULL (core_transition_guard.rs:116) and evaluate_core_spawn writes accepted=0 rows on violation, so 'rejected spawn edges' is a real durable Core-Spawn-Guard output. queue.rs:1229 confirms the queue-repair prompt reads only Some('confirmed') findings, so a signal that never reaches confirmed never reaches repair — exactly as claimed.

- **Anchors:** `src/core/mission/queue.rs::apply_queue_repair_actions`, `src/core/mission/queue.rs::run_agentic_queue_repair`, `src/core/mission/queue.rs::cleanup_queue_scope`
- **Problem:** apply_queue_repair_actions mutates queue items (cancel/block/release/reprioritize/complete) guarded only by per-action existence and the state edge. It never checks the message_key against the model own canonical_hot_path or confirmed ctox_hm_findings, so a parse slip cancels a hot-path item; it emits no harness-flow event (unlike cleanup_queue_scope); and each update_queue_task uses try with no transaction, so a model-proposed complete rejected without terminal-success proof (channels.rs:7643) aborts the loop after earlier actions committed and the verify pass never runs.
- **Risk:** Match exact message_key tokens only; distinguish guard-rejection from infra errors and propagate the latter.
- **Verifier guidance:** Keep the hot-path-refusal and per-action audit additions as proposed (exact message_key token match against the leading token of each canonical_hot_path entry; skip+record matches; emit queue.repair_applied / queue.repair_rejected via the existing record_harness_flow_event_lossy). Tighten two things. (1) Hot-path entries are NOT guaranteed message_keys: the prompt format is `- <message_key or thread> :: <why>` (queue.rs:75), so the leading token can be a thread or free text. That is fail-safe here (a non-key token simply matches no action, so worst case is refusing nothing extra) — but the change must treat the hot-path set as best-effort string tokens, never assume validity, and never use it to AUTHORIZE a mutation, only to REFUSE one. (2) The error-capture mechanism as written is unsound and must change: enforce_core_transition rejects via `anyhow::bail!("{}", ...)` (core_transition_guard.rs:429), an untyped anyhow::Error indistinguishable from a genuine infra error (DB lock/IO). "Capture each update_queue_task Err into a rejected list" would silently swallow infra failures as model mistakes. Instead, determine terminal acceptability deterministically BEFORE mutating — use the existing evaluate_core_transition boolean path (core_transition_guard.rs:424, returns proof.accepted without bailing) or the queue_completed_has_terminal_success_proof predicate to pre-classify a complete/terminal action: if the guard would reject, record it as queue.repair_rejected and skip the mutation entirely; let any actual Err from update_queue_task continue to propagate/abort as today (infra errors must NOT be demoted to rejected outcomes). The Q10 test must therefore assert: (a) an action whose message_key is in canonical_hot_path is refused + a queue.repair_rejected event recorded; (b) a batch of [valid cancel, unproven complete] applies the cancel and records the complete as rejected WITHOUT aborting, while a simulated infra error still propagates.
- **Grounding caveat:** All three anchors exist and every problem sub-claim holds. apply_queue_repair_actions (queue.rs:1410-1483) guards only by per-action load_queue_task is_none() existence (1416-1418) plus the state edge; it never compares action.message_key against canonical_hot_path (parsed at 1347, stored in the view at 1141, never passed to the apply fn — only parsed.repair_actions is, at 1124). It emits no harness-flow event, whereas cleanup_queue_scope DOES emit record_harness_flow_event_lossy("queue.cleanup_scope") at 634-653. Each branch uses `let _ = update_queue_task(...)?` with no batch transaction, so a rejected action propagates and aborts the loop after earlier per-connection commits. Chain confirmed: update_queue_task (channels.rs:2507) -> set_routing_status (2624) -> enforce_queue_route_status_transition (7572) -> terminal-success-proof gate (7643-7647) -> enforce_core_transition (7670). A model `complete` -> handled/Completed without proof bails. run_agentic_queue_repair (1112) propagates `?` (1124) straight up via repair_queue_state (565), skipping the verify pass (1126-1136). Cited channels.rs:7643 is the correct terminal-proof region (line slightly imprecise: the gate is 7643-7647, the enforce call 7670, but substance correct).

So the real gap is broader than "generic creates flood, business-os caps" — even the capped path turns a benign retry into an error. The idempotency-key fix closes both: stable message_key -> stable edge_id -> ON CONFLICT(edge_id)/ON CONFLICT(message_key) in-place. (2) Tighten the changeSketch wording "ON CONFLICT(message_key) makes it a no-op": it is an in-place DO UPDATE (channels.rs:7951-7974), not a literal no-op — it refreshes status/observed_at/metadata. The spawn edge_id = deterministic_spawn_edge_id(request_json) hashes the full CoreSpawnRequest including child_entity_id=message_key (core_transition_guard.rs:439, 593-598), and accepted_spawn_budget_count counts ALL accepted rows sharing budget_key excluding only the current edge_id (core_transition_guard.rs:855-868). So each timestamp-salted retry is a distinct edge that spends one of the 64 budget — the flood claim holds. evaluate_core_spawn uses ON CONFLICT(edge_id) (line 455), which only deduplicates if the edge_id is stable, which requires a stable message_key. upsert_communication_message uses ON CONFLICT(message_key) DO UPDATE (channels.rs:7951), so a stabilized key collapses retries in place. One imprecision: the parenthetical "only business-os-command is idempotent (max_attempts=1)" — business-os-command (channels.rs:2364-2372) is budget-capped at 1, not idempotent; its message_key is still now-salted, so a crash-retry there produces a NEW message_key and is REJECTED by spawn_budget_exhausted (a hard bail), not silently deduped. That strengthens the underlying point.


### `review-outcome` · `review-1` — Terminal no-send decision scrapes free text instead of the parsed structured disposition

🏷 Pass 1 · impact **high** · effort **S** · verifier **revise**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** ✅ **DO — real stability win** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **clear** — All anchors verified against live code (line numbers drifted: 5311→5349, but symbols exact). The bug is real and exactly as framed: a hard terminal business outcome (close a founder/owner mail without sending vs. drive rework) is decided...

> ⚠️ **Canonical issue:** implement the **Canonical scope** + **Verifier guidance** below. (The stale original Fix/Change-sketch fields were removed in the live re-audit cleanup.)

- [x] **shipped**
- **Canonical scope:** Implement the corrected scope in **Verifier guidance**. Treat the superseded original fix/sketch/test mapping as historical context, not instructions.
- **Canonical verification:** Use the Q10/test instructions in **Verifier guidance**; if they conflict with any superseded original field, Verifier guidance wins.
- **Anchors:** `src/core/service/service.rs::review_outcome_is_terminal_no_send`, `src/core/service/service.rs:5311`, `src/core/mission/review.rs::ReviewDisposition`, `src/core/mission/review.rs::parse_disposition`, `src/core/mission/review.rs:1295`
- **Problem:** The reviewer already emits a structured DISPOSITION: SEND|NO_SEND block that parse_review_report parses into outcome.disposition (review.rs:1295 via parse_disposition, review.rs:1624). The ReviewOutcome.disposition docstring (review.rs:386-390) explicitly promises 'The reviewer sets this via the DISPOSITION: block — the service core never scrapes summary or finding text to derive it.' But the actual terminal no-send decision at service.rs:5311 calls review_outcome_is_terminal_no_send(&outcome) (service.rs:569), which lowercases summary+failed_gates+findings+open_items+evidence+categorized text and matches German/English phrase lists ('do not send','nicht senden','wait mode','warte', etc.) to decide whether to close a founder/owner mail terminally without sending. The parsed structured field is ignored at the decision point; the no-send-test helper (service.rs:~15284) does not even set outcome.disposition. This is a documented-invariant violation AND a forbidden semantic decision: a hard terminal business outcome (close-without-send vs. drive-rework) is being inferred by fuzzy keyword equality on prose, exactly the 'semantic equality not on a hard key' anti-pattern.
- **Risk:** Low — the reviewer prompt already mandates the DISPOSITION line; the AND-guard is strictly more conservative (a missing/SEND token now correctly routes to rework instead of silently closing). Only risk is older review reports that emitted no DISPOSITION line, which default to Send and therefore correctly no longer trigger terminal no-send.
- **Verifier guidance:** Finding is real, grounded, and compliant — but the changeSketch over-specifies a second edit that does not exist. There is exactly ONE call site of review_outcome_is_terminal_no_send (service.rs:5311); the "Fail branch at 5402" cited in the sketch is the proactive_founder_action path (5402-5439) and does NOT call the scraper or contain any terminal-no-send predicate, so it must NOT be touched. Tightened change, scoped to 5311 only: replace `if review_outcome_is_terminal_no_send(&outcome)` with `if matches!(outcome.disposition, review::ReviewDisposition::NoSend) && review_outcome_is_terminal_no_send(&outcome)`. This requires the explicit structured token while keeping the text scan as a strictly-narrowing corroborator, so a model that emits NO_SEND but then describes missing required work (says_missing_work=true) still correctly routes to rework instead of silently closing — preserving today's behavior on that axis. Tests: (1) keep both existing tests green but add `outcome.disposition = review::ReviewDisposition::NoSend;` to review_no_send_wait_is_terminal so it pins the new AND-gate; (2) add a false-positive case proving a FAIL report whose disposition is Send but whose summary literally contains 'do not send' is NOT treated as terminal no-send (currently it IS — that is the silent-close bug). Note the one real behavior change the finding correctly flags: legacy reports that emitted no DISPOSITION line default to Send and will no longer trigger terminal no-send; this is the intended tightening (the prompt has mandated the line at review.rs:77/1081/1200), but flag it in the commit so the operator is aware older queued reviews route to hold/rework rather than auto-close.
- **Grounding caveat:** All anchors verified against current code. service.rs:569 `review_outcome_is_terminal_no_send` is a pure text scraper: it lowercases summary + failed_gates + semantic_findings + open_items + evidence + categorized_findings and matches German/English phrase lists (says_no_send && says_wait && !says_missing_work, lines 588-635). The decision point at service.rs:5311 calls it and, when true, returns CompletionReviewDisposition::NoSend (5320) — this is the SOLE producer of that terminal disposition (downstream consumer at 3590 just reads the already-decided enum). The structured field outcome.disposition (review.rs:392, parsed at review.rs:1295 via parse_disposition at review.rs:1624) is provably never read in service.rs: grep for `review::ReviewDisposition` returns only `::Send` constructor sites (6636/6701/11642/11749/15244/18568/20565/20611), no read of outcome.disposition anywhere. The docstrings at review.rs:154-160 and 386-390 explicitly promise "the service core never scrapes summary or finding text to derive it" / "no keyword scraping on summary or evidence text in the service core," and the reviewer prompt at review.rs:77 + 1088 reinforces "the dispatcher reads the DISPOSITION line, not summary prose" — all three are directly contradicted by 5311. Test helper review_outcome_for_no_send_test (15162-15168) uses ReviewOutcome::skipped which defaults disposition to Send and never sets it, so the two existing no-send tests pin the scraper, not the structured contract.


### `review-outcome` · `review-2` — Review-rework retry budget (the loop terminal gate) is controlled by process env-vars

🏷 Pass 1 · impact **high** · effort **M** · verifier **keep**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** ✅ **DO — real stability win** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **clear** — Every anchor verified in live code (only line numbers drifted: 13256/13266 -> 13399/13409). Both helpers read std::env::var with no root/config path, and these thresholds gate genuine terminal failed-vs-requeue decisions (7990 "failed", ...

- [ ] **open**
- **Anchors:** `src/core/service/service.rs::review_checkpoint_requeue_block_threshold`, `src/core/service/service.rs::review_rework_checkpoint_requeue_block_threshold`, `src/core/service/service.rs:13256`, `src/core/service/service.rs:13266`, `src/core/service/service.rs:8688`
- **Scope note:** Canonical ticket for review/rework retry-budget env-var removal. Do not also implement this path through `governance-recovery · govrec-1`.
- **Problem:** The finite review/rework retry budget — the ranking function the state-machine proof relies on to guarantee termination (core_state_machine.rs:1610: 'review_rounds_left + reviewer_unavailable_retries_left + validator_rework_left strictly decreases') — is read at production runtime from std::env::var('CTOX_REVIEW_CHECKPOINT_REQUEUE_BLOCK_THRESHOLD') and CTOX_REVIEW_REWORK_CHECKPOINT_REQUEUE_BLOCK_THRESHOLD (service.rs:13256, 13266). These thresholds gate the terminal 'failed' vs requeue decision at the live call sites service.rs:8183, 8419, 8688 (queue_review_rejection_feedback_disposition) and 7902/3968/13294. This violates the CLAUDE.md hard rule 'No global env-var controls for runtime state' and the constraints doc anti-pattern 'globale Env-Var-Toggles fuer Runtime-Verhalten.' A determinism boundary that bounds the rework cascade is mutable by ambient process environment, so the auditable proof of termination depends on un-audited host state, and tests can drift from production behavior.
- **Fix:** Route the threshold through the typed AppConfig / SQLite runtime store via runtime_env::env_or_config(root, ...) exactly like other runtime settings, removing the bare std::env::var read. The constants REVIEW_CHECKPOINT_REQUEUE_BLOCK_THRESHOLD=5 and the MAX_* clamps (service.rs:120-124) stay as defaults/clamps; only the source of an override changes from process-env to durable config.
- **Change sketch:** Change review_checkpoint_requeue_block_threshold() and review_rework_checkpoint_requeue_block_threshold() (service.rs:13255-13275) to take `root: &Path` and read runtime_env::env_or_config(root, 'review_checkpoint_requeue_block_threshold', ...) instead of std::env::var, clamping with the existing MAX_* constants and falling back to the existing const default. Thread root through review_checkpoint_requeue_block_threshold_for_kind and its callers (they already have root). Add a test that writes the override into the test root's SQLite runtime config and asserts the terminal-failure threshold honors it (the constraints doc Q10 + CLAUDE.md 'tests must write to the SQLite runtime store, not std::env').
- **Prüfsatz:** Q1 hardens the review-rework terminal budget gate (queue_review_rejection_feedback_disposition + review_checkpoint_loop_disposition). Q2-Q6 unchanged: same dispatch path, same queue/internal-work flow, same single main work item, no new spawns. Q7 N/A. Q8 unchanged. Q9 makes the termination proof auditable from durable config rather than ambient env. Q10 a new SQLite-backed override test pins the invariant the env path lacked.
- **Risk:** Medium — must preserve the exact default (5) and clamp behavior so the state-machine termination proof holds; needs the standard env→config migration/backcompat note. Mechanical thread-through of root across ~6 call sites.
- **Verifier guidance:** Real, compliant, unhandled — keep. Two tightening notes for the implementer: (1) MAX_* clamps (5) currently EQUAL the const defaults (5), so today the env override can only LOWER the budget toward 1, never raise it above 5; preserve that exact clamp+default semantics when porting to env_or_config so the termination proof's finite-budget invariant is unchanged. (2) Thread-through is genuinely mechanical: every live call site already has `root: &Path` in scope (outcome_witness_retry_route_status 7900, outcome_witness_outbound_recovery_requeue_allowed 7924, queue_review_rejection_feedback_disposition 8682, the 3966 closure uses &root, and review_checkpoint_loop_disposition 13285 takes root), so only the two helpers and review_checkpoint_requeue_block_threshold_for_kind need a `root` param. Add the SQLite-backed override test (write into the test root's runtime config, assert terminal-failure threshold honors it) per CLAUDE.md "tests must write to the SQLite runtime store, not std::env."
- **Grounding caveat:** All anchors verified. service.rs:13256 reads std::env::var("CTOX_REVIEW_CHECKPOINT_REQUEUE_BLOCK_THRESHOLD") in review_checkpoint_requeue_block_threshold() (13255-13263); 13266 reads the REWORK key in review_rework_checkpoint_requeue_block_threshold() (13265-13275). Constants/clamps at 120-124 are exactly REVIEW_CHECKPOINT_REQUEUE_BLOCK_THRESHOLD=5, REVIEW_REWORK=5, MAX_*=5. Live terminal-gate call sites confirmed: 3968, 7902, 8183, 8419, 8688 (all "failed"-vs-requeue/pending decisions), plus 13294 via review_checkpoint_requeue_block_threshold_for_kind. The proof anchor at core_state_machine.rs:1610 quotes verbatim the ranking function "review_rounds_left + reviewer_unavailable_retries_left + validator_rework_left strictly decreases"; this env-controlled threshold bounds the requeue budget feeding that termination argument. The weakness is real: a determinism boundary (terminal failed vs requeue) is mutable by ambient process environment, violating CLAUDE.md "No global env-var controls for runtime state."


### `router-dispatch` · `router-4` — Durable-queue idle lease short-circuits before fresh founder inbound can preempt

🏷 Pass 1 · impact **high** · effort **M** · verifier **keep**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** ✅ **DO — real stability win** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **clear** — Genuine, well-researched ticket — the priority inversion is real and demonstrable in live code: at an idle tick the durable-queue lease (source_label "queue", rank 1) returns Ok(()) before inbound leasing ever runs, so a freshly-arrived ...

- [ ] **open**
- **Anchors:** `src/core/service/service.rs::route_external_messages`, `src/core/service/service.rs::maybe_lease_next_durable_queue_prompt_for_idle_dispatch`, `src/core/service/service.rs::source_label_dispatch_rank`
- **Problem:** At an idle boundary the router leases a durable-queue task at service.rs:9037 and immediately `return Ok(())`, BEFORE it ever reaches inbound channel leasing at 9128. So a freshly-arrived founder/owner email sitting in `communication_messages` does not get a chance to take the single serial slot that tick — a low/normal-priority bulk durable-queue task wins the race purely because it is examined first in the tick order. The in-memory ordering (`insert_pending_prompt_ordered`) correctly ranks founder mail above queue work via `source_label_dispatch_rank` (email:founder=4 > queue), but that ranking is never consulted at the durable-queue-vs-inbound boundary.
- **Fix:** Tighten the existing tick ordering so the durable-queue idle lease defers when higher-ranked inbound external work is already runnable. Reuse the existing `source_label_dispatch_rank` and a cheap 'is there pending founder/owner inbound' check (the same classification used at 9128) to gate the durable short-circuit — no new scheduler, just a rank comparison before consuming the slot.
- **Change sketch:** Before the `maybe_lease_next_durable_queue_prompt_for_idle_dispatch` branch, add a read-only non-leasing inbound probe (same shape as the existing list/read helpers, not a lease). If it shows a runnable inbound whose `inbound_source_label` rank exceeds the durable-queue rank (or simply is founder/owner), skip the durable lease this tick and fall through to inbound leasing at 9128. Compute the inbound rank from existing `inbound_source_label`/`source_label_dispatch_rank`. Record a 'router_defer_durable_for_founder' governance event for evidence. The durable task is still leased on a later tick once no higher-ranked inbound is pending.
- **Prüfsatz:** Q1 hardens the tick ordering inside route_external_messages and reuses source_label_dispatch_rank. Q2 stays the hot path; still serial, still one lease/tick. Q3 work still flows through Queue/inbound leasing. Q4/Q5/Q6 untouched. Q7 no semantic dedupe — ranking is on explicit source labels/roles. Q9 governance event documents the deferral. Q10 testable: seed one normal durable-queue task + one founder inbound at idle, run route_external_messages once, assert the founder prompt was enqueued and the durable task remained pending.
- **Risk:** Medium. Must avoid starving the durable queue if founder inbound is perpetually present — bound the deferral (e.g. only for top rank bands) and keep the existing FIFO/priority sort so durable work still drains; the governance event makes any starvation observable.
- **Verifier guidance:** Keep, with two tightening notes for implementation. (1) Drop the fabricated "constraints doc lines 121-123" justification — no such doc text exists; justify purely from the code-level rank inconsistency (rank-4 inbound losing the slot to rank-1 durable work because of examination order, contradicting source_label_dispatch_rank intent already applied elsewhere). (2) The deferral probe MUST be a read-only, non-leasing query (a pattern like list_stalled_inbound_messages at channels.rs:2045 returns full RoutedInboundMessage rows without leasing) so the guard does not consume/lease the inbound message it is only inspecting; compute its rank via inbound_source_label + source_label_dispatch_rank. Bound the defer to the top rank band (founder/owner/admin = rank 4, or strictly rank > durable-queue rank) and keep the existing FIFO/priority sort so the durable queue still drains on the next tick once no higher-ranked inbound is pending — the governance event ("router_defer_durable_for_founder", with an idempotence key) makes any starvation observable. Q10 test as proposed is sound: seed one pending durable-queue task + one fresh founder inbound at idle (busy=false), call route_external_messages once, assert the founder inbound was leased/enqueued ahead and the durable task remained pending; add a negative case (durable task only, no founder inbound) asserting the durable lease still fires so the guard does not over-block.
- **Grounding caveat:** All three anchors exist and the core mechanism holds. service.rs:9037 leases a durable-queue task and returns Ok(()) at 9044, strictly BEFORE inbound leasing at 9128. The pre-boundary in-memory check maybe_take_next_queued_prompt_for_idle_dispatch (9030, body at 9463) only inspects shared.pending_prompts, so a freshly-arrived founder email living in communication_messages (not yet leased into pending) is NOT a candidate there and loses the serial slot to a rank-1 queue task that tick. source_label_dispatch_rank (9915) returns 1 for "queue" (default fall-through) vs 4 for email:founder/owner/admin; durable QueuedPrompt is hard-coded source_label="queue" at 9493. The rank is consulted in insert_pending_prompt_ordered (9941) and the inbound sort at 9133-9137, but NOT at the durable-vs-inbound boundary — exactly as claimed. The durable queue list (channels.rs:7372) orders FIFO by route_status/created_at with no founder priority, confirming the "queue work wins purely by examination order" claim.

With busy:false, worker_active_count:1 the gate (service.rs:9027) returns before lease_pending_inbound_messages, so asserting route_status=='pending' AND lease_owner IS NULL AND list_queue_tasks([pending,leased]) empty is exactly the negative the busy-test mirrors for the other half of the gate. The only test that hits the gate, channel_router_does_not_repair_founder_mail_during_active_agent_loop (service.rs:21930), sets busy:true only (line 21971) and seeds route_status='failed', asserting the repair branch is skipped. No coverage of the gate exists outside service.rs. Confirmed: dropping the worker_active_count term would pass every existing test.

(2) apply_ticket_workflow_delta creates steps in a loop (3585-3621) independent of the update_steps loop (3539-3582), so a delta with create_steps but NO update_steps (omit the 'verified' mark on phase-0-reducer) is valid and CREATES implement-one-slice with its predecessor ref while leaving phase-0-reducer unverified — exactly the inspectable closed-gate state the risk note requires. ### `arch-godfiles` · `X2-02` — Worker-side working-hours boundary race can requeue a leased job while Drop fail-acks its keys

🏷 Pass 2 · impact **medium** · effort **S** · kind **bug** · verifier **revise**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** ✅ **DO — real stability win** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **clear** — The ticket is self-correcting and the CANONICAL scope (which Verifier guidance explicitly says wins over the superseded original) is fully grounded. All four anchors exist and are accurate (line numbers drifted ~+240 but symbols/blocks m...

> ⚠️ **Canonical issue:** implement the **Canonical scope** + **Verifier guidance** below. (The stale original Fix/Change-sketch fields were removed in the live re-audit cleanup.)

- [x] **shipped**
- **Canonical scope:** Implement the corrected scope in **Verifier guidance**. Treat the superseded original fix/sketch/test mapping as historical context, not instructions.
- **Canonical verification:** Use the Q10/test instructions in **Verifier guidance**; if they conflict with any superseded original field, Verifier guidance wins.
- **Anchors:** `src/core/service/service.rs::start_prompt_worker working-hours hold (3268-3283)`, `src/core/service/service.rs::PromptWorkerActivity::drop (3139-3238)`, `src/core/service/service.rs::PromptWorkerActivity::start (3109-3130)`, `src/core/service/service.rs::route_external_messages idle dispatch (9068-9070)`
- **Problem:** Dispatch normally checks working-hours hold before spawning (`maybe_start_next_queued_prompt_locked`, `enqueue_prompt`). The remaining bug is a boundary race: hours can flip to hold after the dispatch gate passes and before the worker reaches the defense-in-depth re-check at 3268. When that hold fires, it pushes the job back into pending_prompts (3274) for retry and returns — but it does NOT remove the job's leased keys from leased_message_keys_inflight. PromptWorkerActivity::Drop then runs (3139): the leaked-key filter at 3146/3152 still finds those keys inflight, so it fail-acks the leased queue messages via ack_leased_messages_with_failure_reason+fail_business_command_from_queue_error (3175/3183) and fail-acks leased ticket events (3223). Result: a boundary-race deferral can mark the underlying Business OS queue task and ticket lease 'failed' while the prompt is re-queued.
- **Risk:** Must keep the genuine-leak path (worker actually crashed) still fail-acking; only the intentional after-hours re-queue should release-not-fail. The unlease must use the same channels path the router uses elsewhere to avoid bypassing the queue status gate.
- **Verifier guidance:** REVISE. The lease-leak mechanism is real and the proposed fix is sound, but two things must be corrected before this is actionable. (1) Fix the causal story: the idle-dispatch path is NOT unguarded — maybe_start_next_queued_prompt_locked checks hold_reason at service.rs:10029 and returns None during a hold (and the durable-queue path checks at enqueue_prompt:9877). No worker is spawned during an active hold. The 3268 worker-side hold is reachable ONLY via a working-hours BOUNDARY RACE: hours flip to 'hold' in the window between the dispatch-side hours check passing and the worker thread reaching line 3268. The finding's framing ('route_external_messages calls start_prompt_worker directly without a working-hours check') is wrong and should be rewritten as 'the worker-side hours re-check at 3268 can fire after a clean dispatch when the working-hours window flips, and in that race it leaks the still-inflight leased keys into Drop's fail-ack path.' (2) Downgrade impact from high to medium (closer to low): the trigger is a sub-second boundary race, and only queue/ticket-backed jobs (non-empty leased_message_keys / leased_ticket_event_keys) are affected — TUI prompts carry empty leased keys (2079) and are immune. Corrected fix is exactly as the changeSketch proposes: in the 3269-3282 block, after insert_pending_prompt_ordered, call release_leased_keys_locked(&mut shared, &job.leased_message_keys, &job.leased_ticket_event_keys) so Drop's leaked-key filter (3146/3152) is empty; if you also want the durable queue task itself returned to 'pending', do it through the same channels unlease helper the router uses (do not raw-write), matching reconcile/restore semantics. Test: simulate the boundary race (job dispatched with hold_reason None, then hold_reason Some at the worker re-check), assert the queue task ends 'pending' not 'failed', the Business OS command is not failed, and the prompt is re-queued exactly once with no 'Failed N leaked queue lease(s)' event.
- **Grounding caveat:** Anchors all exist and are accurate. The 3268-3283 working-hours hold block re-inserts the job into pending_prompts (3274) but does NOT call release_leased_keys_locked, so the leased keys stay in shared.leased_message_keys_inflight. PromptWorkerActivity::Drop (3139) then filters keys still inflight (3146/3152) and fail-acks the queue task via ack_leased_messages_with_failure_reason (channels.rs:2208, marks 'failed', terminal) + fail_business_command_from_queue_error (3183), and fail-acks leased ticket events (3223). So a worker that REACHES the 3268 hold with keys still inflight will indeed have its leased queue task/command/ticket marked 'failed' while the prompt is re-queued — a real inconsistency, and untested. HOWEVER the finding's central causal claim is FALSE: it asserts route_external_messages at 9068 calls start_prompt_worker 'directly without a working-hours check'. It does not. The idle-dispatch path 9068 -> maybe_take_next_queued_prompt_for_idle_dispatch (9501) -> maybe_start_next_queued_prompt_after_recovery_locked (10055) -> maybe_start_next_queued_prompt_locked (10025) performs hold_reason() at line 10029 and returns None during a hold, so NO worker is spawned during an active hold. Likewise the durable-queue idle path (9075) goes through enqueue_prompt which checks hold_reason at 9877. Every dispatch path (TUI 2070, enqueue_prompt 9877, idle 10029) gates on working hours BEFORE spawning. The 3268 worker-side re-check is defense-in-depth and is only reachable via a working-hours BOUNDARY RACE (hours flip to hold in the window between the dispatch-gate passing and the worker reaching 3268), not the unconditional gap described.

- **Change sketch:** 3067 unwrap_or(0) -> ?.

Callers build_turn_plan (turn_engine.rs:100) and tui mod.rs:5778 already return Result and propagate with ?, so the ?-fix lands cleanly. CAVEAT: the cited anchor 'preflight loop (528)' is inaccurate — lcm.rs:528 is the LcmFixture.config struct field, not a preflight loop; that part of the narrative is miscited, but the four substantive anchors (3053-3068, 1166-1183, 1192-1202, build_turn_plan 95-107) are all correct and the bug is real right now.


### `compaction-internals` · `lcm-x4` — Compaction-timeout bail leaves CompactPolicy hot; trigger re-fires next turn

🏷 Pass 2 · impact **medium** · effort **S** · kind **concurrency** · verifier **keep**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** ✅ **DO — real stability win** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **clear** — All anchors verified in live code (line numbers drifted ~13 lines but symbols/locations correct). The success/timeout asymmetry is real: the compact-success arm calls policy.note_compacted() (direct_session.rs:1159) while the timeout arm...

- [x] **shipped**
- **Anchors:** `direct_session.rs timeout branch no note_compacted (1172-1202)`, `direct_session.rs policy field (345)`, `compact.rs::note_compacted (255-258), suppression (216-247)`
- **Problem:** CompactPolicy lives across turns and resets only via note_compacted(); the success path calls it (1159) but the timeout path interrupts and bails without it, so the dispatched ThreadCompactStart leaves the policy hot and the next turn first TokenCount immediately re-fires Compact on a thread just interrupted mid-compact.
- **Fix:** Call policy.note_compacted() on the timeout branch before bail, mirroring success.
- **Change sketch:** In the Err timeout arm (~1172) call policy.note_compacted() before the interrupt; keep the bail.
- **Prüfsatz:** Hardens the CompactPolicy state machine and its timeout caller; route_external_messages unchanged; no new spawn/status; no semantic equality; test: after Compact+note_compacted a subsequent in-turn TokenCount returns Continue; no data-plane impact.
- **Verifier guidance:** Real, well-scoped one-line hardening. Minor test-spec sharpening: the pruefsatz test as written ("a subsequent in-turn TokenCount returns Continue") proves in-turn suppression, but the finding's actual symptom is the CROSS-turn re-fire. The test should additionally assert that after the timeout-branch note_compacted(), suppressed_until_turn_end is still true entering the next run_turn (i.e. the first TokenCount of a fresh turn, before any TurnComplete, returns Continue) — mirroring what the success path already guarantees. Also worth a one-line code comment that note_compacted() on the timeout arm is deliberate (mark-then-interrupt) so a later reader doesn't 'tidy' it away as dead, since the bail makes its only effect cross-turn. Fix placement (call note_compacted() before issuing the TurnInterrupt RPC, keep the bail) is correct.
- **Grounding caveat:** All anchors verified. direct_session.rs success arm calls policy.note_compacted() at line 1159; the timeout arm (1172-1202) interrupts and bails via anyhow::bail! without ever calling it. policy is a persistent field of PersistentSession (line 345), passed &mut into run_turn_async (573/903) and NOT reset at turn start. The session is reused across turns: turn_loop.rs:919 calls session.run_turn in a loop and on Err does `continue` (line 930), keeping the same self.policy alive. compact.rs: suppressed_until_turn_end is set true ONLY by note_compacted() (257) and cleared ONLY by EventMsg::TurnComplete (247) — there is no per-turn reset, so the flag genuinely carries across the run_turn boundary. After a timeout bail the turn is interrupted with no TurnComplete, so the flag stays false (never set), and the next reused turn's first TokenCount evaluates emergency/adaptive fresh (compact.rs:219-243); with context still high after an interrupted-mid-compact thread it re-fires Compact. The success/timeout asymmetry is real and unintended.


### `compaction-internals` · `lcm-x5` — Force compaction can durably enlarge context with no rollback

🏷 Pass 2 · impact **medium** · effort **M** · kind **design-pattern** · verifier **keep**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** ✅ **DO — real stability win** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **clear** — Every anchor and behavioral claim verified against live code. The defect is real and reachable: each compaction pass commits its insert+delete via an unconditional SAVEPOINT RELEASE (insert_summary:2910) before the token recompute (compa...

- [x] **shipped**
- **Anchors:** `lcm.rs::compact loops progress-check after insert (1208-1241)`, `lcm.rs::compact_leaf_pass insert+delete (2693-2709)`, `turn_engine.rs::assess_compaction_guard advisory (121-127)`, `lcm.rs::summary_id_for now-salt (5995-6007)`
- **Problem:** Each pass deletes source context_items and inserts a summary BEFORE checking tokens dropped (1216-1222), so a regressing chunk commits a net-larger context irreversibly with no outer tx; NoProgress is only telemetry; summary_id_for also salts the hash with iso_now() defeating content-addressed idempotency (the now-salt anti-pattern Pass-1 flagged for queue keys).
- **Fix:** Wrap each pass in unchecked_transaction and commit only if context_token_count strictly decreased (force: not increased); drop the iso_now() salt.
- **Change sketch:** compact passes: begin tx, insert/delete, recompute; if regressed ROLLBACK+None else commit; remove iso_now() in summary_id_for.
- **Prüfsatz:** Hardens the compact loop and pass fns, behavior-preserving on success and persistence-preserving on regression; dispatch untouched; no new spawn/status; semantic equality none, gate is the deterministic token count; test asserts tokens_after<=tokens_before always; LCM SQLite only.
- **Verifier guidance:** Real, reachable, novel. Keep with three accuracy refinements for the fix: (1) Pruefsatz wording 'persistence-preserving on regression' is imprecise — it is persistence-CORRECTING (today a regression is durably written; after the fix it is rolled back). State this honestly rather than claiming preservation. (2) The cleanest implementation is a SAVEPOINT scoped around ONLY the DB mutation (insert+delete+recompute) inside compact_leaf_pass/compact_condensed_pass — not a fresh outer unchecked_transaction spanning summarize_with_escalation, because the summarizer call must NOT run inside a held write lock; insert_summary already uses savepoints, so reuse that idiom: on recompute showing regression, ROLLBACK TO + return None. (3) Dropping the iso_now() salt is a COUPLED behavior change, not a free drop: with summary_id content-addressed and summaries using INSERT OR REPLACE (PRIMARY KEY summary_id), two passes summarizing identical content at the same depth/conversation would now collide/replace. That is the desired idempotency direction (matches the Pass-1 now-salt rejection) but should be flagged as a deliberate semantic change with the INSERT-OR-REPLACE + summary_messages/summary_edges INSERT-OR-IGNORE accumulation in mind. The mandated test should assert tokens_after<=tokens_before for both force=false and force=true, including a constructed regressing-summarizer case to prove the rollback path.
- **Grounding caveat:** All four anchors verified current. lcm.rs:1216-1222 computes current tokens and only break-s on `current >= previous_tokens` AFTER compact_leaf_pass returns; the pass's insert_summary (2871-2920) wraps insert+delete-of-source-ordinals in a self-contained SAVEPOINT that RELEASEs unconditionally on DB success, independent of token outcome — so a regressing pass durably commits with no outer rollback. assess_compaction_guard (turn_engine.rs:121-127) emits NoProgress/StillHot as an advisory summary string only. summary_id_for (5995-6007) salts the hash with iso_now(), and summaries.summary_id is PRIMARY KEY with INSERT OR REPLACE, so identical content never content-addresses/dedupes. Regression is genuinely reachable: the escalation guard (3128-3136) bounds summary_tokens against input_tokens = estimate_tokens(leaf_source_text) which is INFLATED by per-message `[timestamp]` prefixes + `\n\n` joins + the fallback's appended ' [Truncated from N tokens]', while the context reduction is sum(selected message.token_count) on RAW content — so summary.token_count can exceed the removed sum, especially for small leaf chunks. Worst-case site is real and hot: force=true is the emergency exact-token-overflow compaction at turn_loop.rs:577. No existing test asserts tokens_after<=tokens_before.


### `concurrency-isolation` · `X2-2` — runtime_env_kv full-table DELETE+reinsert under read-modify-write callers loses concurrent writers' keys

🏷 Pass 2 · impact **medium** · effort **S** · kind **concurrency** · verifier **revise**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** ✅ **DO — real stability win** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **clear** — The lost-update race is real and demonstrably reachable: write_runtime_env_map blanket-DELETEs runtime_env_kv and reinserts a stale full snapshot inside one DEFERRED transaction, while every mutator (CLI persist_runtime_turn_timeout, TUI...

> ⚠️ **Canonical issue:** implement the **Canonical scope** + **Verifier guidance** below. (The stale original Fix/Change-sketch fields were removed in the live re-audit cleanup.)

- [ ] **open**
- **Canonical scope:** Implement the corrected scope in **Verifier guidance**. Treat the superseded original fix/sketch/test mapping as historical context, not instructions.
- **Canonical verification:** Use the Q10/test instructions in **Verifier guidance**; if they conflict with any superseded original field, Verifier guidance wins.
- **Anchors:** `src/core/execution/models/runtime_env.rs::write_runtime_env_map (lines 202-214, DELETE FROM runtime_env_kv then reinsert full in-memory map inside one txn)`, `src/core/execution/models/runtime_env.rs::save_runtime_env_map (line 53, entry point)`, `src/core/main.rs::persist_runtime_turn_timeout (lines 1964-1979, load->insert one key->save)`, `src/core/ui/tui/mod.rs::persist_setup_wizard_state (lines 1912-1914, load->insert one key->save from TUI thread)`
- **Problem:** write_runtime_env_map runs `DELETE FROM runtime_env_kv` followed by a reinsert of the caller's entire in-memory BTreeMap, inside a single transaction. Every public mutator is a read-modify-write: load_runtime_env_map (full snapshot) -> mutate exactly one key -> save_runtime_env_map. The TUI worker thread (persist_setup_wizard_state), the CLI (persist_runtime_turn_timeout and main.rs:553-558), and the service loop all do this against the SAME runtime/ctox-runtime.sqlite3 with independent connections. busy_timeout serializes the two transactions but cannot prevent the logical lost update: writer A loads {K_old}, writer B loads {K_old}, A inserts K_a and commits {K_old,K_a}, then B's transaction DELETEs everything and reinserts its stale {K_old,K_b}, erasing K_a. Because the table is rewritten wholesale rather than per-key upserted, any key a concurrent writer added between B's read and B's write is silently dropped — exactly the full-map DELETE+reinsert hazard the concern calls out.
- **Risk:** Low: behavior- and persistence-preserving (same table, same key/value columns). The only semantic care point is deletions-by-absence; if callers rely on 'save replaces the whole map', the remove-set must be made explicit, otherwise a stale key could linger. Mitigated by the fact that all in-tree callers do load->mutate-one->save.
- **Verifier guidance:** KEEP the weakness (real, reachable lost-update race), but the changeSketch's "minimal safe version" — upsert all provided keys and SKIP the blanket DELETE — is wrong and would regress. The blanket DELETE is load-bearing for the projection caller: save_runtime_state_projection (runtime_env.rs:67-78) strips is_runtime_state_key keys then re-injects ONLY the CURRENT state's runtime keys via apply_runtime_state_to_env_map (line 75). When the operator switches config (local->API, drops an aux backend), the new state map contains a DIFFERENT subset of the ~32 is_runtime_state_key keys (runtime_state.rs:493-531), and the DELETE is what removes now-stale projection keys like CTOX_ENGINE_MODEL/CTOX_ENGINE_PORT/CTOX_EMBEDDING_*. The existing test save_runtime_state_projection_preserves_non_runtime_keys (runtime_env.rs:497-539) explicitly asserts `!persisted.contains_key("CTOX_ENGINE_MODEL")` — i.e. a stale key MUST disappear. A pure upsert-without-delete leaves that key behind and breaks that assertion. Corrected fix: per-key DIFF reconcile inside `BEGIN IMMEDIATE` — within the txn, SELECT the current key-set, upsert every provided key via INSERT...ON CONFLICT(env_key) DO UPDATE SET env_value=excluded.env_value, and DELETE only keys present in the prior on-disk row-set but absent from the caller's new map. This preserves stale-key removal AND stops clobbering keys a concurrent writer added (a key not in the prior on-disk snapshot is never deleted). Use BEGIN IMMEDIATE (not the current DEFERRED transaction()) so the read-for-diff takes the write lock up front and the diff is computed against the locked state, closing the read-then-write window busy_timeout alone leaves open. New invariant test as proposed: two concurrent save_runtime_env_map calls each adding a different key must end with BOTH present; ADD a second test that the projection path still removes a stale runtime-state key after a config switch (guard against the naive skip-DELETE fix). Impact medium / effort S stand.
- **Grounding caveat:** Verified all anchors. runtime_env.rs:202 does `DELETE FROM runtime_env_kv` then reinserts the full filtered in-memory map (204-213) inside one plain (DEFERRED) transaction (199-201). All public mutators are read-modify-write of the FULL map: persist_runtime_turn_timeout (main.rs:1964-1979), persist_setup_wizard_state (tui/mod.rs:1912-1914), working_hours (131/141), plus dozens more (service.rs, channels.rs, supervisor.rs, business_os/store.rs) against the same runtime/ctox-runtime.sqlite3 with independent Connections from distinct processes/threads (TUI, service daemon, ad-hoc CLI). busy_timeout (227) only serializes the two write txns; it cannot prevent the logical lost update because both readers snapshot before either writes, and the wholesale DELETE+reinsert means writer B's commit erases the key writer A just added. The race is reachable (e.g. `ctox work-hours set` or `ctox --timeout` run while the service daemon is live). The strategy.rs:368-389 test helper explicitly avoids save_runtime_env_map and uses per-key ON CONFLICT(env_key) DO UPDATE, corroborating both the hazard and the proposed safe pattern. persistence.rs::store_text_value (110-120) exists as the cited safe per-key upsert model.


### `egress-idempotency` · `EGRESS-4` — SendFailed->DeliveryRepair->Sending is a declared-but-dead retry path; send_failed rows silently stall with no bounded re-attempt

🏷 Pass 2 · impact **medium** · effort **M** · kind **dead-code** · verifier **keep**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** ✅ **DO — real stability win** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **clear** — Every anchor and behavioral claim is verified in live code (only minor line drift: send_failed transition emitter is at 5613 as cited, loop at 8949 vs cited 8899). The catalog promises a SendFailed->DeliveryRepair->Sending recovery loop ...

- [x] **shipped**
- **Anchors:** `src/core/service/core_state_machine.rs::allowed_transition_catalog (1162-1163 SendFailed->DeliveryRepair, DeliveryRepair->Sending)`, `src/core/mission/channels.rs::mark_outbound_send_failed (4396-4412)`, `src/core/mission/channels.rs::emit_reviewed_founder_send_failed_transition (5613)`
- **Problem:** The FounderCommunication catalog declares a delivery-repair retry loop SendFailed->DeliveryRepair->Sending (core_state_machine.rs:1162-1163), but grep over all of src/core finds zero emitters of either edge and no DeliveryRepair driver. A provider failure sets the row to send_failed (mark_outbound_send_failed) and emits Sending->SendFailed, then nothing ever re-attempts it: no loop scans send_failed rows, and SendFailed is not a terminal state (terminals are Done/Escalated, core_state_machine.rs:1246). The founder mail is neither delivered, terminally failed, nor retried - a silent stall that Pass-1's 'partial/failed delivery -> durable typed outcome and bounded retry, or a silent stall' probe targets. This is the catalog promising a recovery path that does not exist.
- **Fix:** Either (a) implement a bounded DeliveryRepair re-attempt that re-enters Sending through the SAME entity and the SAME enforce_reviewed_founder_send_core_transition path (with an attempt budget), or (b) if no driver is intended near-term, the catalog edges are a smell that misleads liveness/process-mining - flag and either wire a minimal repair tick or document the stall as the intended manual-recovery contract. Implementing (a) reuses the existing send path; it does NOT add a second runner because it re-enters the existing serial send through the existing transition functions.
- **Change sketch:** Add a bounded repair step in the existing mission/service tick that selects FounderCommunication entities in SendFailed past a cooldown, emits SendFailed->DeliveryRepair then DeliveryRepair->Sending with an attempt counter in metadata, and re-invokes send_reviewed_founder_outbound_request for the same approval_key (still unconsumed because mark_founder_reply_review_sent only runs on success). Cap attempts; on budget exhaustion drive to Escalated (a real terminal).
- **Prüfsatz:** (1) hardens mark_outbound_send_failed + the FounderCommunication lifecycle; (2) the repair tick is invoked from the existing service loop, route_external_messages stays the dispatch hot path; (3) reuses the same entity/approval, no new work item; (4) every retry status change flows through enforce_core_transition; (5) no new spawn; (6) rework bound to the same FounderCommunication entity_id; (7) selection by hard state (status=send_failed) + deterministic cooldown/budget, no semantic matching; (8) skills unaffected; (9) attempt counter + DeliveryRepair transitions are the audit evidence; (10) test: a send_failed entity past cooldown re-enters Sending exactly once per attempt and reaches Escalated at budget exhaustion.
- **Risk:** Medium; a retry loop must be strictly attempt-bounded and idempotent (depends on EGRESS-2's dedup) or it could re-send a message that actually went through. Must escalate to a real terminal (Escalated) so it cannot loop forever.
- **Verifier guidance:** Solid, well-grounded dead-code + silent-stall finding. Verified: the catalog promises a recovery loop with zero emitters; on send failure the entity stalls at the non-terminal SendFailed with no bounded re-attempt and no terminal coercion; the approval stays unconsumed (mark_founder_reply_review_sent is bypassed by the Err short-circuit), and the re-send idempotency guard (existing_durable_outbound_send_result, channels.rs:4350) already exists to make a bounded retry safe. The fix lands in the EXISTING serial start_mission_maintenance_loop (service.rs:8899), so it is hardening, not a new runner. Two presentation tweaks for the author: (1) the changeSketch/opportunity word 'repair tick' should be reworded as 'extend start_mission_maintenance_loop with a bounded send_failed repair step' so it cannot be misread as a new scheduler beside the router; (2) explicitly state the re-send safety depends on EGRESS-2's dedup which is already implemented at channels.rs:4350-4365 (folder_hint='sent' + pendingSend=false), so the dependency is satisfied rather than open. Option (a) is the right action; if the team prefers, option (b) (document the stall as the intended manual-recovery contract AND drop the dead DeliveryRepair edges from the catalog so they stop misleading liveness/process-mining) is an equally valid constraint-compliant resolution.
- **Grounding caveat:** All three anchors verified. core_state_machine.rs:1162-1163 declares SendFailed->DeliveryRepair and DeliveryRepair->Sending. Grep over all of src/core finds ZERO emitters of either edge; the only non-catalog DeliveryRepair refs (process_mining.rs:4814,4831,5220) are a reverse predecessor/event map for liveness rendering, NOT a driver. On adapter failure, send_email_message calls mark_outbound_send_failed (channels.rs:4181/4396 -> status='send_failed') and emit_reviewed_founder_send_failed_transition (4183/5613 -> Sending->SendFailed), then `return Err(err)` (4192) propagates; the `?` at the send call site (5313) means mark_founder_reply_review_sent (5323) never runs, so the approval stays unconsumed. No service-tick scanner re-attempts send_failed rows: the only re-touch is a FRESH explicit reply via the ON CONFLICT WHERE status IN ('draft_pending_send','send_failed') clause (4271), not an automatic retry. SendFailed is non-terminal (terminals Done/Escalated, 1246). The silent stall is real now.


### `egress-idempotency` · `EGRESS-5` — Two divergent copies of the pending-send accepted/failed transition; the live one has no status CAS, the CAS-guarded twin is dead code

🏷 Pass 2 · impact **medium** · effort **S** · kind **dead-code** · verifier **revise**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** ✅ **DO — real stability win** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **clear** — The finding is real and fully grounded: a CAS-guarded, bail-on-zero-rows transition (update_pending_send_to_*) exists but is orphaned to phase1_* tests, while the live send path (mark_outbound_send_*) writes unconditionally WHERE message...

> ⚠️ **Canonical issue:** implement the **Canonical scope** + **Verifier guidance** below. (The stale original Fix/Change-sketch fields were removed in the live re-audit cleanup.)

- [x] **shipped**
- **Canonical scope:** Implement the corrected scope in **Verifier guidance**. Treat the superseded original fix/sketch/test mapping as historical context, not instructions.
- **Canonical verification:** Use the Q10/test instructions in **Verifier guidance**; if they conflict with any superseded original field, Verifier guidance wins.
- **Anchors:** `src/core/mission/channels.rs::mark_outbound_send_accepted (4367-4394 - LIVE, no CAS)`, `src/core/mission/channels.rs::mark_outbound_send_failed (4396-4412 - LIVE, no CAS)`, `src/core/mission/channels.rs::update_pending_send_to_accepted (5491-5529 - CAS-guarded, tests only)`, `src/core/mission/channels.rs::update_pending_send_to_failed (5534-5575 - CAS-guarded, tests only)`
- **Problem:** There are two copies of the draft_pending_send->terminal transition. The live send path (send_email_message:4181,4199) calls mark_outbound_send_accepted/mark_outbound_send_failed, which UPDATE unconditionally WHERE message_key=?1 with no guard on the prior status and write the adapter's raw status string. A second, safer pair update_pending_send_to_accepted/update_pending_send_to_failed exists with a CAS (WHERE status='draft_pending_send') that bails if the row already moved, plus normalized status='accepted' - but grep confirms its only callers are the phase1_* tests at channels.rs:11339+, i.e. it is dead on the production path. So the harder-to-get-wrong version was written, tested, then orphaned, while the live version can blindly overwrite a row a concurrent failure/accept already transitioned (no in-process lock on the send_reviewed_email_communication_request branch).
- **Risk:** Low; the guarded path is already test-covered. Care needed only to preserve the existing 'set status to the adapter-returned string' vs 'normalize to accepted' semantics - reconcile deliberately (the durable-artifact queries at channels.rs:4689/4732 key off both 'accepted' and 'sent', so normalization choice must keep those COUNT queries matching).
- **Verifier guidance:** REAL but the proposed fix direction is wrong and not behavior-preserving as written. The two pairs are NOT equivalent duplicates: (a) the live mark_outbound_send_accepted sets folder_hint='sent' and writes the adapter's RAW status string (e.g. 'queued', 'queued_in_mailserver', 'accepted'); (b) the dead update_pending_send_to_accepted does NOT set folder_hint and HARDCODES status='accepted'. The durable-artifact witness reviewed_send_result_has_durable_outbound_artifact (4724-4738) REQUIRES folder_hint='sent' AND status NOT IN (draft_pending_send,...). Routing the live path through the dead twin (the changeSketch) would leave folder_hint unset and REGRESS that witness to false, and would collapse the queued/accepted distinction that the COUNT query at 4689 (status IN 'accepted','sent','queued','queued_in_mailserver','queued_for_provider') and test phase1...:11455-11475 (which asserts a 'queued' row is a durable artifact) depend on. Metadata key casing differs too (live: $.pendingSend/$.adapterResult camelCase; dead: pending_send/adapter_result snake_case) but readers at 4147-4157/4342-4344/4361/4734 tolerate both via or_else fallbacks, so casing alone is non-breaking.

CORRECTED FIX (inverse of the sketch): keep the LIVE functions as the one transition — add the CAS clause `AND status = 'draft_pending_send'` to both UPDATEs (4384, 4407) and the bail-on-zero-rows error, preserving folder_hint='sent' and the raw-adapter-status semantics — then DELETE the dead update_pending_send_to_* twins (and re-point the phase1_* tests at the now-guarded live functions, since deleting the twins orphans those tests). Equivalently, before swapping, extend the dead twins to also set folder_hint and stop hardcoding 'accepted' — but at that point it is a rewrite-and-rename, so just CAS-guard the live ones. Additionally (separate from the CAS): the send_reviewed_email_communication_request branch (5380) should acquire acquire_reviewed_founder_send_lock like its two siblings, since it is the unlocked outlier; the CAS makes the overwrite safe even without the lock, but the missing lock is the actual concurrency vector the finding correctly identified. Net invariant to test: a second accept/fail call on a row already moved out of draft_pending_send must error, and the witness/COUNT queries (4689, 4731) must still match after the live transition.
- **Grounding caveat:** All four anchors verified exact. mark_outbound_send_accepted (4367-4394) and mark_outbound_send_failed (4396-4412) are the LIVE pair: both UPDATE unconditionally WHERE message_key=?1 with no status guard; called from send_email_message at 4181/4199. update_pending_send_to_accepted (5491-5529) and update_pending_send_to_failed (5534-5575) carry the CAS (WHERE status='draft_pending_send') and bail-on-zero-rows; grep confirms their only callers are phase1_* tests (11339, 11378, 11413, 11493). Race is real and grounded: the reviewed-communication branch send_reviewed_email_communication_request (5380) calls send_email_message at 5394 WITHOUT acquiring REVIEWED_FOUNDER_SEND_LOCK, unlike send_reviewed_founder_reply (5232) and send_reviewed_founder_outbound_request (5299) which both lock; the plain branch at 3333 is also unlocked. So a concurrent accept/failure can blindly overwrite with no CAS and no in-process lock — exactly as claimed.

🏷 Pass 1 · impact **medium** · effort **M** · verifier **revise**/high-conf

Two governance mechanisms are advertised in the rendered prompt block (advisory + safety both pass the mechanism_class filter at governance.rs:421-426) yet neither ever emits: evaluate_loop_govern...

> ⚠️ **Canonical issue:** implement the **Canonical scope** + **Verifier guidance** below. (The stale original Fix/Change-sketch fields were removed in the live re-audit cleanup.)

- [x] **shipped**
- **Canonical scope:** Implement the corrected scope in **Verifier guidance**. Treat the superseded original fix/sketch/test mapping as historical context, not instructions.

- **Anchors:** `src/core/service/governance.rs::DEFAULT_MECHANISMS`, `src/core/service/mission_governor.rs::evaluate_loop_governor`, `src/core/context/lcm.rs::increment_mission_rewrite_failure_count`
- **Problem:** governance.rs registers 'mission_loop_governor' (governance.rs:179) and 'review_rewrite_threshold' (governance.rs:267) as advisory/safety mechanisms shown in the prompt block, but neither is ever emitted. evaluate_loop_governor (mission_governor.rs:16) — the entire repeated-blocker forced-repair/replan governor with its own tests — is never called from service.rs (only re-exported in main.rs:48). - **Verifier guidance:** Real and well-grounded: two registered governance mechanisms that the prompt block advertises as armed/advisory-with-authoritative-events never emit (evaluate_loop_governor uncalled; rewrite_failure_count permanently zero). But the proposal is too broad on its second half. TIGHTEN to:

(1) KEEP and wire the loop-governor half. In the per-turn failure path (service.rs ~3487, right after latest_runtime_error binds and context_health at 3490), call evaluate_loop_governor(goal, mission, health, latest_result, latest_runtime_error.as_deref()). On should_enqueue_repair: emit governance::record_event(mechanism_id="mission_loop_governor", ...) using the SAME idempotence pattern already at 3451-3472, and feed repair_prompt back through the existing requeue_runtime_failed_self_work / review_requeue path on the same ticket_self_work_id.
