Reuse the existing idempotence_key mechanism; do not invent a new state column.

(2) DROP or radically re-scope the review_rewrite_threshold half. Review-loop convergence is ALREADY terminally bounded by queue_review_budget_attempt_count -> enforce_queue_review_budget_exhausted_terminal_transition (service.rs:8100-8166, terminalizes to CoreState::Failed with audit proof) and the founder-rework circuit-breaker (11042-11066). Adding a second increment-based bound on the same review_rework loop risks a redundant/competing terminal gate. If review_rewrite_threshold is to be activated at all, scope it to ONLY drive the rewrite_failure_count column + emit the advisory event WITHOUT a second terminalization (let the existing budget gate own the terminal Fail transition), or otherwise propose retiring/merging the review_rewrite_threshold mechanism row instead of wiring a parallel counter. Otherwise the finding's claim that rewrite-class review is "bounded only indirectly by agent_failure_count" is inaccurate and the wiring is partly duplicative.

Net: the genuinely dead, genuinely unduplicated gap is the main-loop repeated-blocker governor — wire that; treat the rewrite counter as a separate, smaller, audit-only activation or a mechanism-row cleanup, not a new convergence bound.
- **Grounding caveat:** All anchors verified live. governance.rs:179 (mission_loop_governor, class=advisory) and governance.rs:267 (review_rewrite_threshold, class=safety) both exist and BOTH reach the rendered prompt block: render_prompt_block (governance.rs:417) counts mechanisms by mechanism_class (survival/safety/advisory), not by prompt_visibility, so advisory→advice_only (line 453) and safety→automatic_actions (line 447), and the prompt states "their recorded events below are authoritative." evaluate_loop_governor (mission_governor.rs:16) exists with its own passing tests (lines 221-249) and is called NOWHERE in production — grep shows only its definition, its test module, and a re-export at main.rs:48. increment_/reset_mission_rewrite_failure_count (lcm.rs:1868/1880) have ZERO production callers; rewrite_failure_count is read for display only (channels.rs:941, as rewrite_iteration_count) and is therefore permanently zero. Neither "mission_loop_governor" nor "review_rewrite_threshold" is ever passed to governance::record_event. Insertion points are accurate: the per-turn failure block (service.rs:3437-3486) has agent_failure_count, with latest_runtime_error available at 3487 and context_health at 3490; review_rework branch at 4085/4165; requeue_runtime_failed_self_work (13324) is a same-work transition (no new spawn). Dead-mechanism claim holds.


### `governance-recovery` · `govrec-4` — Inner JOIN silently drops governance events from unregistered mechanisms (plan_routing_repair, channel_router_core_guard)

🏷 Pass 1 · impact **medium** · effort **S** · verifier **keep**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** ✅ **DO — real stability win** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **clear** — Every load-bearing claim is independently confirmed in live code, including the self-attested "Grounding caveat" details. Two recovery/keepalive mechanisms (plan_routing_repair, channel_router_core_guard) are emitted via governance::reco...

- [x] **shipped**
- **Anchors:** `src/core/service/governance.rs::list_recent_events_from_conn`, `src/core/service/service.rs::run_plan_routing_repair`, `src/core/service/governance.rs::DEFAULT_MECHANISMS`
- **Problem:** list_recent_events_from_conn (governance.rs:665) reads events with `FROM governance_events e JOIN governance_mechanisms m ON m.mechanism_id = e.mechanism_id` (inner join). Two recovery mechanisms are emitted by production code but are NOT in DEFAULT_MECHANISMS: 'plan_routing_repair' (service.rs:1381, the boot+cycle stale-plan-route repair) and 'channel_router_core_guard' (service.rs:9435, the router-keepalive guard-skip). Their rows are written to governance_events but the inner join filters them out of every prompt snapshot and TUI governance view (governance.rs:682). record_event has no FK either, so the writes succeed and then become permanently invisible — a silent observability hole precisely on two recovery/keepalive paths.
- **Fix:** Register the two emitted mechanisms in DEFAULT_MECHANISMS so the existing join surfaces them, and harden the contract so an emit of an unregistered mechanism cannot silently vanish.
- **Change sketch:** Add two DefaultMechanism entries ('plan_routing_repair' class 'recovery', 'channel_router_core_guard' class 'survival') to DEFAULT_MECHANISMS (governance.rs:89). Then add a debug_assert / test that every literal mechanism_id passed to governance::record_event across the crate is present in DEFAULT_MECHANISMS (a grep-driven unit test over the constant list), so future emitters cannot orphan themselves. Optionally switch list_recent_events_from_conn to LEFT JOIN with a COALESCE'd class so even an unregistered event is at least visible.
- **Prüfsatz:** Q1 hardens list_recent_events_from_conn + the DEFAULT_MECHANISMS registry contract; Q9 restores Audit/Process-Mining visibility for the two recovery paths; Q10 a test enumerating emitted mechanism_ids vs registered ids pins the invariant (no orphan events). No new mechanism behavior — only registration + a coverage test.
- **Risk:** Very low. Adding registry rows is idempotent (upsert). The coverage test is static. LEFT JOIN change, if taken, must keep mechanism_class non-null in render filters (render_prompt_block, governance.rs:421).
- **Verifier guidance:** Keep as-is; two implementation cautions for the executor. (a) The DefaultMechanism struct (governance.rs:80-87) requires ALL six fields — mechanism_id, mechanism_class, autonomy, prompt_visibility, module_hint, description — the changeSketch only names class, so the other four must be filled (e.g. autonomy "autonomous_plan_routing_repair"/"autonomous_router_keepalive_guard_skip", prompt_visibility "inventory_only" or "prompt_visible", module_hint "src/service/service.rs"). (b) Class choice does NOT affect whether the EVENTS surface — events appear as soon as a governance_mechanisms row exists for the id, because the inner join only needs the row. Class only affects render_prompt_block's mechanism counters (421-437), which list survival/safety/advisory. So "recovery" (matching the existing ticket_adapter_sync/ticket_reconciliation recovery mechanisms) is correct for plan_routing_repair and keeps it out of the per-turn automatic_actions count while still surfacing its events — exactly the goal. The optional LEFT JOIN is a genuine belt-and-suspenders improvement but secondary; if taken, COALESCE the class to a non-null sentinel (e.g. 'unregistered') so render filters and the survival/safety/advisory match in render_prompt_block stay total. Primary deliverable is the registry rows + the static coverage test asserting every literal mechanism_id passed to governance::record_event in the crate is in DEFAULT_MECHANISMS.
- **Grounding caveat:** All anchors verified against current code. (1) list_recent_events_from_conn at governance.rs:665 uses inner `JOIN governance_mechanisms m ON m.mechanism_id = e.mechanism_id` (line 682); load_event_by_id (717) has the same join. (2) run_plan_routing_repair (service.rs:1368) emits mechanism_id "plan_routing_repair" via governance::record_event (line 1381), called at boot (801) and per-turn (1115). (3) channel_router_core_guard emitted at service.rs:9435. (4) Neither id appears anywhere in governance.rs (grep exit 1) — confirmed absent from DEFAULT_MECHANISMS (89-290) and from mechanism_inventory() which is just `.map` over the constant (489-492). (5) governance_events schema (governance.rs:586) declares `mechanism_id TEXT NOT NULL` with NO foreign key, so record_event's INSERT OR IGNORE (342) succeeds for unregistered ids, then the inner join drops them. (6) The snapshot feeds the live agent prompt (turn_loop.rs:482/605 via render_prompt_block) and lcm.rs:7089 and the CLI `ctox governance events/snapshot`. conversation_id math holds: plan_routing_repair uses Some(CHAT_CONVERSATION_ID=1) and the chat snapshot queries id=1 (WHERE conversation_id IS NULL OR = ?1); channel_router uses None which always matches — so registration alone genuinely restores visibility for both. The silent-observability-hole claim is true.


### `internal-work-workflow` · `workflow-3` — workflow-delta update_steps can rewrite predecessors/workflow_id on the gating path

🏷 Pass 1 · impact **medium** · effort **S** · verifier **keep**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** ✅ **DO — real stability win** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **clear** — Every anchor, line number, symbol, struct field, and the full control-flow chain match the live code verbatim — exceptionally well-researched ticket, not a hallucination. The vulnerability is real: a model/reducer-authored workflow delta...

- [ ] **open**
- **Anchors:** `src/core/mission/tickets.rs:3560`, `src/core/mission/tickets.rs::apply_ticket_workflow_delta`, `src/core/mission/tickets.rs::workflow_step_ready_internal`
- **Problem:** In the update loop, `update.metadata` is copied verbatim into the row: `for (key,value) in extra { object.insert(key.clone(), value.clone()); }` (tickets.rs:3560-3563), then merged by `merge_ticket_self_work_metadata`. There is no allowlist, so a delta update can overwrite `workflow_predecessor_step_ids`/`workflow_predecessor_work_ids` (clearing a step's predecessors) or even `workflow_id` and `workflow_step_id` — the very keys `workflow_step_ready_internal` (3936) reads to gate materialization. A reducer can thus silently delete the gating edges of a waiting step and make it ready, with no spawn-guard or state-machine involvement.
- **Fix:** Constrain the free-form `update.metadata` passthrough so structural gating keys cannot be mutated through the delta update channel; structural changes must go through `put_ticket_workflow_step` (which sets predecessors deliberately and re-runs the spawn guard).
- **Change sketch:** In the `update.metadata` copy loop (3560), skip a small denylist of protected keys: `workflow_id`, `workflow_step_id`, `workflow_role`, `workflow_predecessor_work_ids`, `workflow_predecessor_step_ids`, `parent_work_id`, `dedupe_key`. Reducer-driven re-shaping of dependencies already has a path: create a new step via `create_steps`. No new mechanism.
- **Prüfsatz:** Q1 hardens `apply_ticket_workflow_delta` metadata merge. Q3/Q4/Q5 unchanged. Q7 protects the hard keys (`workflow_step_id`, predecessor ids, `dedupe_key`) the doc lists as identity belege. Q9 audited via existing `self_work_metadata_updated` row. Q10 add a test: a delta update attempting to clear `workflow_predecessor_step_ids` leaves the persisted predecessors intact and the step stays waiting.
- **Risk:** Very low; the protected keys are never meant to be edited via update. Confirm no current caller legitimately rewrites them (none found in tree).
- **Verifier guidance:** Denylist is precise: the gating reads only the _ids variants (workflow_predecessor_work_ids/_step_ids at 4050-4054), not the non-_ids workflow_predecessor_steps which is read-side-only (service.rs:10315) — so the proposed set {workflow_id, workflow_step_id, workflow_role, workflow_predecessor_work_ids, workflow_predecessor_step_ids, parent_work_id, dedupe_key} matches exactly the keys put_ticket_workflow_step stamps deliberately (3444-3461) and is not over-broad. Intentionally-mutable keys (workflow_phase, source_label, workflow_step_status) stay mutable — correct, since workflow_step_status has its own dedicated first-class update field (WorkflowDeltaUpdateStep.workflow_step_status, 635-636) so denying it in the passthrough loses nothing. Minor implementation note for the author: apply the skip in the 3560-3563 loop (drop protected keys before insert) AND optionally record skipped keys in the audit details so a reducer attempting a blocked structural rewrite is observable, not silently dropped.
- **Grounding caveat:** Re-opened all anchors. apply_ticket_workflow_delta at tickets.rs:3523; the verbatim copy loop is exactly at 3560-3563 (`for (key,value) in extra { object.insert(key.clone(), value.clone()); }`), fed by WorkflowDeltaUpdateStep.metadata which is a free-form serde Value (struct at 630-643, field 642). That metadata_update flows into merge_ticket_self_work_metadata (3968) -> merge_json_object_values (4011-4018), a blind key-by-key overwrite of persisted metadata with no allowlist/denylist. The gate workflow_step_ready_internal (3936) reads exactly workflow_predecessor_work_ids (3940), workflow_predecessor_step_ids (3949) and workflow_id (3948/3964) off that same metadata; these keys are the ones put_ticket_workflow_step deliberately stamps (3444-3461). materialize_ready_workflow_steps_for_workflow (3658) sweeps candidates, calls workflow_step_ready_internal off persisted metadata (3686) and marks them queue-ready (3699). So a model-authored delta (delta arrives raw via --delta-json at 1177-1180, produced by the reducer's workflow_delta_candidate) can clear a waiting step's predecessor edges and make it materialize with no predecessor re-check, spawn-guard, or state-machine step. Claim holds verbatim.


### `internal-work-workflow` · `workflow-4` — Steps can be created and queued against a closed/cancelled/superseded workflow case

🏷 Pass 1 · impact **medium** · effort **S** · verifier **keep**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** ✅ **DO — real stability win** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **clear** — Every anchor is accurate (line numbers exact except service.rs drifted 9046->9134, within tolerance). The defect is real and demonstrable: put_ticket_workflow_step (3408) loads the case but never inspects case.state/workflow_status; appl...

- [ ] **open**
- **Anchors:** `src/core/mission/tickets.rs::put_ticket_workflow_step`, `src/core/mission/tickets.rs::load_ticket_workflow_case_internal`, `src/core/mission/tickets.rs::apply_ticket_workflow_delta`
- **Problem:** `put_ticket_workflow_step` (3403) loads the case via `load_ticket_workflow_case_internal` (3849) only to read `source_system`/`thread_key`/`priority` — it never checks the case `state` or `workflow_status`. `apply_ticket_workflow_delta` (3523) likewise never re-validates the case is active. So after a workflow case is closed/cancelled/superseded, a stray delta or `workflow-step-put` (CLI 1142) can still spawn new `workflow-step` items and `materialize_ready_workflow_steps` (service.rs:9046) will route them into the worker — work continues on a terminated case. `workflow_prompt_block` already excludes terminal cases (tickets.rs:3711), so this is an inconsistency the create path doesn't honor.
- **Fix:** Gate new step creation and delta application on the case being non-terminal, reusing the same terminal-state set already used in `workflow_prompt_block`'s SQL filter — a guard riding the existing case lookup, not a new lifecycle.
- **Change sketch:** In `put_ticket_workflow_step` after loading `case` (3408): if `workflow_step_satisfied(&case)`-style terminal check (or the `closed|done|completed|handled|cancelled|superseded|failed` set already inlined at 3711) matches `case.state` or `case.metadata.workflow_status`, `anyhow::bail!`. `apply_ticket_workflow_delta` inherits the guard through `put_ticket_workflow_step`; add the same check before its update loop for status-only deltas.
- **Prüfsatz:** Q1 hardens `put_ticket_workflow_step`/`apply_ticket_workflow_delta` against the case row. Q3 work stays Internal Work. Q4 prevents materialization that would otherwise drive guarded transitions on a dead case. Q5 unchanged. Q6 keeps rework on a live main item. Q9 reuses the existing terminal-state set; audited via the bail. Q10 test: closing the case, then a delta create, is rejected and materializes nothing.
- **Risk:** Low; must allow legitimate reopen flows if any exist (none found). Keep the terminal set identical to the 3711 filter to avoid drift.
- **Verifier guidance:** Real, uncovered, compliant — keep. One tightening for the changeSketch: do NOT key the guard on workflow_step_satisfied(&case). That helper (tickets.rs:4019) keys on workflow_step_status (a step metadata key) plus a narrower verified/passed/satisfied set; a CASE instead carries metadata.workflow_status (set to "active" at 3334, NOT workflow_step_status) and the row state. Using workflow_step_satisfied would silently never match the case's status field and would drift from the case terminal vocabulary. Instead gate on the exact set from the 3711 SQL filter applied to case.state: normalize_token(&case.state) in {closed, done, completed, handled, cancelled, superseded, failed} OR normalize_token(metadata workflow_status) in that set -> anyhow::bail!. Put the check in put_ticket_workflow_step right after the case load at 3409 (this single point covers the CLI put, the create_steps loop in apply_ticket_workflow_delta via 3600, and case-creation's first_step at 3377 which is harmless since a fresh case is "open"). For status-only deltas (update_steps with no create_steps), also load the case once at the top of apply_ticket_workflow_delta and bail before the update loop, so a closed case cannot be driven by metadata flips either. Keep the terminal set as a shared const to avoid drift from the 3711 filter. Test: create workflow, transition the case row to "closed", then (a) workflow-step-put and (b) a delta create_steps both bail, and materialize_ready_workflow_steps returns materialized_count 0.
- **Grounding caveat:** Verified all anchors. put_ticket_workflow_step (tickets.rs:3403) loads the case at 3408 but only reads source_system (3512), metadata priority/thread_key/workspace_root, and case.work_id (3457); it never inspects case.state or case.metadata.workflow_status. apply_ticket_workflow_delta (3523) creates steps via put_ticket_workflow_step (3600) without re-validating the case. The materialization path materialize_ready_workflow_steps_for_workflow (3658) + workflow_step_ready_internal (3936) checks only the step's own runnable-state and step predecessors, never the parent case; service.rs:9046 routes materialized steps into the worker. CLI workflow-step-put (1125/1142) and delta (1181) both reach the create path. workflow_prompt_block SQL (3711) DOES exclude terminal cases (closed|done|completed|handled|cancelled|superseded|failed), confirming the create-path inconsistency. The case is a ticket_self_work_item whose state can reach those terminal values via transition_ticket_self_work_item (3174).


### `internal-work-workflow` · `workflow-5` — Dangling predecessor references stall a workflow silently instead of being rejected at create time

🏷 Pass 1 · impact **medium** · effort **M** · verifier **revise**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** ✅ **DO — real stability win** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **clear** — All three anchors and every behavioral claim are verified in live code with only small line drift. A typo'd or not-yet-created predecessor (free strings accepted at split_workflow_predecessor_refs:4093) yields a step that is permanently ...

> ⚠️ **Canonical issue:** implement the **Canonical scope** + **Verifier guidance** below. (The stale original Fix/Change-sketch fields were removed in the live re-audit cleanup.)

- [ ] **open**
- **Canonical scope:** Implement the corrected scope in **Verifier guidance**. Treat the superseded original fix/sketch/test mapping as historical context, not instructions.
- **Canonical verification:** Use the Q10/test instructions in **Verifier guidance**; if they conflict with any superseded original field, Verifier guidance wins.
- **Anchors:** `src/core/mission/tickets.rs::workflow_step_ready_internal`, `src/core/mission/tickets.rs::apply_ticket_workflow_delta`, `src/core/mission/tickets.rs::locate_workflow_step_in_conn`
- **Problem:** `workflow_step_ready_internal` (3936) returns `Ok(false)` when a referenced predecessor work_id (3941) or step_id (3950) cannot be loaded. A `create_steps` entry that lists a typo'd or not-yet-created `predecessor_steps` (delta accepts free strings, split at 4083) produces a step that is permanently WAITING and is never reported as broken — it just never materializes. There is no validation in `apply_ticket_workflow_delta`/`put_ticket_workflow_step` that predecessors resolve within the same workflow, and no surfacing of an unsatisfiable edge to audit/process-mining.
- **Risk:** Medium: must allow a delta that creates predecessor and dependent in the same call (validate against `created_items` accumulated so far, in declaration order, or two-pass). Must not break the legitimate case where a predecessor is a non-step parent work item.
- **Verifier guidance:** Real weakness, in-scope hardening, but the changeSketch is too loose and risks a regression as written. Pin the implementation precisely: (1) Do the validation in apply_ticket_workflow_delta as a TWO-PASS over the batch, NOT solely inside put_ticket_workflow_step. The create loop (3600) persists each step immediately, so a sibling predecessor declared LATER in the create_steps array does not yet exist in the DB when an earlier-declared dependent is created — a per-step DB lookup (the 'accumulated so far, in declaration order' variant the sketch offers) would wrongly reject legitimate forward/any-order intra-delta references. Build the allowed-id set up front = {step_ids already present in this workflow via list_ticket_workflow_steps_internal/locate_workflow_step_in_conn} UNION {every step_id that will be created by this delta — resolving each create's effective step_id the same way put_ticket_workflow_step does, including the phase:digest fallback at 3424-3430 when step_id is omitted}, then bail! on any predecessor_step_id not in that set, before creating anything. (2) For predecessor_work_ids, resolve via load_ticket_self_work_item_raw and require kind==WORKFLOW_STEP_KIND AND same workflow_id — but per the finding's own risk note, do NOT reject a predecessor that is a non-step parent work item if that is a supported pattern; scope the work_id check to in-workflow step refs only, or relax to 'must load' to stay safe. (3) Inside put_ticket_workflow_step itself (CLI single-step path at 1142, which cannot batch) a single-pass locate_workflow_step_in_conn check IS correct and sufficient since any predecessor must pre-exist. (4) Reject self-reference (a step listing its own step_id) here too. (5) Emit an audit record on rejection so process-mining sees the explicit failure (Q9). Q10 tests: (a) delta create referencing a non-existent predecessor step_id is rejected with bail!; (b) delta declaring predecessor and dependent in the SAME create_steps array — in BOTH orders — is accepted and both materialize; (c) existing forward-reference test at 12446 (implement-one-slice -> phase-0-reducer created in a prior call) still passes. Note start_ticket_workflow's first reducer step (3388-3389) has empty predecessors so it is unaffected. Tests must write to the SQLite ticket DB under a temp root, not std::env.
- **Grounding caveat:** All three anchors exist and behave as claimed. `workflow_step_ready_internal` (tickets.rs:3936) returns Ok(false) when a predecessor work_id (3941-3943) or step_id via locate_workflow_step_in_conn (3950-3952) cannot be loaded. `put_ticket_workflow_step` (3403-3521) and the apply_ticket_workflow_delta create loop (3585-3621) write predecessor refs into metadata (3450-3456) with ZERO referential-integrity validation; split_workflow_predecessor_refs (4083) accepts arbitrary free strings (anything not prefixed `self-work:` becomes a step_id). A dangling/typo'd predecessor produces a step that lands silently in waiting_steps (load_ticket_workflow, 3804-3805) indistinguishable from a legitimately-waiting step — no audit, no error, no distinguishing field. Confirmed the silent infinite stall.


### `internal-work-workflow` · `workflow-6` — No workflow-wide step budget; only a 16-per-call cap bounds graph growth

🏷 Pass 1 · impact **medium** · effort **M** · verifier **revise**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** ✅ **DO — real stability win** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **clear** — All anchors and behavioral claims verified against live code (only line numbers drifted). The per-call 16 cap and the per-step-identity spawn budget (64, keyed on unique dedupe_key) are real, and there is genuinely no aggregate per-workf...

> ⚠️ **Canonical issue:** implement the **Canonical scope** + **Verifier guidance** below. (The stale original Fix/Change-sketch fields were removed in the live re-audit cleanup.)

- [ ] **open**
- **Canonical scope:** Implement the corrected scope in **Verifier guidance**. Treat the superseded original fix/sketch/test mapping as historical context, not instructions.
- **Canonical verification:** Use the Q10/test instructions in **Verifier guidance**; if they conflict with any superseded original field, Verifier guidance wins.
- **Anchors:** `src/core/mission/tickets.rs:3531`, `src/core/mission/tickets.rs::ticket_self_work_spawn_budget`, `src/core/mission/tickets.rs::enforce_ticket_self_work_spawn`
- **Problem:** `apply_ticket_workflow_delta` caps `create_steps.len()` at `WORKFLOW_MATERIALIZE_DEFAULT_LIMIT` (16) PER CALL (tickets.rs:3531). The per-step spawn budget from `ticket_self_work_spawn_budget` (2926) keys on the per-step `dedupe_key` (`service-self-work-spawn:{kind}:{key}`, max 64), so it bounds RETRIES of one step identity, not the TOTAL number of distinct steps in a workflow. A reducer that keeps issuing deltas (each <=16) can grow one workflow to an unbounded number of `workflow-step` items, all guarded individually but with no aggregate ceiling per `workflow_id` — a slow runaway the spawn guard cannot see because every edge has a distinct child identity.
- **Risk:** Low-medium: pick a cap that comfortably exceeds real long-task decompositions; make it a typed constant (no env toggle). Counting query is already O(steps) and bounded by LIMIT 512 elsewhere.
- **Verifier guidance:** The weakness and the opportunity are correct and compliant; only the changeSketch's count mechanism needs correcting. It proposes reusing list_ticket_workflow_steps_internal (3857), but that query is LIMIT-bounded — called with 512 at 3791, and the sibling materialize query (3672) also caps at LIMIT 512. A LIMIT-bounded list saturates and cannot enforce a ceiling at or above its limit, and double-counts intent with the runtime row cap. Corrected, tighter version: (1) add a dedicated count helper `SELECT COUNT(*) FROM ticket_self_work_items WHERE kind = 'workflow-step' AND json_extract(metadata_json,'$.workflow_id') = ?1` — the COUNT-on-self-work-items pattern already exists at 4343/4364, no new query shape. (2) Enforce the ceiling in put_ticket_workflow_step (3403), NOT in apply_ticket_workflow_delta: put_ticket_workflow_step is the single choke point through which BOTH the reducer-bootstrap path (3381) and the per-create delta loop (3585-3620) flow, so checking `existing_count + 1 > WORKFLOW_MAX_STEPS_PER_WORKFLOW` there holds the cap regardless of entry point, whereas a delta-only check leaves the bootstrap path and any future caller unguarded. (3) Make the constant a typed value comfortably above real decompositions and distinct from the 512 row cap (e.g. 128 or 256) so the 512-row materialize/list bound stays unrelated. (4) bail! before create (no DB write) and rely on the existing record_audit / record_harness_flow_event_lossy emitted by put_ticket_self_work_item for process-mining visibility; do NOT add a separate failed/blocked item just to record the rejection. (5) Test (Q10): seed a case, drive put_ticket_workflow_step past the cap, assert the (cap+1)th create returns Err and list_ticket_workflow_steps_internal still returns exactly cap rows — written against a tempdir SQLite root, not std::env.
- **Grounding caveat:** All anchors verified against current code. tickets.rs:3531: `if delta.create_steps.len() > WORKFLOW_MATERIALIZE_DEFAULT_LIMIT` (=16, defined at line 64) bails — confirmed PER-CALL only. ticket_self_work_spawn_budget (2926): the fallthrough returns `(format!("service-self-work-spawn:{kind}:{key}"), 64)` at 2944, where `key` = per-step `dedupe_key` (2937). Each workflow step's dedupe_key is unique: `ticket-workflow-step:{workflow_id}:{step_id}` (put_ticket_workflow_step, line 3461). The spawn guard counts budget by exact key match: core_transition_guard.rs accepted_spawn_budget_count (855) does `SELECT COUNT(*) ... WHERE accepted=1 AND budget_key=?1`, compared against max_attempts at 699-701. So the 64-budget bounds RETRIES of ONE step identity, not the count of distinct steps. grep for MAX_WORKFLOW_STEPS / total-step / per-workflow ceiling found nothing — no aggregate cap exists. On budget exhaustion put_ticket_self_work_item (2802-2851) sets the item blocked/failed and bails, but a brand-new distinct step never reaches that branch because its budget_key has zero prior count. apply_ticket_workflow_delta is a CLI command (1173-1187) callable arbitrarily many times by a reducer agent; reducers re-spawn per phase as distinct identities. The unbounded-growth weakness is real.

🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** ✅ **DO — real stability win** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **clear** — Every anchor and behavioral claim verified against live code. channels.rs:6248-6271 and lcm.rs:1051-1071 are exactly the unguarded probe-then-ALTER described; both run via ensure_schema/init_schema on the shared runtime/ctox.sqlite3 (cor...

> ⚠️ **Canonical issue:** implement the **Canonical scope** + **Verifier guidance** below. (The stale original Fix/Change-sketch fields were removed in the live re-audit cleanup.)

- [x] **shipped**
- **Canonical scope:** Implement the corrected scope in **Verifier guidance**. Treat the superseded original fix/sketch/test mapping as historical context, not instructions.
- **Canonical verification:** Use the Q10/test instructions in **Verifier guidance**; if they conflict with any superseded original field, Verifier guidance wins.
- **Anchors:** `channels.rs::ensure_terminal_no_send_column (6248-6271)`, `lcm.rs::ensure_column (1051-1071)`
- **Problem:** With ensure_schema on every open_channel_db across processes, two pass the pragma probe before either ALTERs; the second gets duplicate column name terminal_no_send and open_channel_db fails at first-boot-after-upgrade. lcm.rs::ensure_column identically unguarded.
- **Verifier guidance:** KEEP the finding, tighten the fix to match the existing CTOX idiom rather than the proposed re-probe dance. Corrected fix: instead of 'on Err re-probe then decide', adopt the same shape as src/core/report/schema.rs:184 migrate_add_column — attempt the ALTER and treat a 'duplicate column name' error as success (swallow it); the pre-probe may remain as a fast-path but the error-tolerance is what actually closes the race. Apply to BOTH ensure_terminal_no_send_column (channels.rs:6248) AND lcm.rs::ensure_column (1051), since ensure_column is the more widely-used helper across many tables and carries the same race on the shared runtime DB. Be precise on error matching: match on the SQLite extended/primary code message text 'duplicate column name' (rusqlite Error::SqliteFailure with the message), not a blanket swallow, so unrelated ALTER failures still propagate. Test (deterministic, item 10): open two writer connections to one temp ctox.sqlite3 with the column absent, race the two ensure_* calls (threads or sequential after both probe), assert both return Ok and pragma_table_info shows terminal_no_send exactly once. Anchor path correction for the report: the channels fn lives at src/core/mission/channels.rs, not channels.rs at repo root.
- **Grounding caveat:** Anchors real (anchor path slightly off: it's src/core/mission/channels.rs:6248-6271, finding wrote channels.rs; lines exact). ensure_terminal_no_send_column does pragma_table_info EXISTS probe then ALTER ADD COLUMN terminal_no_send if absent. lcm.rs::ensure_column (1051-1071) is the identical unguarded probe-loop-then-ALTER. ensure_schema runs on every open_channel_db (6068) against the SHARED unified runtime/ctox.sqlite3 (resolve_db_path->paths::core_db, channels.rs:8566 / paths.rs:34), opened by service daemon + CLI + TUI processes. Race is real: two conns both pass probe; first ALTERs and commits; second acquires write lock via busy_timeout but its ALTER hits SQLITE_ERROR 'duplicate column name' (busy_timeout retries only on busy/locked, not this), so open_channel_db returns Err. Window = first-boot-after-upgrade, narrow but nonzero. Strongest corroboration: the SAME codebase already tolerates this exact error — src/core/report/schema.rs:129 comment 'we swallow duplicate column errors' + migrate_add_column (184) does `let _ = conn.execute(sql)`. The two cited sites simply fail to follow that established idiom.


### `process-mining-audit` · `pm-4` — Global event prune deletes transition-evidence by raw seq, with no minimum-retention floor for non-debug events

🏷 Pass 1 · impact **medium** · effort **M** · verifier **revise**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** ✅ **DO — real stability win** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **clear** — The core finding is fully grounded in live code: the global prune deletes by raw shared AUTOINCREMENT seq with no case_id filter, debug bursts advance MAX(event_seq) and can evict genuine transition-evidence rows that are young in wall-c...

> ⚠️ **Canonical issue:** implement the **Canonical scope** + **Verifier guidance** below. (The stale original Fix/Change-sketch fields were removed in the live re-audit cleanup.)

- [x] **shipped**
- **Canonical scope:** Implement the corrected scope in **Verifier guidance**. Treat the superseded original fix/sketch/test mapping as historical context, not instructions.
- **Canonical verification:** Use the Q10/test instructions in **Verifier guidance**; if they conflict with any superseded original field, Verifier guidance wins.
- **Anchors:** `src/core/service/process_mining.rs::prune_process_events_global`, `src/core/service/process_mining.rs::prune_sqlite_access_process_events`, `src/core/service/process_mining.rs::ensure_process_mining_schema`
- **Problem:** prune_process_events_global deletes ALL rows with `event_seq <= MAX-500_000`, blind to case_id. The dedicated prune_sqlite_access_process_events trims debug 'sqlite-access:%' rows to 200_000, but the global prune runs over the combined stream. Because sqlite-access debug rows and real state-transition rows share one AUTOINCREMENT seq, a burst of debug events (or any high-volume table) advances MAX(event_seq) and can age genuine transition-evidence rows past the 500k window even though the meaningful evidence is far younger in wall-clock time. ctox_pm_state_violations and ctox_pm_core_transition_audit reference those event_ids but are not co-pruned and are never pruned at all, leaving dangling references. The Pruefsatz Q9 evidence the repair/conformance path depends on can be evicted by debug noise it was supposed to be insulated from.
- **Risk:** Medium — must ensure the non-debug stream still has an upper bound so the table cannot grow unbounded; the existing span-skip optimization must be re-derived per stream.
- **Verifier guidance:** Finding is real and compliant, but the changeSketch is self-contradictory ("OR add `case_id LIKE 'sqlite-access:%'` is already excluded so instead floor...") and the 'dangling references' impact framing overstates a cosmetic concern. Corrected tighter version: in prune_process_events_global, compute the deletion cutoff from the NON-debug seq stream only, so debug bursts can never advance the eviction frontier for genuine transition evidence, while non-debug MAX still bounds growth. Concretely: `DELETE FROM ctox_process_events WHERE case_id NOT LIKE 'sqlite-access:%' AND event_seq <= (SELECT MAX(event_seq) - ?window FROM ctox_process_events WHERE case_id NOT LIKE 'sqlite-access:%')` — keep the existing span-skip guard but compute span over the non-debug stream too; the sqlite-access stream stays bounded by its own prune (:508). Drop the 'dangling references / co-prune the audit tables' scope from the fix — the audit/violation rows are self-contained once written; the load-bearing harm is pre-scan eviction of recent genuine transition events, which this fix addresses directly. Q10 test (keep as proposed but reframe): insert 600k sqlite-access rows + a handful of genuine (case_id NOT LIKE 'sqlite-access:%') transition rows interleaved so the genuine rows are well within the non-debug window but past MAX-500k overall; assert all genuine rows survive prune_process_events_global while debug rows are bounded. Today that test fails (genuine rows dropped); after the fix it passes. Keep effort M / risk Medium — verify the non-debug stream still has its own upper bound (it does, via its own MAX advancing) so the table cannot grow unbounded.
- **Grounding caveat:** Re-opened all three anchors. process_mining.rs:525-550 prune_process_events_global DELETEs `event_seq <= MAX(event_seq) - 500000` with ZERO case_id filter (verified: grep found 0 case_id refs in the body) — blind to source. Schema at :166-190 confirms event_seq is a single shared `INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT` across all case_ids, so sqlite-access debug rows (case_id 'sqlite-access:%', emitted up to 512/command per :56) and genuine transition rows share one seq space. prune_sqlite_access_process_events (:508-523) only trims debug rows by their own 200k window; it does not stop MAX(event_seq) from climbing, so the global prune frontier is driven by total volume regardless of what is debug noise. ctox_pm_state_violations.event_id (:212) and ctox_pm_core_transition_audit.event_id (:223) reference events; the only DELETEs on those tables (:4399-4413) are per-event idempotent re-scan cleanups keyed by a specific event_id, NOT a retention prune — so there is genuinely no co-prune. load_state_machine_events (:4742-4776) derives audit/coverage from events still present (ORDER BY event_seq DESC LIMIT), so a genuine transition event evicted by the seq-window prune before a scan derives it loses its Q9 evidence permanently. No direct test for prune_process_events_global exists (only sqlite_access_prune_keeps_recent_debug_window at :5795 tests the per-source prune). The weakness is real. Minor imprecision in the finding: once an audit/violation row IS written it is self-contained, so the literal 'dangling references' are cosmetic; the load-bearing harm is the pre-scan eviction of young transition evidence.


### `spawn-liveness-subagents` · `liveness-3` — Interrupted child is non-terminal: completion watcher and agent-job loop can hang until the 30-min reaper

🏷 Pass 1 · impact **medium** · effort **S** · verifier **revise**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** ✅ **DO — real stability win** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **clear** — Genuine, well-grounded bounded liveness hole. is_final excludes Interrupted, and three is_final-gated collection/finalize sites (find_finished_threads:903, reconciliation finalize-vs-track:868, and serialized wait_for_final_status:402) l...

> ⚠️ **Canonical issue:** implement the **Canonical scope** + **Verifier guidance** below. (The stale original Fix/Change-sketch fields were removed in the live re-audit cleanup.)

- [x] **shipped**
- **Canonical scope:** Implement the corrected scope in **Verifier guidance**. Treat the superseded original fix/sketch/test mapping as historical context, not instructions.
- **Canonical verification:** Use the Q10/test instructions in **Verifier guidance**; if they conflict with any superseded original field, Verifier guidance wins.
- **Anchors:** `src/core/harness/core/src/agent/status.rs:20 (is_final)`, `src/core/harness/core/src/agent/control.rs:621 (maybe_start_completion_watcher)`, `src/core/harness/core/src/tools/handlers/agent_jobs.rs:896 (find_finished_threads)`, `src/core/harness/core/src/tools/handlers/agent_jobs.rs:940 (reap_stale_active_items)`
- **Problem:** is_final (status.rs:20) returns false for AgentStatus::Interrupted. The completion watcher loop (control.rs:636-650) only injects the parent notification when is_final, so an interrupted thread-spawn child NEVER notifies its parent — the parent waits indefinitely with no completion edge, only later observing via list_agents. In the agent-job loop, an interrupted worker is likewise never collected by find_finished_threads (agent_jobs.rs:903), so its item stays Running and its slot stays occupied until reap_stale_active_items fires at job_runtime_timeout (default DEFAULT_AGENT_JOB_ITEM_TIMEOUT = 30 min, agent_jobs.rs:46). Bounded, but a 30-minute stall on an interrupted worker is a liveness hole for a 'better harness'.
- **Risk:** Interrupted can be a transient state if the harness re-runs a turn; treating it as terminal-for-collection in the agent-job loop must coexist with the lease check in report_agent_job_item_result (assigned_thread_id match) so a late report from a re-running interrupted worker is still correctly rejected rather than double-counted.
- **Verifier guidance:** Real bounded liveness hole, but the changeSketch is wrong in one branch and must stay split by consumer.

(1) WATCHER BRANCH IS UNSAFE AS WRITTEN. Interrupted is genuinely transient: it is produced by abort_all_tasks(TurnAbortReason::Interrupted) (codex.rs:3973/5064) and a subsequent TurnStarted flips status back to Running (status.rs:8). ThreadSpawn children CAN be re-driven after interrupt — send_input (control.rs:350), resume_agent, and the send_input_interrupts_before_prompt test (multi_agents_tests.rs:706) all exist. The completion watcher (control.rs:621) does NOT shut the child down before notifying the parent, so treating Interrupted as terminal there would inject a premature 'child finished (interrupted)' parent notification and then the child could keep running on a resume — a spurious/duplicate edge, not a fix. Do NOT apply is_subagent_terminal to the watcher unless the watcher also shuts the child down (shutdown_agent) at the same instant, making Interrupted actually terminal. Safer minimal correction: leave the watcher gated on is_final and instead give the watcher a bounded fallback wake (it currently relies only on the watch-channel error at 638-640).

(2) AGENT-JOB BRANCH IS SAFE BUT THE SCOPE MISSES TWO MORE CONSUMERS. In the job loop the terminal-for-collection treatment is safe because finalize_finished_item (agent_jobs.rs:970) calls shutdown_agent (996-1000), removing the thread+slot, and the lease in report_agent_job_item_result rejects any late report from a resumed worker. Good. BUT the SAME is_final-gated subagent hang exists in two consumers the finding omits: wait_for_final_status (control.rs:402, used by the serialized-subagent dispatch at 393) and the restart/reconciliation finalize-vs-track decision at agent_jobs.rs:868. A predicate that fixes only find_finished_threads (903) leaves the serialized-subagent path and the recovery path with the identical 30-min hole.

Tighter corrected version: introduce is_subagent_terminal(status) = is_final(status) || Interrupted, and apply it ONLY at collection/finalize sites that also shut the thread down, namely find_finished_threads at 903 and the reconciliation finalize-vs-track check at 868. Do NOT apply it to the completion watcher unless the watcher is changed to shutdown_agent on Interrupt. Do NOT apply it to wait_for_final_status unless the serialized-subagent caller first adopts an explicit shutdown/resume policy; otherwise it can treat a resumable Interrupted status as a final worker outcome. Keep the test split: one test that an Interrupted job-worker is collected exactly once and its slot freed (no double-count vs a late lease-rejected report), and one test that an Interrupted ThreadSpawn child does NOT emit a premature parent notification if it is later resumed.
- **Grounding caveat:** All four anchors verified accurate. status.rs:23 explicitly lists Interrupted in the not-final set so is_final returns false for it. control.rs:637 (while !is_final) and 648 (final !is_final gate) confirm an interrupted ThreadSpawn child never reaches inject_user_message_without_turn (659), so the parent gets no completion edge. agent_jobs.rs:903 (find_finished_threads gates on is_final) confirms an interrupted worker is not collected; DEFAULT_AGENT_JOB_ITEM_TIMEOUT=30min at agent_jobs.rs:46 and reap_stale_active_items at 940 confirm the 30-min bound. The bounded liveness stall is real exactly as described.


### `state-machine-guards` · `outcome-witness-dedup-1` — Outcome-witness is validated twice with divergent satisfaction rules (pure validate_outcome_witness vs DB-backed validate_outcome_artifact_state), risking guard inconsistency

🏷 Pass 1 · impact **medium** · effort **M** · verifier **keep**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** ✅ **DO — real stability win** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **clear** — Every anchor and structural claim verifies against live code (line numbers drifted by ~30-90 lines but symbols exact). This is not merely drift risk: it is an active over-rejection. For external-chat (teams/jami/whatsapp/meeting) termina...

- [x] **shipped**
- **Anchors:** `src/core/service/core_state_machine.rs::validate_outcome_witness (line 489) + artifact_ref_satisfies (line 518)`, `src/core/service/core_transition_guard.rs::validate_outcome_artifact_state (line 215) + artifact_ref_satisfies (line 313)`
- **Problem:** There are two artifact_ref_satisfies implementations with DIFFERENT rules: the pure one in core_state_machine.rs (matches on '*', or primary_key starts_with 'thread:') and the guard one in core_transition_guard.rs which additionally matches OutboundCommunication keys containing ':'. validate_transition runs the pure check (WP-Outcome-Missing if no satisfying delivered ref), then evaluate_core_transition runs validate_outcome_artifact_state which re-checks the SAME expected refs plus DB state. The two satisfaction predicates can disagree (an OutboundCommunication artifact the guard considers satisfied is rejected by the pure pass before the DB check ever runs), so the effective contract depends on which layer fires first and the duplicated logic can drift on the next edit.
- **Fix:** Collapse to one source of truth for artifact_ref_satisfies and one outcome-witness entry point: keep the DB-backed validate_outcome_artifact_state (it strictly subsumes the pure presence check) and have it call a single shared satisfies() predicate, removing the divergent pure copy from the per-request path. This tightens the existing WP-Outcome gate by making it deterministic regardless of layer ordering.
- **Change sketch:** Make core_transition_guard::artifact_ref_satisfies the single predicate (or move it next to ArtifactRef and re-export), delete the divergent copy, and either remove validate_outcome_witness from validate_transition (since validate_outcome_artifact_state already enforces presence) or have it delegate to the shared predicate. Existing outcome-witness tests in both files pin the behavior.
- **Prüfsatz:** Q1 hardens the WP-Outcome-Missing/WP-Outcome-Wrong-State gate by deduplicating artifact_ref_satisfies. Q2 router untouched. Q4 outcome witness stays part of the core transition. Q7 satisfaction stays on explicit hard keys (kind+terminal_state+primary_key/thread), no fuzzy matching. Q9 the artifact refs are durable evidence. Q10 the existing outcome_witness tests plus a new case proving an OutboundCommunication ':' key is treated identically by both former paths.
- **Risk:** validate_transition is a pure function used by tests without a DB; removing the pure presence check there means pure-context callers lose the early presence check, so keep a pure presence-only check that delegates to the shared predicate rather than deleting it outright.
- **Verifier guidance:** Keep, with two tightenings. (1) Impact is understated: this is not merely drift risk — it is an ACTIVE over-rejection of OutboundCommunication (external-chat) outcome witnesses today. Because validate_transition runs first and the pure predicate lacks the OutboundCommunication+':' clause, a valid delivered ref (primary_key=message_key) never satisfies its expected ref (primary_key="channel:thread"); report.accepted goes false and validate_outcome_artifact_state's early-return at guard:220 means the guard's correct verdict is never reached. The guard's OutboundCommunication special-case (guard:319) is therefore effectively dead code. (2) Direction of dedup: put the single shared satisfies() predicate in core_state_machine.rs next to ArtifactRef (the pure/lower layer the guard already depends on via csm::), absorbing the OutboundCommunication+':' clause into it, and have both validate_outcome_witness (pure presence check) and validate_outcome_artifact_state delegate to it — rather than promoting the guard's copy upward and risking a layering inversion. Keep validate_outcome_witness as a pure presence-only check delegating to the shared predicate (the risk_note is correct: pure-context test callers at csm:1776+ rely on it without a DB). The new test must assert both former paths now agree on the (expected="channel:thread", delivered=message_key) OutboundCommunication case AND that a genuinely-missing OutboundCommunication artifact is still rejected, so the dedup tightens rather than loosens the gate.
- **Grounding caveat:** Re-opened both anchors. Pure artifact_ref_satisfies at core_state_machine.rs:518-524 has 3 OR-conditions (primary_key==delivered | =="*" | starts_with "thread:"). Guard artifact_ref_satisfies at core_transition_guard.rs:313-321 adds a 4th: (kind==OutboundCommunication && primary_key.contains(':')). Ordering confirmed: evaluate_core_transition (guard:163) calls csm::validate_transition first (runs pure validate_outcome_witness at csm:394 -> pure predicate, pushes WP-Outcome-Missing, sets report.accepted=false), THEN validate_outcome_artifact_state (guard:164) which early-returns on !report.accepted (guard:220). The divergence is live in production: expected_outcome_artifacts_for_job emits an OutboundCommunication expected ref with primary_key="{channel}:{thread_key}" (service.rs:6927-6931) while delivered_outcome_artifacts_for_job emits the same kind with primary_key=raw message_key (service.rs:6993). For that (expected="chan:thread", delivered="msg-key") pair the pure predicate returns false (no match, no "*", no "thread:") and rejects, while the guard predicate returns true. Real call path enforce_reviewed_work_terminal_success -> enforce_core_transition -> evaluate_core_transition (service.rs:3790, guard:424). The guard's OutboundCommunication special-case is effectively dead today because the pure pass short-circuits first.


### `turn-loop-context` · `turnloop-3` — Deterministic exact-repeat + repeated structured failure signals never hard-gate a doomed retry

🏷 Pass 1 · impact **medium** · effort **M** · verifier **keep**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** ✅ **DO — real stability win** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **clear** — Every anchor and behavioral claim verifies against live code. The harness deterministically computes hard loop facts (exact-normalized user-turn repetition and structured-failure count, both reaching Critical) yet the only invocation-ref...

- [x] **shipped**
- **Anchors:** `src/core/context/context_health.rs::repeated_recent_user_turns`, `src/core/context/context_health.rs::recent_blocked_status_count`, `src/core/context/context_health.rs::context_health_preempts_current_slice`, `src/core/execution/agent/turn_loop.rs::ensure_rendered_prompt_is_invocable`
- **Problem:** context_health computes hard, deterministic loop facts: an exact-normalized-match user turn count (repeated_recent_user_turns) and a repeated structured non-success/failure count over the last 8 assistant rows (recent_blocked_status_count), and raises blocked_status_loop / recent_user_turn_repeated to Critical at >=3 / >1. But the turn loop only refuses invocation when context selection is EMPTY and Critical (ensure_rendered_prompt_is_invocable, turn_loop.rs:826). A turn that is re-issuing an identical user prompt after repeated structured failures is still invoked — the harness burns another full local-inference turn (up to the 3600s budget) on a retry the deterministic signal already marked critical. There is no distinct `Blocked` outcome today, so the ticket must not pretend the signal is narrower than the code actually is.
- **Fix:** Add a deterministic short-circuit on the EXISTING critical loop codes (blocked_status_loop AND recent_user_turn_repeated both Critical) inside the existing ensure_rendered_prompt_is_invocable guard, or first introduce a narrower `Blocked`/`ContextRejected` outcome and gate only on that. Bail BEFORE invoke-model with a typed, retry-coolable error so the existing service classify path records it and cooldown handles it. This stays a hard-fact gate (exact key match on prompt text + structured outcome tokens), never a semantic 'are these similar' judgement.
- **Change sketch:** In ensure_rendered_prompt_is_invocable, after the existing critical-empty check, add: if health has BOTH a Critical recent_user_turn_repeated (exact-match, repetition>1) AND a Critical blocked_status_loop, anyhow::bail!("context_loop_short_circuit: exact-duplicate user turn re-entering an N-deep structured-failure loop with no new evidence"). Add the marker substring to hard_runtime_blocker_retry_cooldown_secs (turn_loop.rs:1199) so it gets a cooldown rather than a tight re-fire. Add negative tests for TurnTimeout/Cancelled or other structured failures you do not want this gate to over-block.
- **Prüfsatz:** Q1 hardens ensure_rendered_prompt_is_invocable + the loop scoring it already consumes. Q2 router untouched. Q3 same slice; the bail routes through the same service error handling. Q4 the resulting failure flows through the existing classify/agent_failure status path, not a bypass. Q5 no spawn. Q6 same conversation. Q7 the gate fires only on EXACT normalized prompt equality + structured outcome tokens — explicit hard keys, never semantic similarity. Q8 Skills untouched. Q9 produces an auditable typed bail + cooldown. Q10 a turn-loop test pins 'exact-duplicate prompt + 3 intended structured loop-failure rows -> guard bails before invoke' and negative cases prove non-loop transient failures do not trip it accidentally.
- **Risk:** Medium. Must be conservative: require BOTH exact duplication AND structured blocked loop so legitimate 'continue' prompts (which are not exact duplicates) never trip it. Risk of over-blocking a genuinely progressing loop is bounded because repeated_recent_user_turns uses exact normalized equality, not similarity.
- **Verifier guidance:** Keep, with two tightening notes for the implementer. (1) Frame it as completing an existing-but-unwired design rather than net-new: the loop codes already have a designed consumer (evaluate_loop_governor) that is advisory and, more importantly, not invoked anywhere in production. The hardening should make the deterministic exact-repeat + repeated structured loop-failure fact actually gate the invoke inside ensure_rendered_prompt_is_invocable, after the existing critical-empty checks (turn_loop.rs:826-832). (2) Keep the conjunction conservative: require BOTH a Critical recent_user_turn_repeated (repetition>1, i.e. >=3 identical user prompts total) AND a Critical blocked_status_loop (blocked_count>=3), but verify what counts as "blocked" in current code before widening behavior. recent_blocked_status_count prefers structured agent_outcome tokens and does not expose a dedicated `Blocked` variant today, so either introduce a narrower token first or add negative tests for transient outcomes. Use a distinct marker substring (e.g. "context_loop_short_circuit") and add it to hard_runtime_blocker_retry_cooldown_secs (turn_loop.rs:1199 block) so it cools down like context_selection_empty rather than tight-refiring. Add the bail to all three call sites' shared guard (it already is one function). Test: exact-duplicate prompt + 3 intended structured loop-failure rows -> guard bails before invoke; non-duplicate "continue" prompt and transient-failure histories do NOT bail.
- **Grounding caveat:** All four anchors exist and the problem claim holds when re-read. repeated_recent_user_turns (context_health.rs:1020) is exact-normalized-match only (line 1032), skip(1).take(8). recent_blocked_status_count (1036) counts over the last 8 assistant rows, preferring the structured agent_outcome (F3) path (message_indicates_blocked_status, 1051-1058) with a legacy text fallback. blocked_status_loop reaches Critical at blocked_count>=3 (722); recent_user_turn_repeated reaches Critical at repetition>1 (704). ensure_rendered_prompt_is_invocable (794) has exactly two invocation-refusal bails, both for context_selection_empty (822, 829); neither consumes the loop codes. The only other consumer of the codes in the turn surface is context_health_preempts_current_slice (280), which matches ONLY mission_contract_thin/failure_memory_missing (284-286), not the loop codes, and only produces advisory prompt text via render_prompt_block. So a turn re-issuing an exact-duplicate prompt after >=3 counted failure/blocked rows is still invoked (invoke-model at turn_loop.rs:633), burning a full turn the deterministic signal already marked critical.
