### `crate-boundary` · `x-flow-event-lossy-nontxn` — Harness-flow forensic bridge is non-transactional + error-swallowing + non-idempotent, so a durable state change and its audit event can silently diverge

🏷 Pass 2 · impact **high** · effort **M** · kind **bug** · verifier **revise**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** ⚠️ **REVISE — implement only the Verifier-guidance scope** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **clear** — All anchors are real and the core smell is live: record_harness_flow_event_lossy silently drops errors (incl. SQLITE_BUSY) from a fresh second WAL connection to the same ctox.sqlite3, and at put_ticket_self_work_item (tickets.rs:2750) th...

> ⚠️ **Canonical issue:** implement the **Canonical scope** + **Verifier guidance** below. (The stale original Fix/Change-sketch fields were removed in the live re-audit cleanup.)

- [ ] **open**
- **Canonical scope:** Implement the corrected scope in **Verifier guidance**. Treat the superseded original fix/sketch/test mapping as historical context, not instructions.
- **Canonical verification:** Use the Q10/test instructions in **Verifier guidance**; if they conflict with any superseded original field, Verifier guidance wins.
- **Anchors:** `src/core/service/harness_flow.rs::record_harness_flow_event_lossy`, `src/core/service/harness_flow.rs::record_harness_flow_event`, `src/core/service/harness_flow.rs::open_event_connection`, `src/core/service/harness_flow.rs::event_id`, `src/core/mission/tickets.rs::put_ticket_self_work_item`
- **Problem:** Every forensic flow event for internal-work/queue/ticket/channel activity goes through `record_harness_flow_event_lossy(root, ...)`, which (1) opens a *fresh second connection* to ctox.sqlite3 (`open_event_connection`, harness_flow.rs:1350) rather than reusing the caller's `conn`, (2) is `_lossy` — `let _ = record_harness_flow_event(...)` (harness_flow.rs:307) silently drops any error including SQLITE_BUSY under the serial router's WAL contention, and (3) derives `event_id` from a SHA256 that includes `created_at = Utc::now()` (event_id fn), so it is *not* idempotent on retry. Concretely in `put_ticket_self_work_item` (tickets.rs:2745-2790) the durable upsert + `record_audit` run on one `conn` (their own transaction), then the flow event is written on a *different* connection afterward — they cannot be atomic. Result: a committed internal-work creation can have no forensic flow event (write lost, silently), or a rolled-back caller can still have emitted unrelated lossy events. The flow ledger is the harness-flow page's source of truth and the cross-cutting bridge between the two DBs' views; it is the weakest-durability writer in the whole audit plane.
- **Risk:** Medium: threading a connection through ~14 callers must avoid nested-transaction errors — where a caller is mid-transaction the event INSERT must use the same conn, not BEGIN again. Idempotency change is safe because event_id is already a content hash.
- **Verifier guidance:** Core weakness is real (silent-drop + non-atomic forensic writer is the weakest-durability audit writer), but two parts of the proposal are factually wrong and must be corrected. (c) IDEMPOTENCY FIX IS HARMFUL: event_id is a content+TIME hash, not 'already a content hash'; created_at is load-bearing for an append-only ledger whose indexes are all (...,created_at ASC). Dropping created_at + INSERT OR IGNORE would silently collapse legitimately-repeated identical events into one row (e.g. same message spilled->restored->spilled again with the default reason at queue.rs:1650, or repeated queue.cleanup_scope with same reason at queue.rs:634). And there is NO retry loop around these _lossy calls, so the non-idempotency is largely moot anyway. DROP part (c) (or make dedupe an explicit opt-in caller key, never by stripping time). (a) ATOMICITY SCOPE OVERSTATED: queue.rs:634/1650/1733 operate purely through root-based helpers (channels::update_queue_task(root,..), tickets::set_ticket_self_work_state(root,..)) that each open their own connection — those mutations are already multi-connection/non-atomic, so there is no single conn to thread and threading one would not make them atomic. Conn-threading is only meaningful at sites holding a live conn (e.g. put_ticket_self_work_item at tickets.rs:2750). CORRECTED VERSION: (b) replace the bare `let _ =` with a logged+counted drop on the existing telemetry surface so lost forensic writes are detectable (clean, zero-collision-risk, the highest-value piece); (a) at the subset of call sites that genuinely hold a live conn, add record_harness_flow_event_on(conn,..) that reuses that conn (no nested BEGIN) so state-change+event commit together. Add a parity test there. Keep the smell, fix the prescription.
- **Grounding caveat:** All anchors verified. harness_flow.rs:306-308 record_harness_flow_event_lossy = `let _ = record_harness_flow_event(...)` silent drop. record_harness_flow_event (256) opens fresh conn via open_event_connection (260->1350) on the same runtime/ctox.sqlite3 as the router/ticket writers, so SQLITE_BUSY under WAL contention is plausible and silently swallowed. event_id (1540) hashes created_at (1550) with created_at=Utc::now() (262), schema event_id TEXT PRIMARY KEY (1372). In put_ticket_self_work_item (tickets.rs:2750-2801) upsert+record_audit run on a live `conn`, then record_harness_flow_event_lossy(root,...) writes on a SEPARATE connection -> cannot be atomic. 15 call sites (queue/tickets/channels), no loss counter, only a renderer test exists (1651). Atomicity gap and silent-drop gap are real now.


### `review-outcome` · `review-3` — Closure-blocking outcome-witness claims are advisory only — no deterministic closure gate

🏷 Pass 1 · impact **high** · effort **M** · verifier **revise**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** ⚠️ **REVISE — implement only the Verifier-guidance scope** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **clear** — The core finding is real and grounded: closure-blocking outcome-witness claims are persisted but never consumed by a deterministic gate — validate_ticket_closure only checks verification_id is non-empty, so a worker/model can close a tic...

> ⚠️ **Canonical issue:** implement the **Canonical scope** + **Verifier guidance** below. (The stale original Fix/Change-sketch fields were removed in the live re-audit cleanup.)

- [x] **shipped**
- **Canonical scope:** Implement the corrected scope in **Verifier guidance**. Treat the superseded original fix/sketch/test mapping as historical context, not instructions.
- **Canonical verification:** Use the Q10/test instructions in **Verifier guidance**; if they conflict with any superseded original field, Verifier guidance wins.
- **Anchors:** `src/core/service/core_state_machine.rs::validate_ticket_closure`, `src/core/service/core_state_machine.rs:775`, `src/core/mission/verification.rs::RecordedSliceAssurance::closure_blocking_open_items`, `src/core/context/lcm.rs::mission_assurance_snapshot`, `src/core/context/live_context.rs:1369`
- **Problem:** verification.rs derives operational_state/artifact_state/completion_gate claims with blocks_closure=true and persists them (record_slice_assurance, verification.rs:138; closure_blocking_open_items, verification.rs:91/171). But these closure-blocking claims are only rendered into live context (live_context.rs:1369) and the turn-loop snapshot (turn_loop.rs:472) as advisory prompt text. The deterministic closure gate validate_ticket_closure (core_state_machine.rs:775) checks ONLY that evidence.verification_id is non-empty — it never checks whether the referenced verification run still has OPEN closure-blocking claims. So a worker/model can satisfy the gate by attaching any verification_id while an operational_state claim ('rollout still 502', verification.rs test:614) is open. The outcome witness exists but does not actually witness closure; the hard fact 'no open closure-blocking claim' is left to model judgement.
- **Risk:** Medium — must ensure the count is read for the SAME verification_id presented as closure evidence (avoid a stale or cross-conversation snapshot); operational_state claims auto-expire after OPERATIONAL_CLAIM_EXPIRY_HOURS so the gate self-clears, preventing permanent deadlock.
- **Verifier guidance:** The weakness is real and worth fixing, but the proposed KEYING is wrong and must be corrected before this can be implemented. The finding assumes the closure-blocking count is 'queryable via mission_assurance_snapshot keyed by verification_id' (Q7: 'keyed on the durable claim_key / verification run id'). It is NOT. Two distinct, non-overlapping id namespaces exist:\n(a) ticket_verifications table (tickets.rs:10309-10315): PK verification_id, keyed by case_id, columns (verification_id, case_id, status, summary, created_at). This is what supplies evidence.verification_id at ticket closure via latest_passed_ticket_verification_id (tickets.rs:9405, 9508-9525).\n(b) verification_runs table (lcm.rs:906-924): PK run_id (a 'vrun_' SHA prefix, verification.rs:539-548), keyed by conversation_id, the only place closure_blocking_claim_count lives. mission_assurance_snapshot (lcm.rs:2181) takes conversation_id, NOT a verification_id.\nThese ids never match. There is also no case_id -> conversation_id bridge on tickets, so the count cannot be sourced from the verification_id presented as closure evidence, contrary to the changeSketch and risk note ('read for the SAME verification_id presented as closure evidence').\n\nCORRECTED tighter version: validate_transition (core_state_machine.rs:370) is a PURE function with no DB handle, so the claim-count must be resolved at the guard call site, where evaluate_core_transition/enforce_core_transition DO hold `conn` (core_transition_guard.rs:137/420). Two viable scopes:\n1. Narrow (chat/slice closure on the verification_runs subsystem): at the call site that closes a conversation-scoped work item, call engine.mission_assurance_snapshot(conversation_id), compute open closure_blocking count, stamp it onto a NEW deterministic CoreEvidenceRefs field (e.g. open_closure_blocking_claims: u32). validate_ticket_closure pushes a 'closure_blocked_by_open_witness_claims' violation when that field > 0 AND to_state==Closed. This keys on conversation_id (a hard key), not verification_id.\n2. For ticket closure specifically, this gate does NOT apply as written, because tickets use ticket_verifications and have no conversation linkage — do not claim it hardens ticket closure unless a case_id->conversation_id key is first established (out of scope; would be its own change).\nKeep the determinism-split framing and the auto-expiry deadlock argument; both are correct. Add the state-machine test mirroring verification.rs:614 but driving the NEW evidence field, asserting reject while count>0 and accept at 0. The finding's id-keying claims (changeSketch + Q7 + risk) must be rewritten to conversation_id (or case_id once bridged) before merge.
- **Grounding caveat:** All anchors exist and the core weakness is real. validate_ticket_closure (core_state_machine.rs:779-794) checks ONLY that evidence.verification_id is non-empty — confirmed. closure_blocking_claim_count is persisted on VerificationRunRecord (verification.rs:169-218, schema lcm.rs:922) and closure_blocking_claims are rendered ONLY as advisory prompt text in render_verified_evidence_block (live_context.rs:1369-1376). claim_is_open (verification.rs:501) and the test records_operational_failure_as_open_closure_blocking_claim (verification.rs:614) exist. No deterministic gate consumes open closure-blocking claims. The weakness (witness claims are advisory, not a closure gate) holds.


### `skills-evidence` · `skills-1` — Skill name is carried but the skill body is never guaranteed into the worker turn

🏷 Pass 1 · impact **high** · effort **M** · verifier **revise**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** ⚠️ **REVISE — implement only the Verifier-guidance scope** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **clear** — Real, live, fully-grounded reproducibility/correctness defect: a deterministic skill binding (suggested_skill, used as a hard binding at scrape.rs:835, iot/commands.rs:1661, follow_up.rs) is rendered only as advisory text with no $ sigil...

> ⚠️ **Canonical issue:** implement the **Canonical scope** + **Verifier guidance** below. (The stale original Fix/Change-sketch fields were removed in the live re-audit cleanup.)

- [ ] **open**
- **Canonical scope:** Implement the corrected scope in **Verifier guidance**. Treat the superseded original fix/sketch/test mapping as historical context, not instructions.
- **Canonical verification:** Use the Q10/test instructions in **Verifier guidance**; if they conflict with any superseded original field, Verifier guidance wins.
- **Anchors:** `src/core/context/live_context.rs::render_skill_dispatch_block`, `src/core/harness/core/src/skills/injection.rs::collect_explicit_skill_mentions`, `src/core/harness/core/src/skills/injection.rs::build_skill_injections`, `src/core/mission/channels.rs::create_queue_task_with_metadata`
- **Problem:** A skill-bound queue/internal-work task carries only the skill NAME (queue metadata `skill` -> `suggested_skill`). render_skill_dispatch_block emits the plain hint `preferred_skill: X` (not a $mention), and build_skill_injections/collect_explicit_skill_mentions only load a skill body when the prompt text literally contains a $skill-name mention. So for a deterministically skill-bound task the procedure body is injected only if the model volunteers a $mention; the binding is advisory, not enforced. Mass skill-bound tasks are not reproducible because two runs of the same bound skill may or may not have seen the procedure.
- **Risk:** Double-inject risk if the model also mentions it is covered by existing seen_paths/seen_names dedupe; skill names are valid mention tokens ([a-z0-9-]).
- **Verifier guidance:** REAL weakness, but the proposed fix (append plain "$name" to the dispatch block) is NOT actually deterministic and so fails the reproducibility goal it is built on. A plain $name mention only resolves to a body in select_skills_from_mentions (injection.rs:361-395) when skill_count == 1 AND connector_count == 0 AND the name is not a blocked plain name (lines 370, 373, 387). For an ambiguous skill name (same name under two scopes, e.g. user+system or repo+plugin) skill_count != 1, or for a connector-slug collision, the mention is SILENTLY DROPPED and the body is still not injected -- exactly the non-reproducible case the finding targets. Tighter correct fix: resolve the bound skill's path at turn construction (when suggested_skill is set) and either (a) inject a structured UserInput::Skill { name, path } alongside the UserInput::Text -- collect_explicit_skill_mentions resolves it by EXACT PATH at injection.rs:137-154, bypassing the ambiguity gate -- or (b) emit the existing linked mention form [name]($path), which extract_tool_mentions resolves by path at injection.rs:266-278, also bypassing the ambiguity gate. Both are deterministic and reuse the unchanged build_skill_injections path. The plain-$name sketch should be rejected in favor of the path-resolved form. Note this requires the render/turn layer to know the skill path, which suggested_skill (name only) does not currently carry, so the fix must add a name->path lookup against the enabled-skills catalog at turn construction (deterministic lookup, not a new injector). Existing seen_paths/seen_names dedupe (injection.rs:133-134) covers the double-inject-if-model-also-mentions risk, so that risk note is fine. Test must assert that a bound suggested_skill -- including an AMBIGUOUSLY-NAMED one -- produces exactly one SkillInstructions injection, and must write any host state to the test root's SQLite runtime config, not std::env.
- **Grounding caveat:** All four anchors exist and the weakness is real. Verified path: render_skill_dispatch_block (live_context.rs:482-489) emits plain "preferred_skill: {skill}" with NO $ sigil. That prompt flows verbatim to the worker turn: turn_loop.rs:636 -> session.run_turn_inner(&rendered_prompt.prompt) -> direct_session.rs:948 wraps it as a single UserInput::Text { text: prompt } -> codex.rs:5440 collect_explicit_skill_mentions(&input,...). collect_explicit_skill_mentions (injection.rs:118-171) only resolves skills from structured UserInput::Skill inputs (none are constructed in CTOX) or from extract_tool_mentions, which (injection.rs:257-311) only collects names after a '$' sigil byte (or a [..]($path) linked form). "preferred_skill: system-onboarding" has no '$' -> zero mentions -> build_skill_injections returns empty -> no SkillInstructions injected. render_skills_section (render.rs:6-57) injects only name+description+path, never the body. So a deterministically skill-bound task only gets its procedure body if the model volunteers a $mention. Confirmed suggested_skill carrier is the queue metadata "skill" key (channels.rs:2280, 2386-2387) and is used as a real binding (scrape.rs:835 DEFAULT_REPAIR_SKILL, iot/commands.rs:1661, follow_up.rs change-lifecycle, etc.).


### `crate-boundary` · `x-subagent-liveness-static-only` — Subagent leaf/depth liveness is proven only against a static source-string model, never against the running harness's actual threads

🏷 Pass 2 · impact **medium** · effort **M** · kind **missing-test** · verifier **revise**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** ⚠️ **REVISE — implement only the Verifier-guidance scope** · grounded **partial** · stability **marginal** — All 5 anchors are real and accurately cited (only line numbers drift). The core claim is true: analyze_harness_subagent_spawn_model() really is a source-string conformance proof and is the only harness half of spawn-liveness. But the tic...

> ⚠️ **Canonical issue:** implement the **Canonical scope** + **Verifier guidance** below. (The stale original Fix/Change-sketch fields were removed in the live re-audit cleanup.)

- [ ] **open**
- **Canonical scope:** Implement the corrected scope in **Verifier guidance**. Treat the superseded original fix/sketch/test mapping as historical context, not instructions.
- **Canonical verification:** Use the Q10/test instructions in **Verifier guidance**; if they conflict with any superseded original field, Verifier guidance wins.
- **Anchors:** `src/core/harness/core/src/harness_spawn_liveness.rs::analyze_harness_subagent_spawn_model`, `src/core/service/process_mining.rs:1080`, `src/core/service/process_mining.rs:2376`, `src/core/harness/core/src/tools/handlers/multi_agents/spawn.rs:45`, `src/core/harness/state/migrations/0021_threads_subagent_forensics.sql`
- **Problem:** `analyze_harness_subagent_spawn_model()` proves the subagent liveness invariant by scanning *embedded source text* — e.g. asserting `spawn_handler.contains("exceeds_thread_spawn_depth_limit(child_depth, max_depth)")` (harness_spawn_liveness.rs:54-62) — and checking config defaults. This is the only subagent half of `ctox process-mining spawn-liveness` (process_mining.rs:1080/2376). It is a *model-conformance* proof, not runtime evidence: it confirms the source still has the right shape, but nothing reads the actual `threads` rows (with their migrated `subagent_depth`/`agent_path`) to confirm the *running* harness never produced a thread deeper than `agents.max_depth` or a non-leaf subagent. Because the subagent spawn writes no row into the orchestration ledger (spawn.rs enforces depth against config only, by design per liveness-1-revise), a real runtime divergence — a forked Codex delta, a stale config, or a depth check that regresses behind an unchanged string — would pass the proof while violating the invariant in production.
- **Risk:** Low: read-only over the state DB; the only subtlety is locating the state DB (use the same `find_codex_home`/state_db_path the runtime already uses) and tolerating its absence (no-threads = vacuously ok).
- **Verifier guidance:** REVISE — real but the proposal as written is over-motivated and has a soundness flaw. Two corrections: (1) Drop the framing that the invariant is untested — guards_tests.rs:19-31 and spec_tests.rs:622 already cover the depth-fn-regression and leaf-tool-surface modes against real code, so the only genuinely uncovered mode is 'a forked Codex delta (or out-of-band writer) persisted a thread row deeper than the modeled bound.' Scope the finding to THAT. (2) The proposed live invariant `MAX(subagent_depth) > current agents.max_depth` is config-drift-UNSOUND: the persisted subagent_depth was gated against the max_depth in effect AT SPAWN TIME (spawn.rs:46 reads turn.config.agent_max_depth per turn), so legitimately lowering agents.max_depth later would flag valid historical rows as violations and produce false 'critical' subsystem reports in process-mining (process_mining.rs:2380). The seed test masks this because it pins config. Corrected version: make it a deterministic FORENSIC backstop, not a config-relative invariant — assert the structural shape that holds regardless of config, namely (a) every non-root thread's subagent_depth strictly exceeds its parent's persisted subagent_depth by exactly 1 (monotone parent/child via subagent_parent_thread_id), and (b) no thread is both a subagent (subagent_parent_thread_id NOT NULL) AND a parent of a thread that itself has a child — i.e. the leaf/path-shape invariant — neither of which depends on the current config value. Compare against max_depth only as a soft warning, never as the 'critical' gate. Also note the preventive value is limited: in CI/fresh DBs there are no deep rows so the check is vacuously ok (the finding admits this), meaning it catches a breach only AFTER it occurred in production — acceptable as a forensic backstop, but it should be sold as detective evidence, not a preventive invariant. With those two fixes it is a legal, in-bounds, low-risk hardening of the existing process-mining harness_subagent_liveness subsystem.
- **Grounding caveat:** All 5 anchors verified. analyze_harness_subagent_spawn_model() is genuinely a source-string proof: it scans include_str! of spawn.rs/spec.rs/FORK.md (harness_spawn_liveness.rs:37-72) and is wired as the ONLY harness half of spawn-liveness (process_mining.rs:1080 and 2376). The subagent_depth column exists (migration 0021) and IS populated at runtime: spawn.rs:45-47 computes child_depth, thread_spawn_source (multi_agents.rs:283-295) carries it into the child source, and thread_metadata.rs:326 + threads.rs:265/418 persist it; thread_metadata.rs:376 reads it back. So the data path is live, not a dead column. BUT the problem statement is overstated: it claims the leaf/depth invariant is proven 'never against the running harness's actual threads.' In fact two of its three named failure modes are already covered by behavior-level unit tests that exercise the SAME code spawn.rs calls: guards_tests.rs:19-31 (thread_spawn_depth_increments_and_enforces_limit) directly calls next_thread_spawn_depth + exceeds_thread_spawn_depth_limit (guards.rs:63-69, the identical fns at spawn.rs:45-47), so a 'depth check that regresses behind an unchanged string' fails that test; spec_tests.rs:622 (test_build_specs_thread_spawn_subagents_are_leaf_workers) builds the real SubAgent tool spec and asserts spawn tools are absent, covering the recursive-tool-surface leaf bound. Only the 'forked Codex delta producing a thread row deeper than max_depth' mode is genuinely uncovered.


### `failmode-patterns` · `x2-3` — Durable governance audit-write `record_event` is dropped-on-failure at ~half its callsites — accountability evidence vanishes invisibly under DB contention

🏷 Pass 2 · impact **medium** · effort **M** · kind **design-pattern** · verifier **revise**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** ⚠️ **REVISE — implement only the Verifier-guidance scope** · grounded **partial** · stability **marginal** — Anchors are real and the underlying smell is genuine: a fallible audit-write primitive is swallowed at 27 production sites and surfaced at only 2, an inconsistent pattern. But the ticket is wrong twice over on magnitude — the original "3...

> ⚠️ **Canonical issue:** implement the **Canonical scope** + **Verifier guidance** below. (The stale original Fix/Change-sketch fields were removed in the live re-audit cleanup.)

- [ ] **open**
- **Canonical scope:** Implement the corrected scope in **Verifier guidance**. Treat the superseded original fix/sketch/test mapping as historical context, not instructions.
- **Canonical verification:** Use the Q10/test instructions in **Verifier guidance**; if they conflict with any superseded original field, Verifier guidance wins.
- **Anchors:** `src/core/service/governance.rs:326 (record_event: fallible — open_governance_db, upsert_default_mechanisms, INSERT, all `?`)`, `src/core/service/service.rs:816,860,891,939,1172,1195,1249,1378,9186 (let _ = governance::record_event — sample of 23 swallowed sites in service.rs)`, `src/core/mission/strategy.rs / channels.rs / lcm.rs / plan.rs (further `let _ = record_event` sites)`, `31 swallowed `let _ = ...record_event` vs 35 checked across src/core (grep)`
- **Problem:** `record_event` IS the durable accountability primitive — every governance decision (mission defer, stale-lease reclaim, sender block, queue pressure) is supposed to leave a row. Across src/core ~31 callsites invoke it as `let _ =` and ~35 check it, with no principle distinguishing them — the same kind of event is checked in one file and swallowed in another. When `record_event` fails (DB locked under the serial router's concurrent writers, or a schema/mechanism regression), the audit row never lands and nothing records that it failed. Process-mining and the TUI feed then present an incomplete, silently-lossy audit history: the harness's central claim of being 'auditable' is undermined by a coin-flip on whether each event actually persisted. This is the systemic root of the eprintln/swallow-vs-evidence concern.
- **Risk:** Low — mechanical, control-flow-preserving. Risk is only completeness of the sed sweep; a leaf grep audit confirms coverage.
- **Verifier guidance:** REAL smell, but the fix is mechanically broken and the magnitude is overstated. Corrected version: (1) Scope is 29 production `let _ = record_event(` sites, NOT 31 — drop governance.rs:810/889 (they are #[cfg(test)]). (2) The intended surfacing already exists and is correct at service.rs:9895 and 14213: on Err they call push_event_locked(shared, "...persistence failed: {err}") — that is the pattern to GENERALIZE, not eprintln. (3) The proposed free fn `record_event_or_log(root, req)` is wrong: it can only do eprintln (it has no access to `shared`), which is the weaker stderr-only path the codebase already moved past at the 2 good sites; a sed sweep into it would actively DOWNGRADE those 2 sites if they were included. (4) Correct fix is two-tier: where the lock is held (the bulk of service.rs sites under `shared`), convert `let _ =` to `if let Err(err)` + push_event_locked (feed-visible, process-mining-visible). For the few sites with no feed handle (lcm.rs:4338, strategy.rs:242/259, plan.rs:458, channels.rs:10944/10966), a log+counter wrapper is acceptable as fallback. (5) Optional AtomicU64 dropped_audit_writes counter is a good add for status surfacing but is the lesser half — the feed push is the load-bearing part. (6) Test: assert a forced record_event Err results in a feed event (not just no-panic), matching the 9895/14213 contract. With these corrections it is a sound, constraint-compliant audit-evidence hardening.
- **Grounding caveat:** record_event at governance.rs:326 is fallible (open_governance_db/upsert/INSERT all `?`) — confirmed. Swallow pattern is real and widespread. BUT the finding's counts are inflated/wrong. Actual: 29 PRODUCTION `let _ = record_event(` sites vs only 2 production sites that check (service.rs:9895 and 14213, both `if let Err(err)` → push_event_locked to the feed). The cited "31 swallowed vs 35 checked, ~half, coin-flip" is inaccurate: 2 of its 31 swallow anchors (governance.rs:810, 889) are inside `#[cfg(test)]` (test module starts at governance.rs:795), and the "35 checked" has no basis — grep finds only 5 non-`let _=` occurrences total, 2 of which are the test-assert captures (838/851) and 1 is the fn defn. So the real ratio is ~29:2, which makes the inconsistency argument STRONGER, not a coin-flip.

- **Canonical verification:** Use the Q10/test instructions in **Verifier guidance**; if they conflict with any superseded original field, Verifier guidance wins.
- **Anchors:** `src/core/execution/models/supervisor.rs::ensure_persistent_backends`, `src/core/execution/models/supervisor.rs::start_backend_supervisor`, `src/core/execution/models/supervisor.rs::persistent_backend_alerts`
- **Problem:** start_backend_supervisor (supervisor.rs:405) prints a Chat-role Err to stderr (supervisor.rs:408) and retries forever; no durable record captures the reason. persistent_backend_alerts (supervisor.rs:685) reports only live residue, not the launch-failure reason, so a host where the chat model never starts loops quietly with no last-launch-failure field in ServiceStatus.
- **Risk:** Store a status string not a control flag; clip the reason.
- **Verifier guidance:** Invariant is real and worth hardening, but the change sketch's "persist via a runtime_env setter" is imprecise and risky as written. The ONLY public writer is save_runtime_env_map (runtime_env.rs:53-65), which (a) round-trips the WHOLE map through runtime_state::derive_runtime_state_from_env_map (line 63) — feeding a status key through runtime-state derivation — and (b) write_runtime_env_map (192-217) does a full `DELETE FROM runtime_env_kv` + re-insert of the entire map per call. Invoked from the forever-retry supervisor loop on every Chat Err, this races with concurrent config writers (service.rs / TUI worker) and can clobber their edits, and there is no narrow single-key setter exposed. TIGHTER VERSION: (1) Record on BOTH the Chat-role Err path in ensure_persistent_backends (422-431) AND, preferably, at the failure source inside wait_for_backend_ready (2420-2455) where managed_backend_failure_detail is already computed, so the reason is captured before it is flattened into the bail! string. (2) Persist via a read-modify-write that loads the current map, sets ONE namespaced status key (e.g. CTOX_CHAT_BACKEND_LAST_LAUNCH_FAILURE = `<ts>|<clipped reason>`, mirroring the existing CTOX_PLATFORM_CONTRACT_STATUS status-string precedent so it is ignored by runtime-state derivation), and writes back — but only writing the delta is not supported, so the safest minimal move is to add a tiny dedicated single-key upsert (INSERT ... ON CONFLICT) into runtime_env_kv inside runtime_env (mirroring write_runtime_env_map's transaction shape) instead of rewriting the full map and re-deriving runtime state. (3) Clear the key on the Ok branch (success in wait_for_backend_ready / ensure_backend_process). (4) Surface it through persistent_backend_alerts unconditionally (not gated on !service_running, since the whole point is a running service with a dead chat model). (5) Q10 test: reuse the existing temp_root scaffolding (supervisor.rs test mod, e.g. wait_for_backend_ready_reports_child_exit_status at 4451) to assert the key is persisted on Err and cleared on Ok, writing to the test root's SQLite store (not std::env). Keep the reason clip identical to managed_backend_failure_detail (last 3 non-empty log lines + exit status) to avoid unbounded growth.
- **Grounding caveat:** Verified all 3 anchors. start_backend_supervisor (supervisor.rs:405-412) prints Chat Err to stderr at line 408 and retries forever on SUPERVISOR_POLL_SECS. ensure_persistent_backends (414-435) returns Err for non-auxiliary/Chat at 422-431. persistent_backend_alerts (685-687) -> persistent_backend_residue_with_scope (697-733) reports ONLY live residue (alive/stale pids, transports, ports, startup locks, runtime groups), no launch-failure reason. managed_backend_failure_detail (2493-2518) computes a clipped 3-line reason but is consumed ONLY inside anyhow::bail! messages (2420-2428, 2447-2455). service.rs:2725-2732 only extends alerts with backend residue when !service_running, so a service-running host whose chat backend never starts produces no machine-readable record. No durable last-launch-failure field exists. Minor inaccuracy: finding attributes the stderr print to line 408 'inside' ensure_persistent_backends, but 408 is in start_backend_supervisor; substance holds.

- **Problem:** ensure_persistent_backends skips an auxiliary error (supervisor.rs:423-428) but returns Err on a Chat error (supervisor.rs:430). This boundary decides whether a model-infra failure becomes a durable InfraFailed outcome. The supervisor tests (from supervisor.rs:3515, e.g. child-exit at supervisor.rs:4405) never pin this split, so a refactor could silently make chat best-effort.
- **Risk:** Keep hermetic via unresolved binary paths; write config to the test root SQLite store.

(1) Fix the framing: do NOT claim this boundary "decides whether a model-infra failure becomes a durable InfraFailed outcome." All three callers of ensure_persistent_backends discard its Err (poll loop eprintln:407; tui:4015 `let _`; runtime_control:231 `let _ =`). The durable chat InfraFailed path is ensure_chat_backend_ready (turn_loop.rs:402-403). The honest invariant: at the fleet-supervisor layer, an auxiliary backend failure is downgraded to continue (423-428) while a Chat failure aborts the reconcile pass with Err (430) — i.e., chat failures are never silently absorbed there.

(2) Fix hermeticity: the sketch's two scenarios are not deterministically triggerable as described. For the AUX branch, an unresolved aux model hits the soft-skip at ensure_backend_process:1821-1834 and returns Ok(()) — it never reaches the is_auxiliary() error arm, so the test would prove nothing. For the CHAT branch, ensure_backend_process must first pass reconcile_chat_runtime_plan (1804, can `?`-fail host-dependently), survive the empty-model early-return (1808 returns Ok not Err), then resolve_gpu_admission (1837), before any missing-binary spawn — so a temp root + CTOX_CHAT_SOURCE=local + model name does not obviously yield a deterministic Err vs Ok.

Tighter recommendation: rather than driving the full ensure_backend_process spawn path (host-dependent), pin the propagation policy at the unit it actually owns. Either (a) refactor the branch decision (line 422-431) into a tiny pure helper `fn propagate_backend_outcome(role, Result<()>) -> Result<()>` that returns Ok on aux-Err and passes through chat-Err, and unit-test that helper with synthetic Ok/Err for each of the 5 roles (deterministic, zero host deps, mirrors is_auxiliary at 185); or (b) if no refactor is wanted, add a test that asserts is_auxiliary()==true for Embedding/Stt/Tts/Vision and false for Chat AND a comment-anchored test documenting that ensure_persistent_backends returns Err iff a non-auxiliary role fails — driven through the helper, not the live spawn. Keep it to one #[test], no std::env writes (use save_runtime_env_map to the temp root only if config is actually read). Drop the InfraFailed wording from impact/pruefsatz. Effort stays S; with the helper extraction it is honestly hermetic.
- **Grounding caveat:** All three anchors exist. ensure_persistent_backends at supervisor.rs:414-435 has exactly the claimed split: is_auxiliary() error -> eprintln+continue (423-428), else return Err(err) (430). is_auxiliary at 185-187 (self != Chat). api_runtime_does_not_keep_primary_generation_managed at 3583-3593 uses temp_root (3622) + save_runtime_env_map as cited. Confirmed via awk that NO test calls ensure_persistent_backends (only refs are def:414 and poll-thread caller:407), so the chat-vs-aux propagation split is genuinely unpinned. HOWEVER the finding's causal claim is overstated: ensure_persistent_backends's Err is discarded by ALL THREE callers (supervisor poll loop eprintln:407-409; tui/mod.rs:4015 `let _`; runtime_control.rs:231 `let _ =`). The durable InfraFailed chat path is actually ensure_chat_backend_ready (turn_loop.rs:402-403, `.context(...)?`-propagated), not ensure_persistent_backends. So the Err at line 430 does not itself become a durable outcome; the real invariant is narrower: a chat-backend failure is never silently swallowed at the fleet-supervisor layer while aux failures always are.

### `queue-lifecycle` · `queue-3` — Spill candidate scoring is blind to durable failure evidence in transition proofs

🏷 Pass 1 · impact **medium** · effort **S** · verifier **revise**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** ⚠️ **REVISE — implement only the Verifier-guidance scope** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **marginal** — Anchors and every grounding claim verify against live code. The scorer is genuinely failure-blind, durable Failed proofs exist, and last_error is non-durable — the gap is real. But the original change sketch (min(count,3)*3; test seeds "...

> ⚠️ **Canonical issue:** implement the **Canonical scope** + **Verifier guidance** below. (The stale original Fix/Change-sketch fields were removed in the live re-audit cleanup.)

- [x] **shipped**
- **Canonical scope:** Implement the corrected scope in **Verifier guidance**. Treat the superseded original fix/sketch/test mapping as historical context, not instructions.
- **Canonical verification:** Use the Q10/test instructions in **Verifier guidance**; if they conflict with any superseded original field, Verifier guidance wins.
- **Anchors:** `src/core/mission/queue.rs::score_queue_spill_candidate`, `src/core/mission/channels.rs::queue_completed_has_terminal_success_proof`
- **Problem:** score_queue_spill_candidate ranks only on structure and never reads failure history, so a repeatedly failed-and-released task scores like a fresh one. Failure evidence is durable: each failed transition writes ctox_core_transition_proofs to_state Failed failure_class queue_route_failure (channels.rs:7658-7663); last_error is useless because set_routing_status nulls it on every non-failed transition.
- **Risk:** Cap with min(count,3) so an ancient task is not pinned permanently.
- **Verifier guidance:** Real, compliant, not-already-handled gap — but the proposed change as written overstates what the count measures, so revise rather than keep. Defect: proof_id = SHA256(request_json) with ON CONFLICT(proof_id) DO UPDATE (core_transition_guard.rs:173,184,586-590), and CoreTransitionRequest (core_state_machine.rs:242-253) carries NO timestamp/attempt-nonce — only entity_type/entity_id/lane/from_state/to_state/event/actor/evidence/metadata. The failure_reason lives in metadata (channels.rs:7659). Therefore N repeated failures with the SAME (from_state, actor, failure_reason) collapse into ONE proof row; the count never exceeds 1 for an identical-reason retry loop. The proposed 'min(count,3)*3' and the test 'a key with 2 Failed proofs' only hold if each failure carries a DISTINCT reason string — which a real same-error retry loop does not produce. Corrected/tightened version: (1) Rename the signal honestly — it is 'distinct durable failure signatures', i.e. COUNT(DISTINCT request_json) of accepted to_state='Failed' rows, not 'failure count'. (2) Either accept that semantic and weight it modestly (e.g. +2 when count>=1, +3 when count>=2, capped), with a reason string that says 'has prior durable failure evidence' rather than implying a precise retry tally; OR, if a true attempt tally is wanted, that requires a separate durable per-attempt counter and is OUT OF SCOPE for this read-only hardening (do not add it here — it would touch the proof-write path). (3) The test must therefore seed TWO proofs with DIFFERENT failure_reason metadata to get count=2, and should also include a guard test asserting that two same-reason failures yield count=1 — documenting the collision so a future reader does not assume it counts attempts. (4) Keep the min(count,3) cap as proposed so an old failure does not pin a task permanently. Net: keep the idea (feed accepted Failed-proof evidence into the scorer, deterministic, rides the proof table), fix the measurement framing and the test.
- **Grounding caveat:** All anchors and claims verified in real code. score_queue_spill_candidate (queue.rs:2082-2184) reads only priority/route_status/workspace_root/suggested_skill/parent_message_key — no failure history. queue_completed_has_terminal_success_proof (channels.rs:7687) is the real mirror pattern. The Failed proof write with failure_class='queue_route_failure' exists at channels.rs:7658-7663. last_error non-durability is accurate: set_routing_status (channels.rs:7585-7600) only writes failure_note when route_status=='failed'; release_stale_queue_task_leases nulls it (2728). The Pending->Failed->Pending re-failure cycle is reachable: allowed_transition_catalog has (Failed, Pending) at core_state_machine.rs:1068, so a failed-and-released task does re-enter the scorer as 'pending' (queue.rs:2062 lists pending+blocked).

Unlike `ensure_queue_guard_locked` — which DOES record a 'queue_pressure_guard' governance event when it inserts a guard slice — this separate early-return records nothing. - **Risk:** Low. Additive audit only; idempotence key bounds row volume.
- **Verifier guidance:** Substance is correct (grounded, compliant, not already-handled) but two parts of the proposal are wrong and must be tightened before keep:

1. TEST IS INCORRECT AS WRITTEN. "Push 20 pending prompts and assert the governance row" will NOT reach 9034. With busy=false and no dispatch gate, maybe_take_next_queued_prompt_for_idle_dispatch (9030) pops and dispatches a prompt via maybe_start_next_queued_prompt_locked (10000) and returns at 9032 — 9034 is never hit, and pending drops below 20. To exercise 9034 the test must ALSO establish a deferral gate so dispatch returns None while pending stays >=20: set a working-hours hold (working_hours::hold_reason at 9991) or a runtime-blocker backoff (runtime_blocker_backoff_remaining_secs at 10032) — written to the test root's SQLite runtime store (NOT std::env, per constraints), then call route_external_messages and assert exactly one "queue_pressure_router_skip" row. Re-running the tick within the same 300s bucket must assert no second row (idempotency).

2. REGISTER THE NEW MECHANISM. The changeSketch omits adding "queue_pressure_router_skip" to governance::DEFAULT_MECHANISMS (governance.rs:89-283). record_event will persist the row regardless (no FK on mechanism_id), so the Process-Mining evidence goal is met — but every existing survival/safety mechanism is registered there, and render_prompt_block (417) only surfaces registered mechanisms. For consistency add a DefaultMechanism entry (mechanism_class:"survival", autonomy:"autonomous_queue_containment", module_hint:"src/service.rs") so the new audit mechanism appears in the governance inventory like its sibling queue_pressure_guard.

3. SCOPE NOTE (keep as-is): keep the early-return semantics byte-identical and place the record_event call immediately before `return Ok(())` at 9035. Do not add a push_event-only path — the whole value is the DURABLE governance row, since the in-memory event ring is capped at 24 (14075) and is not Process-Mining evidence. With these three corrections the finding is a clean keep-grade hardening.
- **Grounding caveat:** All three anchors exist and the weakness is real. service.rs:9034 is a bare `if queue_pressure_active(state) { return Ok(()) }` with no push_event/governance write, sitting before durable-lease (9037), workflow-materialize (9046), ticket-self-work (9065), founder-repair (9075), scheduled-emit (9100) and inbound leasing. queue_pressure_active (14081) = pending_prompts.len() >= QUEUE_PRESSURE_GUARD_THRESHOLD(=20, line 112). ensure_queue_guard_locked (14155) DOES record a governance::record_event "queue_pressure_guard" (14175-14188) — but only at ENQUEUE sites (2112, 9881), not on the router tick, and it describes a different action (inserting a guard slice), not the per-tick router-stage skip. I confirmed the 9034 early-return is genuinely REACHABLE under sustained pressure: maybe_take_next_queued_prompt_for_idle_dispatch (9463) returns None while busy=false when dispatch is gated by working-hours hold (9991), runtime-blocker backoff (10032), or outcome-recovery-pending (10022) — in each case pending stays >=20 (nothing popped at 10000), control falls through to 9034 and returns silently. So under blocker+pressure the router stops repairing founder comms / materializing workflow steps every tick with zero new audit signal. Claim holds.

The closure already needs `root` captured, which is in scope. (3) Test must write to the test SQLite root (not std::env) and prove an event surfaces through `governance::list_recent_events` (the JOIN read path), not merely that a row was inserted — otherwise the test passes while mining stays blind.
- **Grounding caveat:** All three anchors exist and the weakness is real. `route_external_messages` is at service.rs:9006; the `log_ack_failure` closure at service.rs:9359-9367 only `eprintln!`s (body confirmed at 9361-9365) — no durable row. The documented past-regression comment is at service.rs:9354-9358 exactly as quoted. `channels::ack_leased_messages_with_reason` exists at channels.rs:2196; `governance::record_event` at governance.rs:326 and already supports `idempotence_key` dedupe (governance.rs:362-383). The four ack call sites (9369/9378/9387/9396) each route through `log_ack_failure`, so a re-emergent ack-reject loop is currently stderr-only.

(4) Q10 test: a completed skill-bound queue/internal-work job writes a work.outcome flow event whose metadata.skill == job.suggested_skill and metadata.agent_outcome == 'success'; a failed one writes the failure outcome. Effort is M-to-L (new event kind + emission + aggregation + test), not the trivial 'additive metadata' the sketch implies. Keep the determinism split as stated: the per-skill failure-rate is deterministic; the skill-repair decision stays human/skill-lifecycle judgement (no auto-disable).
- **Grounding caveat:** Anchors exist and the underlying weakness is real. process_mining.rs:3577-3602 maps ctox_skill_bundles/ctox_skill_files as static registry telemetry (records_runtime_skill_registry:true); process_mining.rs:3975 maps ctox_harness_flow_events itself only as static telemetry — nothing joins skill to a task pass/fail. The OTEL claim holds: emit_skill_injected_metric (skills/injection.rs:91) and track_skill_invocations (analytics_client.rs:380) live in the Codex harness, external to durable SQLite. RecordHarnessFlowEventRequest exists with a free metadata:Value (harness_flow.rs:101-110). BUT the finding's mechanism claim is FALSE: it says to stamp suggested_skill onto 'the EXISTING completion/failure harness-flow events' that 'already have job.suggested_skill in scope' at service.rs ~3399. I read service.rs 3360-3600: the outcome-classification site emits ZERO record_harness_flow_event calls — it classifies agent_outcome, writes messages.agent_outcome, bumps a failure counter, runs completion review. The only harness-flow event kinds that exist (queue.cleanup_scope/spilled/restored, knowledge.loaded, ticket.self_work_*, review.approved/no_send) are lifecycle events in queue.rs/tickets.rs/channels.rs, none is a per-task pass/fail outcome, and none sits at the cited service.rs site. The skill-to-outcome problem is genuine; the 'just add a metadata field to an existing event' framing is not.

🏷 Pass 1 · impact **medium** · effort **S** · verifier **revise**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** ⚠️ **REVISE — implement only the Verifier-guidance scope** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **clear** — The core claim is grounded: validate_terminal_failure_gate (core_state_machine.rs:403) only enforces a durable failure_reason/failure_class on to_state==Failed for QueueItem/WorkItem/Ticket, while three failure-shaped terminals in the hi...

> ⚠️ **Canonical issue:** implement the **Canonical scope** + **Verifier guidance** below. (The stale original Fix/Change-sketch fields were removed in the live re-audit cleanup.)

- [x] **shipped**
- **Canonical scope:** Implement the corrected scope in **Verifier guidance**. Treat the superseded original fix/sketch/test mapping as historical context, not instructions.
- **Canonical verification:** Use the Q10/test instructions in **Verifier guidance**; if they conflict with any superseded original field, Verifier guidance wins.
- **Anchors:** `src/core/service/core_state_machine.rs::validate_terminal_failure_gate (line 403, entity guard restricts to QueueItem|WorkItem|Ticket)`, `src/core/service/core_state_machine.rs::allowed_transition_catalog (Commitment AtRisk->Escalated line ~1179; FounderCommunication Sending->SendFailed line ~1161)`, `src/core/service/core_state_machine.rs::core_terminal_states (Commitment terminal Escalated; FounderCommunication terminal Escalated, line 1234)`
- **Problem:** validate_terminal_failure_gate forces a durable failure_reason+failure_class only for QueueItem/WorkItem/Ticket moving to Failed. But Commitment->Escalated and FounderCommunication->Escalated are terminal states that represent failure outcomes (a missed deadline, an abandoned founder reply), and FounderCommunication->SendFailed is a delivery failure, yet none of these require any durable reason/class. For owner/founder-protected and commitment lanes — the highest-priority lanes — a failure can terminate with no auditable cause, which is exactly the kind of un-evidenced terminal the gate was built to prevent.
- **Risk:** Existing callers that drive Escalated/SendFailed may not yet pass these keys, so this can break a live path; stage by first auditing the real callsites (channels.rs/approval_nag.rs) and adding the metadata there, then enabling the gate, each behind its own test.
- **Verifier guidance:** Real, compliant, ungated — keep the intent but TIGHTEN the changeSketch; as written it would reject the one live caller. Findings from the producers (verified by repo-wide grep for `to_state: CoreState::Escalated|SendFailed`): (1) The ONLY production producer of any of these three terminals is the FounderCommunication Sending->SendFailed emitter at channels.rs:5613 (emit_reviewed_founder_send_failed_transition). It already writes a durable cause into metadata as `provider_error` (line 5632-5635, clipped to 500 chars) but does NOT set `failure_reason`/`failure_class`. So requiring brand-new keys `failure_reason`+`failure_class` on SendFailed would immediately reject this live, kernel-witnessed path. (2) There is currently NO production producer of Commitment->Escalated or FounderCommunication->Escalated anywhere in src — those transitions exist in the catalog but nothing drives them yet; the gate there is purely preventive. approval_nag.rs (which the risk_note names) does not produce any Escalated transition — its only enforce_core_transition drives QueueItem->Blocked (line 682), so that callsite reference in the risk note is wrong.

Corrected, tighter proposal:
- SendFailed branch: accept the durable cause the producer ALREADY emits. Require a non-empty cause that is satisfied by ANY of {metadata `failure_reason`, metadata `provider_error`, evidence.escalation_id}. Do NOT mandate `failure_class` for SendFailed (the live caller has no class concept; mandating it breaks channels.rs:5637 with zero added safety since provider_error is already present). If you want class parity, add `failure_class` defaulting at the channels.rs:5623 metadata block in the SAME commit and add the gate after — never gate-first.
- Commitment->Escalated and FounderCommunication->Escalated: since there is no live producer, the gate is safe to add now and is genuinely preventive. Require a non-empty cause satisfied by {evidence.escalation_id OR metadata failure_reason}. escalation_id is the natural key here (an escalation terminal should reference the escalation it raised) and reuses the existing field at line 233.
- Keep the P3Housekeeping exemption pattern (line 416) for symmetry, though these protected lanes are never P3.
- Tests (write to the SQLite runtime store, not std::env): (a) Commitment AtRisk->Escalated with empty evidence/metadata is REJECTED; with escalation_id is ACCEPTED. (b) FounderCommunication Sending->SendFailed with neither failure_reason nor provider_error nor escalation_id is REJECTED; the existing channels.rs payload carrying provider_error is ACCEPTED (this is the regression-guard that the live path still passes). (c) FounderCommunication ReplyNeeded->Escalated with escalation_id ACCEPTED, without REJECTED.

Net: medium-impact, S effort, low real-world risk if SendFailed accepts provider_error/escalation_id rather than demanding new keys. The finding's own risk_note flags the staging concern correctly but mis-identifies provider_error as the existing cause key and mis-names approval_nag.rs as the SendFailed callsite — fix those in the writeup.
- **Grounding caveat:** Re-opened the code. validate_terminal_failure_gate exists at core_state_machine.rs:403 and gates ONLY when to_state == CoreState::Failed (line 407) AND entity_type in {QueueItem, WorkItem, Ticket} (lines 410-415). CoreState::Failed (line 68), CoreState::SendFailed (line 96) and CoreState::Escalated (line 100) are three DISTINCT enum variants, so the gate provably never fires for SendFailed/Escalated. Anchors verified: Commitment AtRisk->Escalated at line 1179; FounderCommunication Sending->SendFailed at line 1161; FounderCommunication terminal {Done, Escalated} at line 1246 (finding said 1234 — that is the fn signature, a minor off-by-12 anchor imprecision, not a fabrication); Commitment terminal {Delivered, Escalated, CancelledWithNotice} at line 1247. These failure-shaped terminals carry no kernel-enforced durable failure reason. Claim holds.

### `turn-loop-context` · `turnloop-4` — Exact-token overflow preflight is a silent no-op for API runtimes, leaving rendered-prompt overflow ungated there

🏷 Pass 1 · impact **medium** · effort **M** · verifier **revise**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** ⚠️ **REVISE — implement only the Verifier-guidance scope** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **clear** — Every anchor and behavioral claim is verified in live code: the exact-overflow preflight is a hard guard that silently breaks for API (is_local()==false → Ok(None)), so ctox_core_api turns get NO deterministic pre-invocation overflow gat...

> ⚠️ **Canonical issue:** implement the **Canonical scope** + **Verifier guidance** below. (The stale original Fix/Change-sketch fields were removed in the live re-audit cleanup.)

- [x] **shipped**
- **Canonical scope:** Implement the corrected scope in **Verifier guidance**. Treat the superseded original fix/sketch/test mapping as historical context, not instructions.
- **Canonical verification:** Use the Q10/test instructions in **Verifier guidance**; if they conflict with any superseded original field, Verifier guidance wins.
- **Anchors:** `src/core/execution/agent/turn_loop.rs:528`, `src/core/execution/agent/direct_session.rs::exact_prompt_token_count`, `src/core/execution/agent/direct_session.rs::exact_prompt_safe_input_budget`
- **Problem:** The hard, deterministic overflow guard in the turn loop (turn_loop.rs:528-631) depends on direct_session::exact_prompt_token_count, which returns Ok(None) for any non-local runtime (direct_session.rs:95: `if !kernel.state.source.is_local() { return Ok(None) }`). The loop's first iteration then hits `let Some(count) = ... else { break };` and the entire exact preflight + compaction-retry-until-fit machinery is skipped for ctox_core_api sessions. API turns therefore rely solely on the heuristic build_turn_plan compaction decision; an over-budget rendered prompt is only discovered when the upstream returns an overflow error mid-turn, after the lease is held and tokens are spent. The determinism split says terminal/overflow gates must be deterministic — this one is deterministic only for local.
- **Risk:** Medium. A heuristic count for API risks false overflow bails if the estimate is too aggressive; mitigate by reusing the SAME estimator build_turn_plan already trusts and keeping the existing safe-budget ratio. Behavior for local is unchanged.
- **Verifier guidance:** Problem is real; the proposed change is wrong in two ways. (1) Semantic lie: it returns a chars/4 heuristic from a function named exact_prompt_token_count / struct ExactPromptTokenCount, while the audit emit ('exact-token-preflight ... source={}') and both bail strings say 'exact rendered prompt tokens'. A guess presented as exact, gated at the tight 3/4 safe budget (NUMERATOR=3/DENOMINATOR=4, direct_session.rs:57-58), can fire FALSE-POSITIVE HARD overflow bails on API turns where the prompt actually fits. (2) The bail string is NOT in the cooldown classifier (turn_loop.rs:1194-1254), so on API a false positive becomes an UNCLASSIFIED hard failure with no retry, not the graceful classify/cooldown the pruefsatz claims. Tighter corrected version: do NOT overload exact_prompt_token_count. Instead add a separate, explicitly-named heuristic preflight for the non-local branch — e.g. heuristic_prompt_token_estimate() returning a distinct struct with source 'heuristic-api' and an emit phase 'heuristic-token-preflight' (not 'exact-token-preflight'), and use a LOOSER safe-budget ratio for the heuristic path (e.g. estimate must exceed context_limit outright, or use a generous fraction like 95-100%) so it only catches gross overflow the heuristic is actually confident about, never trimming prompts that merely look big. Reuse lcm::estimate_tokens (chars.div_ceil(4), lcm.rs:5924) over base_instructions+rendered prompt so the system prompt is included — that is the genuine gap. Keep the local /tokenize path authoritative and unchanged. Add the heuristic bail string ('context_preflight_heuristic_overflow' or similar) to hard_runtime_blocker_retry_cooldown_secs so a false positive degrades to a bounded cooldown-retry, not an unclassified crash. Q10 test: API runtime with a grossly-over-budget rendered prompt triggers the heuristic overflow bail; an API prompt that is merely large-but-fits does NOT bail (false-positive guard test).
- **Grounding caveat:** All anchors verified. turn_loop.rs:528 is the `for exact_preflight_round in 0..=2` loop; lines 533-536 break immediately when exact_prompt_token_count returns None. direct_session.rs:89-97 confirms exact_prompt_token_count returns Ok(None) for `!kernel.state.source.is_local()` (line 95-97), so the entire 528-631 exact-preflight + compaction-retry machinery is skipped for ctox_core_api. exact_prompt_safe_input_budget at direct_session.rs:78 exists (ratio 3/4). The only remaining pre-invocation gate for API is build_turn_plan -> evaluate_compaction (lcm.rs:1166) -> context_token_count (lcm.rs:3053), which counts stored conversation content only, NOT base_instructions+rendered prompt. The in-loop comment (turn_loop.rs:517-521) explicitly states the worker system prompt is several thousand tokens and must be counted. Gap is real.



## 🔵 DEFER — grounded but audit/cosmetic, no hardening payoff (25)

### `governance-recovery` · `govrec-2` — Boot stale-lease reclaim writes no governance event — crash recovery is invisible to audit/process-mining

🏷 Pass 1 · impact **high** · effort **S** · verifier **keep**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** 🔵 **DEFER — audit/cosmetic, not hardening** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **marginal** — The finding is genuinely grounded: the boot-only communication-route reclaim (communication_routing_state, reclaimed only by the boot path, not by the periodic reconcile) records no governance event, while the structurally analogous peri...

- [x] **shipped**
- **Anchors:** `src/core/service/service.rs::release_stale_service_communication_leases_on_boot`, `src/core/service/service.rs::release_stale_service_communication_leases`, `src/core/service/service.rs::reconcile_ticket_runtime_state`
- **Problem:** On every restart, release_stale_service_communication_leases_on_boot (service.rs:1268) flips orphaned 'leased' communication routes back to 'pending' (the core crash-recovery path for a daemon that died mid-turn) but only calls push_event — it records NO governance event. The structurally identical periodic reconcile (reconcile_ticket_runtime_state, service.rs:9566) DOES emit a 'ticket_reconciliation' governance event for the same kind of reclaim. So a crash that stranded N leased work items, then got auto-reclaimed at boot, leaves zero durable audit/process-mining evidence — exactly the restart scenario where you most want it. The boot state-invariant check right next to it (service.rs:816) is fully audited, making the gap an inconsistency, not a design choice.
- **Fix:** Add a governance::record_event on the boot reclaim path, mirroring the existing ticket_reconciliation event shape, so crash-recovery lease reclaims are durably auditable and surface in the governance prompt block and process-mining.
- **Change sketch:** In release_stale_service_communication_leases_on_boot, on Ok(count) where count>0, call governance::record_event with mechanism_id 'ticket_reconciliation' (already registered) or a new 'boot_lease_recovery' mechanism, severity 'info', reason 'stale service communication leases survived a restart', action_taken 'released orphaned boot leases back to pending', details {released_count}, idempotence_key keyed on a boot epoch so each boot reclaim is one event. The function already returns the count; just thread root (already in scope) into record_event.
- **Prüfsatz:** Q1 hardens release_stale_service_communication_leases_on_boot; Q4 the state transition (leased→pending) already flows through enforce_queue_route_status_transition, only its audit is added; Q9 adds the missing Audit/Process-Mining evidence; Q10 a test asserting a governance row after a seeded stale-lease boot pins it. Rides the existing record_event + enforce_queue_route_status_transition path, no new mechanism required.
- **Risk:** Very low. Pure additive audit write; the lease transition itself is unchanged. Use a per-boot idempotence key to avoid event spam on repeated boots with the same stranded keys.
- **Verifier guidance:** Keep as-is with one design refinement on the idempotence key. The finding offers either reusing 'ticket_reconciliation' or a new 'boot_lease_recovery' mechanism; reuse is simplest and 'ticket_reconciliation' is already registered (governance.rs:243), so no DEFAULT_MECHANISMS change is needed. For the idempotence_key, prefer a captured boot timestamp (now_iso_string() at reclaim time) over the content-hash pattern the periodic reconcile uses (normalize_token of joined keys, service.rs:9562). Reason: a content-based key would cross-boot dedupe whenever the SAME message_keys get stranded again (e.g. a crash loop on the same item), silently swallowing the very repeat-crash signal you want visible; a per-boot timestamp key gives exactly one event per boot reclaim. Concretely: on Ok(count) where count>0 in release_stale_service_communication_leases_on_boot, call governance::record_event(root, GovernanceEventRequest{ mechanism_id:'ticket_reconciliation', conversation_id:None, severity:'info', reason:'leased service communication routes survived a daemon restart with no active worker', action_taken:'released orphaned boot communication leases back to pending', details: json!({\"released_count\": count}), idempotence_key: Some(&boot_ts) }). root is already in scope at the call site (service.rs:717) but NOT inside release_stale_service_communication_leases_on_boot's body for the event — thread it: the on_boot fn already receives root (param at 1269), so the call is in scope. Q10 test: extend or add alongside boot_releases_stale_service_communication_leases to assert a governance_events row with mechanism_id='ticket_reconciliation' (or the chosen id) exists after the seeded stale-lease reclaim; the test writes only to the temp_root SQLite store, no std::env.
- **Grounding caveat:** All three anchors verified. release_stale_service_communication_leases_on_boot (service.rs:1268-1283) calls only push_event on Ok(count) — no governance::record_event. release_stale_service_communication_leases (service.rs:1285) does the leased->pending flip through enforce_queue_route_status_transition. The structurally identical periodic reconcile_ticket_runtime_state (service.rs:9545) DOES emit mechanism_id 'ticket_reconciliation' governance events at 9566/9598/9625 for the same reclaim. The adjacent boot state-invariant check (816/860/891/939) is fully audited. ticket_reconciliation is a real registered DEFAULT_MECHANISM (governance.rs:243). The audit asymmetry is genuine.

The struct CompletionReviewRequest (review.rs:121-143) has NO field for the bound skill. build_review_prompt (review.rs:806-1104) renders only "Review skill: {review_skill_path}" at line 1015. Crucially, the asymmetry is confirmed at the executor edge: service.rs:3378 passes job.suggested_skill.as_deref() as a distinct out-of-band parameter to run_chat_turn_with_events_extended_guarded, NOT embedded in execution_prompt — so the bound skill does not leak into task_prompt/task_goal and genuinely never reaches the reviewer.
