🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** 🔵 **DEFER — audit/cosmetic, not hardening** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **marginal** — Grounded and accurate: the byte-identical triplication of a 6-line trimmed-non-empty string extractor across service/channels/tickets is real, no divergent overload exists, and the three copies do parse the same durable metadata keys (ti...

- [ ] **open**
- **Anchors:** `src/core/service/service.rs::metadata_string (10248) + metadata_string_list (10257)`, `src/core/mission/channels.rs::metadata_string_value (2418)`, `src/core/mission/tickets.rs::metadata_string_value (2951)`, `src/core/mission/mod.rs (1-18, module home)`
- **Problem:** The same trimmed-non-empty JSON-string extractor exists as three byte-identical private copies — metadata_string (service.rs) and metadata_string_value (channels.rs, tickets.rs) — feeding ~65 call sites (25 in service.rs, 7 in channels.rs, 33 in tickets.rs). These three files all parse the SAME durable metadata_json blobs (workflow_*, dedupe_key, thread_key, inbound_message_key) that cross the channel/ticket/service boundary, so a future tweak to trimming/empty-handling in one copy silently diverges the others — the exact stringly-typed cross-file drift the metadata keys already risk. This is a pure behavior-preserving dedup target.
- **Fix:** Hoist one canonical pub(crate) metadata_string(+_list) into a small mission util module and re-point all three modules at it, so metadata parsing semantics are single-sourced across the boundary.
- **Change sketch:** Add `pub(crate) mod metadata_util;` to src/core/mission/mod.rs with metadata_string / metadata_string_list. Replace the three local definitions with `use crate::mission::metadata_util::metadata_string as metadata_string_value;` (alias to preserve local names) and drop the duplicate bodies. No call-site edits, no behavior change.
- **Prüfsatz:** Hardens the metadata-parsing helpers that feed enforce_queue_task_spawn / workflow predecessor reads / render_ticket_self_work_prompt. route_external_messages unaffected. No work/status/spawn path changes — pure helper consolidation. Hard keys only (still reads explicit metadata keys). No semantic-equality change. Evidence: existing tests across the three modules continue to pass unchanged. Test: a single unit test in metadata_util pins trim/empty-array/non-string behavior so all three modules share one proven contract.
- **Risk:** Visibility: the canonical fn must be pub(crate); keeping local aliases avoids touching 65 call sites. Confirm no module defines a subtly different overload before aliasing.
- **Verifier guidance:** Keep. Two small precisions to the changeSketch (not defects): (1) service.rs already uses the name `metadata_string`, so its alias is a plain `use crate::mission::metadata_util::metadata_string;` (no rename); only channels.rs/tickets.rs need `as metadata_string_value`. (2) Only the single-value extractor is actually triplicated — metadata_string_list has just one (service.rs) caller, so the dedup *necessity* is the single-value fn; hoisting _list alongside is fine for single-sourcing the list variant but is optional. Risk note in finding is correct (must be pub(crate), keep local aliases to avoid touching ~65 call sites, confirm no divergent overload — verified none exists).
- **Grounding caveat:** Confirmed all four anchors by direct Read: service.rs:10248 metadata_string + :10257 metadata_string_list; channels.rs:2418 metadata_string_value; tickets.rs:2951 metadata_string_value. The three single-value extractors are byte-identical (get->as_str->trim->filter non-empty->owned). grep confirms no fifth/divergent overload in src/core/. All four are private (no pub). They parse the same durable metadata_json keys crossing channel/ticket/service (ticket_self_work_id, business_os_command_id, skill, workspace_root, core_run_class), so a trim/empty-handling tweak in one copy silently diverges the others. Real drift risk now.


### `egress-idempotency` · `EGRESS-3` — require_reviewed_outbound body/recipient hash gate is a tautology: both sides derived from the same request value

🏷 Pass 2 · impact **medium** · effort **M** · kind **bug** · verifier **keep**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** 🔵 **DEFER — audit/cosmetic, not hardening** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **marginal** — Exceptionally well-grounded and honest ticket: every anchor, symbol, line range, schema claim, and fix-availability claim matches live code exactly (only line numbers drifted ~6-20 lines). The tautology is real — both evidence fields com...

- [ ] **open**
- **Anchors:** `src/core/service/core_state_machine.rs::require_reviewed_outbound (907-957)`, `src/core/mission/channels.rs::enforce_reviewed_founder_send_core_transition (5431-5455)`, `src/core/mission/channels.rs::emit_reviewed_founder_send_failed_transition (5621-5652)`, `src/core/mission/channels.rs::require_any_unconsumed_founder_outbound_review (5027-5053)`
- **Problem:** require_reviewed_outbound is the kernel gate that is supposed to prove the reviewed body == the outgoing body (founder_send_body_hash_mismatch) and reviewed recipients == outgoing recipients. But every caller fills both evidence fields from the same source: enforce_reviewed_founder_send_core_transition computes one body_sha256 = sha256(request.body) and assigns it to BOTH approved_body_sha256 and outgoing_body_sha256 (channels.rs:5451-5452), same for the recipient set (5453-5454); the failure twin does the same (5649-5652). The comparison can therefore never fail. The actual body binding is enforced elsewhere - require_any_unconsumed_founder_outbound_review looks up the approval by action_digest which embeds the body hash (founder_outbound_review_digest, channels.rs:4585-4590) - so the line is held, but the kernel evidence check provides false defense-in-depth: a future caller that fetches the approval_key but mutates request.body before the transition would still pass the kernel gate.
- **Fix:** Make the kernel check load-bearing by sourcing approved_body_sha256 from the durable review approval record (communication_founder_reply_reviews body hash for the matched approval_key) and outgoing_body_sha256 from the request actually being sent, so the two are independent. This hardens the existing require_reviewed_outbound gate without changing the data plane.
- **Change sketch:** require_any_unconsumed_founder_outbound_review already has the approval row; return its stored body_sha256/recipient_set hash alongside approval_key. In enforce_reviewed_founder_send_core_transition set approved_*_sha256 from the approval record and outgoing_*_sha256 from request, so require_reviewed_outbound compares two genuinely-independent values.
- **Prüfsatz:** (1) hardens require_reviewed_outbound + enforce_reviewed_founder_send_core_transition; (2) hot path unchanged; (3) no new work item; (4) strengthens the existing Approved->Sending kernel transition; (5) no spawn; (6) same entity; (7) hard-key sha256 equality only - exactly the allowed deterministic case; (8) skills unaffected; (9) makes the kernel evidence comparison meaningful audit evidence rather than a no-op; (10) test: feed a transition whose request.body differs from the approval-record body and assert founder_send_body_hash_mismatch now fires (today it cannot).
- **Risk:** Low-medium; the approval record must reliably carry the approved body hash. Since the approval is found by action_digest (which already contains that hash), the value is available; main care is that the two computations use identical normalization (trim) so legitimate sends are not falsely rejected.
- **Verifier guidance:** Confirmed real and well-scoped. The changeSketch is implementable as-is: the durable body_sha256 already lives on communication_founder_reply_reviews (channels.rs:6214, written at 4525), so require_any_unconsumed_founder_outbound_review (5027-5053) only needs to add body_sha256 (and recipient hash) to its SELECT and return it alongside approval_key. Then enforce_reviewed_founder_send_core_transition sources approved_*_sha256 from the approval row and outgoing_*_sha256 from the live request, making the kernel comparison genuinely independent. Two refinements for the implementer: (1) the same helper is reused by enforce_reviewed_communication_send_core_transition_if_approved (5408) and the failure twin (5613) — thread the approval-record hash through all three so none re-derives both sides; (2) recipient set: the review row stores action_json (which contains to/cc) not a precomputed recipient-set hash, so the approved recipient hash must be derived from the stored action_json, not recomputed from the live request — otherwise it stays a tautology. Normalization (trim) must match founder_send_recipient_set_sha256 to avoid false rejects of legitimate sends. Impact medium is fair: today the line holds via the digest, so this is auditability/defense-in-depth hardening that closes a real future-caller gap, with a test that currently cannot fail being made able to fail.
- **Grounding caveat:** All four anchors verified. require_reviewed_outbound (core_state_machine.rs:907-957) compares evidence.approved_body_sha256 vs evidence.outgoing_body_sha256 (934) and approved/outgoing recipient hashes (951). enforce_reviewed_founder_send_core_transition (channels.rs:5431) computes ONE body_sha256 = sha256(request.body.trim()) and assigns it to BOTH approved_body_sha256 and outgoing_body_sha256 (5451-5452), same recipient set (5453-5454). Failure twin emit_reviewed_founder_send_failed_transition does the same (5649-5652). Comparison is value-against-itself: structurally cannot fail. The body binding is currently held by require_any_unconsumed_founder_outbound_review (5027-5053) which looks up by action_digest embedding sha256(body) (founder_outbound_review_digest 4585-4590), so the line holds TODAY — the finding honestly frames this as false defense-in-depth, not a live exploit. The two-step path enforce_reviewed_communication_send_core_transition_if_approved (5408) passes the approval tuple separately from request, which is exactly the future-caller shape that could mutate request.body past the tautological kernel gate.


### `failmode-patterns` · `x2-4` — Dead `terminal_reaped_at` column with zero writers makes the spawn-edge audit lie: always-null field implies reaping is tracked

🏷 Pass 2 · impact **medium** · effort **S** · kind **dead-code** · verifier **keep**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** 🔵 **DEFER — audit/cosmetic, not hardening** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **marginal** — Fully grounded and unusually honest: every anchor exists, the zero-writer claim is true, and the ticket pre-emptively corrects its own one inaccuracy (6611 is a test fixture, not a third production schema). But this is a pure dead-audit-...

- [x] **shipped**
- **Anchors:** `src/core/service/core_transition_guard.rs:121 (terminal_reaped_at TEXT — schema, INSERT-only table; no UPDATE ctox_core_spawn_edges anywhere)`, `src/core/service/process_mining.rs:6611 (mirror schema), :1102/:1128 (SELECTed + surfaced into spawn-edges audit JSON as always null)`, `src/apps/desktop/src/db_reader.rs:1695 (SpawnEdgeRow.terminal_reaped_at), :1921/:1943 (read into desktop reader)`, `grep: zero `terminal_reaped_at =` / `SET terminal_reaped_at` / `UPDATE ctox_core_spawn_edges` writers in the whole tree`
- **Problem:** `ctox_core_spawn_edges` is INSERT-only (no UPDATE statement exists against it), and `terminal_reaped_at` has no writer anywhere. Yet it is declared in three schema definitions, SELECTed in the process-mining `spawn-edges` audit (process_mining.rs:1102) and the desktop db_reader (db_reader.rs:1921), and serialized into the audit JSON (process_mining.rs:1128) and the SpawnEdgeRow struct. The result: every spawn-edge audit/explain output presents `terminal_reaped_at: null` for every row, implying the harness tracks when a spawn edge's terminal was reaped — when in fact reaping is never recorded. This is dead audit state that makes the audit lie by omission: an operator inspecting spawn edges sees a field that can never be anything but null and may conclude no reaping ever occurred, rather than that it is simply untracked.
- **Fix:** Two behavior/persistence-preserving options, both valid under the architecture rule: (a) delete the column from all three schema sites + both readers (zero writers, zero behavior change — the field is structurally always null); or (b) if spawn-edge reaping SHOULD be tracked, wire the existing spawn-reaper to write `terminal_reaped_at` so the audit stops lying. The table is local SQLite, NOT an rxdb-replicated collection (no hits in src/core/rxdb or business-os/rxdb), so the data-plane contracts pipeline does NOT gate this. Recommend (a) for now plus a follow-up to wire reaping if the field is wanted.
- **Change sketch:** Option (a): drop `terminal_reaped_at TEXT` from core_transition_guard.rs:121 and process_mining.rs:6611 (CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS is forward-safe for new roots; for existing DBs the column simply remains unused and unread — acceptable, or add a one-line note), remove it from the two SELECT column lists (process_mining.rs:1102, db_reader.rs:1921), the JSON map (1128), the struct field (db_reader.rs:1695), and the row.get (1943). Since CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS won't alter existing tables, deletion is purely additive-safe; the column lingers harmlessly in old DBs but is no longer surfaced as a lying field.
- **Prüfsatz:** 1) hardens the ctox_core_spawn_edges audit (stops surfacing a never-written field). 2) route_external_messages unaffected. 3) no work-item change. 4) no status change. 5) no spawn behavior change (column was never part of spawn acceptance). 6) review-rework untouched. 7) no semantic equality. 8) skills untouched. 9) makes the spawn-edge audit honest. 10) test: assert the spawn-edges audit output no longer contains a terminal_reaped_at key (or, under option b, that the reaper writes it).
- **Risk:** Low for option (a): not replicated, IF NOT EXISTS keeps old DBs valid. The only constraint to respect is that this is a schema touch — confirm no rxdb contract references it (verified: none).
- **Verifier guidance:** Real, grounded, constraint-compliant dead-column finding. Two framing corrections for the fix, neither a kill: (1) process_mining.rs:6611 is a TEST fixture (inside #[test] fn runtime_housekeeping_tables_have_explicit_telemetry_coverage, line 6540), not a third production schema — so option (a) touches ONE production schema (core_transition_guard.rs:121) + the two readers (process_mining.rs:1102/1128, db_reader.rs:1695/1921/1943); the test fixture at 6611 can keep or drop the column independently. (2) The desktop field is even deader than stated: forensics.rs render_spawn_edges (the only SpawnEdgeRow consumer) never references terminal_reaped_at, so removing it from SpawnEdgeRow/db_reader has zero UI impact. Recommend option (a) as written. Note for completeness: dropping the SELECT'd column at process_mining.rs:1102/db_reader.rs:1921 requires re-indexing the subsequent row.get() positional offsets (the audit map reads request_json at idx 13, created/updated at 14/15, terminal_reaped_at at 16; db_reader reads positionally up to idx 12) — straightforward but must be done carefully or the executor will shift columns. Keep test from pruefsatz item 10: assert the spawn-edges audit output no longer contains a terminal_reaped_at key.
- **Grounding caveat:** Verified all anchors. core_transition_guard.rs:104-122 declares terminal_reaped_at in the production CREATE TABLE; the only INSERT (lines 448-454) omits it and the ON CONFLICT DO UPDATE (455-459) updates only accepted/violation_codes_json/request_json/updated_at — never terminal_reaped_at. Tree-wide grep finds ZERO writers (no `terminal_reaped_at =`, no `SET terminal_reaped_at`, no `UPDATE ctox_core_spawn_edges`). process_mining.rs:1102 SELECTs it and :1128 serializes it into the spawn-edges audit JSON unconditionally → always null. db_reader.rs:1918-1943 reads it into SpawnEdgeRow. So the audit-by-omission claim is real. ONE inaccuracy: the finding calls process_mining.rs:6611 a third 'schema definition' — it is actually a TEST fixture inside #[test] fn runtime_housekeeping_tables_have_explicit_telemetry_coverage (line 6540), not a production schema. Does not invalidate the problem. Bonus: the only SpawnEdgeRow consumer (forensics.rs:336 render_spawn_edges) never references terminal_reaped_at — the desktop field is read but never rendered, strengthening the dead-code claim.

🏷 Pass 1 · impact **medium** · effort **S** · verifier **revise**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** 🔵 **DEFER — audit/cosmetic, not hardening** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **marginal** — Every anchor, line citation, and behavioral claim is accurate against the live code: reset_mission_agent_failure_count (lcm.rs:1848) clears both agent_failure_count and deferred_reason with no governance event, the defer side (service.rs...

> ⚠️ **Canonical issue:** implement the **Canonical scope** + **Verifier guidance** below. (The stale original Fix/Change-sketch fields were removed in the live re-audit cleanup.)

- [x] **shipped** — distinct `agent_failure_recovery` mechanism (governance.rs, class `recovery`) emitted by `record_agent_failure_recovery` (service.rs) only when a deferral is actually cleared. `reset_mission_agent_failure_count` now returns `MissionFailureReset { record, previous_deferred_reason, recovered_at }` (lcm.rs), capturing the pre-reset reason; the emit is idempotence-keyed on the per-recovery `recovered_at` timestamp (the obvious `watcher_trigger_count` is dead — never incremented in production — so it would have collapsed every cycle to one row). Tests pin the once-only `previous_deferred_reason` lifecycle, two distinct recoveries → two rows, a healthy turn → no row (isolated), and conversation scoping. (Adjacent: the pre-existing defer-side key has the same per-cycle collision; tracked separately.)
- **Canonical scope:** Implement the corrected scope in **Verifier guidance**. Treat the superseded original fix/sketch/test mapping as historical context, not instructions.
- **Canonical verification:** Use the Q10/test instructions in **Verifier guidance**; if they conflict with any superseded original field, Verifier guidance wins.
- **Anchors:** `src/core/context/lcm.rs::reset_mission_agent_failure_count`, `src/core/service/service.rs::run_add_assistant_turn`, `src/core/service/service.rs::mission_agent_failure_threshold`
- **Problem:** When agent_failure_count hits the threshold, defer_mission_for_reason records a durable 'agent_failure_threshold' governance event and freezes the mission (is_open=false). But the inverse — recovery — is silent: reset_mission_agent_failure_count (lcm.rs:1848) is called on the next successful turn (service.rs:3484) and clears both agent_failure_count AND deferred_reason (lcm.rs:1856-1858) with NO governance event. So the audit trail shows a mission entering the deferred/blocked state but never shows it leaving: process-mining sees a one-sided deferral with no matching un-defer, breaking the deadlock-recovery evidence chain exactly at the point you want to confirm the loop actually escaped.
- **Risk:** Very low. Additive audit only; the reset semantics are unchanged. Keep the idempotence key turn-scoped so a long-running healthy mission does not re-emit a recovery event every successful turn.
- **Verifier guidance:** Real, grounded, compliant, unhandled — but tighten two things in the proposed change. (1) Mechanism id: do NOT reuse 'agent_failure_threshold'. Its registered description (governance.rs:128) is exclusively the defer direction ('Defers a mission after repeated structured agent failures...'); emitting a severity-'info' recovery under it pollutes the audit registry and makes process-mining pairing ambiguous. Instead add a dedicated mechanism to DEFAULT_MECHANISMS (e.g. mechanism_id 'agent_failure_recovery', mechanism_class 'recovery', module_hint 'src/service.rs', description 'Records that a previously deferred mission recovered after a successful agent turn, clearing the agent-failure deferral and reopening the mission.') so the defer and recover events live under distinct, registry-described mechanisms. record_event auto-upserts mechanisms (governance.rs:331), so registration is the clean route. (2) Signature change is required and must be minimal: reset_mission_agent_failure_count returns the POST-reset record where deferred_reason is already None, so the caller cannot tell a deferral was cleared. Capture the pre-reset deferred_reason inside the fn (it already loads the record at lcm.rs:1852) and return it — simplest is a small struct or tuple (MissionStateRecord, Option<String> previous_deferred_reason), not a bare bool, so the details payload can carry previous_deferred_reason. Only emit the recovery event when previous_deferred_reason.is_some(), NOT on every healthy turn (the else branch at service.rs:3484 fires for every non-failure turn). (3) Idempotence key: the sketch says key on conversation_id+turn, but the defer side keys on conversation_id+failure_count (service.rs:3467-3470). There is no clean 'turn' id in scope at 3484; key on conversation_id alone is wrong (a mission can defer/recover repeatedly). Key on conversation_id + a monotonic recovery counter or conversation_id + previous_deferred_reason + the watcher_trigger_count/timestamp already on the record, so each distinct recovery is one row and a long healthy mission never re-emits. (4) Test belongs where the existing one is (service.rs:24934 area, or a service-level test that drives the else branch), asserting exactly one recovery governance row after defer-then-success and zero recovery rows after a success on a never-deferred mission — and it must write to the test root SQLite store, not env.
- **Grounding caveat:** All anchors verified. reset_mission_agent_failure_count at lcm.rs:1848 clears agent_failure_count (1856) AND deferred_reason (1858) with no governance event; early-return at 1853 only fires when count==0 && deferred_reason.is_none(). defer_mission_for_reason (lcm.rs:1897) IS paired with governance::record_event at service.rs:3451-3472 (mechanism_id 'agent_failure_threshold', severity 'error', idempotence-keyed). The reset call at service.rs:3484 sits in the else branch and emits NO governance event. Confirmed the asymmetry is not covered elsewhere: the persist_mission_state_with clobber guard (lcm.rs:4400-4451) protects only next_slice/done_gate, NOT deferred_reason/mission_status, so the deferred->running transition is genuinely unaudited. The defer->recover audit pair is one-sided as claimed.

### `process-mining-audit` · `pm-5` — No test pins that confirmed findings actually reach the queue-repair prompt or that the watcher records anything

🏷 Pass 1 · impact **medium** · effort **S** · verifier **keep**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** 🔵 **DEFER — audit/cosmetic, not hardening** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **marginal** — Unusually well-researched for a backlog with known hallucinations: every anchor, line number, format string, and behavioral claim is verified against live code, and the "no test references" claim is literally true. But grounded is not th...

- [x] **shipped**
- **Anchors:** `src/core/mission/queue.rs::render_confirmed_harness_findings_block`, `src/core/service/service.rs::harness_audit_tick_once`, `src/core/service/service.rs::start_harness_audit_watcher`
- **Problem:** The entire feedback value of this subsystem rests on render_confirmed_harness_findings_block injecting confirmed findings into the queue-repair prompt, and on harness_audit_tick_once producing those confirmed rows. findings.rs has unit tests for the lifecycle, but there is NO test proving the integration invariant: 'a seeded confirmed finding appears verbatim in the queue-repair prompt block' and 'two audit ticks over a seeded breach yield a status=confirmed row'. The block also silently returns String::new() on any error (table missing, read fails), so a regression that breaks the read would be invisible — the prompt just quietly loses the findings section with no test catching it. This is an un-pinned, load-bearing invariant.
- **Fix:** Pin the existing feedback path with a test that drives the real functions: seed a finding via record_or_confirm twice (→confirmed), call render_confirmed_harness_findings_block against the same root, assert the finding_id/kind/severity appear in the returned string. This hardens the existing path with no code change beyond test-only construction.
- **Change sketch:** Add a test module next to render_confirmed_harness_findings_block (or in findings tests) that opens an in-root sqlite, runs ensure_findings_schema + two record_or_confirm calls, then asserts the rendered block contains the [severity] kind :: id substring. Use a temp root and write to its runtime/ctox.sqlite3 (per the SQLite-runtime-store test rule, never std::env).
- **Prüfsatz:** Q1 hardens render_confirmed_harness_findings_block + the audit-tick→prompt contract. Q3: confirms findings flow into the queue-repair work item, not a side channel. Q9/Q10: the test IS the Q10 proof that the Q9 evidence reaches a consumer. Q6: repair stays the same queue-repair work item; no new spawn.
- **Risk:** Low — test-only; cannot regress runtime. Pure invariant pinning.
- **Verifier guidance:** Keep as-is. Two small implementer notes that tighten it without broadening scope: (1) the test must std::fs::create_dir_all the runtime/ parent of crate::paths::core_db(root) before opening the write connection — Connection::open creates the file but not parent dirs, and the existing temp_root tests only create the root itself. (2) The highest-value assertion is that the rendered string is NON-EMPTY and contains the '[severity] kind :: id' substring after two record_or_confirm calls + render against the same root — that single assertion simultaneously pins the format contract AND guards the silent-String::new() regression that is the real load-bearing risk. Place the test in queue.rs's existing tests module (use super::* already grants access to the private render fn) rather than findings.rs, since render_confirmed_harness_findings_block lives in queue.rs.
- **Grounding caveat:** All three anchors exist and the weakness is real. render_confirmed_harness_findings_block is at src/core/mission/queue.rs:1207 and silently returns String::new() on every error path (lines 1216 open-fail, 1226 table-missing, 1231 list-fail, 1234 empty) — confirmed. 🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** 🔵 **DEFER — audit/cosmetic, not hardening** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **marginal** — Anchors and the described asymmetry are all real and the change is feasible exactly as sketched — but this is a prompt-enrichment, not a robustness fix. By the ticket's own admission it is "purely additive prompt context"; it adds one re...

- [x] **shipped** — the worker's declared skill is threaded into the review request: `CompletionReviewRequest.bound_skill: Option<String>` (review.rs:143) is populated from `job.suggested_skill` in `run_completion_review` (service.rs:5450) and rendered as `Executor bound skill: {skill}` in `build_review_prompt` (review.rs:1026), with test `build_review_prompt_renders_executor_bound_skill` (review.rs:2100) asserting present-when-set / `(none recorded)`-when-None. - **Anchors:** `src/core/service/service.rs:4941`, `src/core/mission/review.rs::CompletionReviewRequest`, `src/core/mission/review.rs::build_review_prompt`, `src/core/service/service.rs::QueuedPrompt`
- **Problem:** The task-vs-review contract is asymmetric. The worker is dispatched with QueuedPrompt.suggested_skill (service.rs:459) — the declared procedure it must follow. It therefore cannot verify the result against the SAME skill contract the worker was bound to (expected output format, required evidence, allowed failure classes per the constraints doc 'Aehnliche Massentasks' section). For the recurring skill-task class this is the core hardening gap: review against the skill is the prescribed defense, but the skill identity never reaches the reviewer.
- **Fix:** Thread the worker's declared skill identity into the review request as an explicit hard field (not inference): add executed_skill: Option<String> to CompletionReviewRequest, populate it from job.suggested_skill at the call site, and surface it in build_review_prompt as a named 'Worker skill contract' line so the reviewer reads the same SKILL.md and checks declared required-evidence/output-format. This tightens the existing review prompt, not a new path.
- **Change sketch:** Add `executed_skill: Option<String>` to CompletionReviewRequest (review.rs:120). At service.rs:4999 set executed_skill: job.suggested_skill.clone(). In build_review_prompt (review.rs:806) render a 'Worker skill contract: <skill>' line near 'Review skill:' and an instruction to open and check against that skill's required deliverables/evidence when present. Add review.rs test asserting build_review_prompt includes the declared skill when set and stays generic when None (extends build_review_prompt_uses_metadata_only_and_points_to_skill, review.rs:2054).
- **Prüfsatz:** Q1 hardens build_review_prompt / CompletionReviewRequest. Q2-Q6 unchanged. Q7 keys review context on the explicit declared skill id, not similarity. Q8 directly: Skills become the verifiable source-of-procedure on BOTH worker and reviewer sides. Q9 the executed skill is recorded in the review prompt/audit. Q10 new prompt test pins the symmetry.
- **Risk:** Low — purely additive prompt context; when suggested_skill is None behavior is unchanged. No state-machine or routing change.
- **Verifier guidance:** Keep as-is, with one location correction for the change sketch: the executed_skill field should be populated in the review::CompletionReviewRequest literal in run_completion_review, which begins around service.rs:5004 (the block starting task_goal: job.goal.clone(), task_prompt: job.prompt.clone(), ... — not the cited 4999). Add executed_skill: job.suggested_skill.clone() there alongside the existing review_skill_path. Everything else (new Option<String> field on CompletionReviewRequest, rendering a "Worker skill contract: <skill>" line near "Review skill:" in build_review_prompt with an instruction to open and check against that skill's declared deliverables/evidence when present, and the additive test extending build_review_prompt_uses_metadata_only_and_points_to_skill at review.rs:2054 to assert the line appears when set and stays absent/generic when None) is correct and tight. Keep the field Option<String> so None preserves current behavior exactly. Recommend the reviewer instruction phrase the skill as additional context, not an override of the read-only external-review skill, so it does not weaken the existing "Open the review skill first" binding.
- **Grounding caveat:** All anchors verified by re-opening the code. service.rs:4941-4944 hardcodes review_skill_path = root/skills/system/review/external-review/SKILL.md and never threads job.suggested_skill. CompletionReviewRequest (review.rs:120-143) has no skill field other than review_skill_path. build_review_prompt (review.rs:806) renders only "Review skill: {review_skill_path}" at review.rs:1015 plus "Open the review skill first" (1038) and "infer any required output files from the task contract" (984) — it never renders the worker's declared skill. Test build_review_prompt_uses_metadata_only_and_points_to_skill exists at review.rs:2054. ### `router-dispatch` · `router-1` — Silent loop-active early-return writes no audit/process-mining evidence

🏷 Pass 1 · impact **medium** · effort **S** · verifier **keep**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** 🔵 **DEFER — audit/cosmetic, not hardening** · grounded **partial** · stability **marginal** — Anchors all real and line-drifted only: the loop-active early-return (9115-9117) is genuinely a bare `return Ok(())` that emits no audit/process-mining evidence, and record_event's INSERT OR IGNORE + (mechanism_id, idempotence_key) uniqu...

- [x] **shipped**
- **Anchors:** `src/core/service/service.rs::route_external_messages`, `src/core/service/service.rs::active_agent_loop_in_progress`, `src/core/service/governance.rs::record_event`
- **Problem:** When a worker is active, `route_external_messages` returns at service.rs:9027-9029 with zero evidence. Every other router skip records a governance event (preflight, guard-block, queue-pressure-guard, runtime-backoff), but the single most frequent arbitration decision — 'this tick leased nothing because a turn is in flight' — leaves no durable trace. Process-mining cannot reconstruct how long the serial slot was occupied, how many ticks starved waiting, or whether founder mail sat blocked behind a long task, because the deciding gate is invisible.
- **Fix:** Make the existing serial-router gate auditable without changing its behavior: emit one throttled governance event on the loop-active early-return, keyed so it does not flood. This rides the existing `governance::record_event` sink that process-mining already consumes, and turns an un-mined hot-path decision into Process-Mining evidence (constraints doc line 209/212).
- **Change sketch:** In `route_external_messages`, before `return Ok(())` at the `active_agent_loop_in_progress` branch, call `governance::record_event` with mechanism_id 'channel_router_loop_active', action 'skipped external leasing while an agent loop was active', details {worker_active_count, pending_prompts_len, active_source_label}, and an `idempotence_key` bucketed to a coarse time window (e.g. active_source_label + floor(epoch/300)) so at most one row per 5-min window per active source. No new table, no new mechanism — reuse the same `GovernanceEventRequest` pattern already used 6+ times in this function.
- **Prüfsatz:** Q1 hardens `active_agent_loop_in_progress` gate. Q2 keeps route_external_messages THE hot path (only adds a log line). Q3/Q4/Q5/Q6 untouched. Q7 idempotency on an explicit time-bucketed key, not semantic similarity. Q9 adds the missing Audit/Process-Mining evidence. Q10 testable: a unit test that sets busy=true, calls route_external_messages, and asserts exactly one 'channel_router_loop_active' governance row.
- **Risk:** Low. Pure additive logging behind an idempotence key; the time-bucket prevents audit-table flooding at the 8s poll cadence.
- **Verifier guidance:** Keep the change as scoped — it is grounded, compliant, and unmitigated — but correct two inaccuracies in the writeup before implementing. (1) Drop the false claim that 'every other router skip records a governance event': the sibling queue_pressure_active early-return at service.rs:9034 is ALSO silent, and runtime-backoff/queue-pressure-guard events live in enqueue_prompt/ensure_queue_guard_locked, NOT in route_external_messages. The honest framing is: 'the loop-active AND queue-pressure early-returns are the two un-audited skip paths in this function; only the error-conditioned guard-block and preflight paths emit events.' Consider emitting a parallel throttled event on the queue_pressure_active return at 9034 too, since it has the identical blind-spot. (2) Fix the doc citation: the supporting constraint is harness-hardening-constraints.md line 208 ('Lease- und Repriorisierungsentscheidungen auditierbar machen'), not 209 (line 209 is about prompt rendering). Implementation note: model the new call exactly on the blocked-inbound record_event at service.rs:9148-9163 and key it 'channel_router_loop_active' with idempotence_key = format!('loop-active:{}:{}', active_source_label_or_unknown, epoch/300); test it with the SharedState{busy:true} pattern from service.rs:21930 plus a direct query of governance_events asserting exactly one row.
- **Grounding caveat:** All three anchors exist and the core weakness is real. service.rs:9006 `route_external_messages`; early-return at 9027-9029 (`if active_agent_loop_in_progress(state) { return Ok(()); }`); helper at 9001-9004; governance::record_event at governance.rs:326. The loop-active early-return writes zero audit/process-mining evidence — confirmed it is a bare `return Ok(())`. No `channel_router_loop_active` mechanism exists anywhere (grep clean). record_event supports idempotence-keyed dedupe via INSERT OR IGNORE on a (mechanism_id, idempotence_key) unique index (governance.rs:347-380, schema 592-598), so the proposed 5-min time-bucket throttle is mechanically supported. CAVEAT: the finding's premise that "every other router skip records a governance event (preflight, guard-block, queue-pressure-guard, runtime-backoff)" is overstated/inaccurate. The sibling `queue_pressure_active` early-return at service.rs:9034 is ALSO silent (bare return Ok(())). The runtime_blocker_backoff event fires in enqueue_prompt (9857) and queue_pressure_guard in ensure_queue_guard_locked (14178) — neither is inside route_external_messages. Only handle_channel_router_guard_block (9432) and run_ticket_dispatch_preflight (9522) emit events from within the function, and only on error/issue conditions. The underlying gap is real but the comparative framing is wrong.


### `router-dispatch` · `router-5` — Durable-queue priority leasing order is unpinned by any test

🏷 Pass 1 · impact **medium** · effort **S** · verifier **revise**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** 🔵 **DEFER — audit/cosmetic, not hardening** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **marginal** — Accurately grounded: every anchor, the timestamp-folding scheme, the external_created_at-ASC ORDER BY, the hardcoded 16-row lease window, and the claim that no test pins durable-queue priority lease ordering all verified in live code. Th...

> ⚠️ **Canonical issue:** implement the **Canonical scope** + **Verifier guidance** below. (The stale original Fix/Change-sketch fields were removed in the live re-audit cleanup.)

- [x] **shipped**
- **Canonical scope:** Implement the corrected scope in **Verifier guidance**. Treat the superseded original fix/sketch/test mapping as historical context, not instructions.
- **Canonical verification:** Use the Q10/test instructions in **Verifier guidance**; if they conflict with any superseded original field, Verifier guidance wins.
- **Anchors:** `src/core/mission/channels.rs::queue_sort_at`, `src/core/mission/channels.rs::list_queue_tasks_from_conn_with_statuses`, `src/core/service/service.rs::maybe_lease_next_durable_queue_prompt_for_idle_dispatch`
- **Problem:** Durable-queue priority is implemented implicitly: `queue_sort_at` shifts the timestamp (urgent -24h, high -1h, normal 0, low +1h) and writes it into `external_created_at` (channels.rs:7872, 2322/2613), and `maybe_lease_next_durable_queue_prompt_for_idle_dispatch` leases the first row of `list_queue_tasks(...,16)` ordered by route_status then `external_created_at` ASC. This invariant — 'an urgent durable task is leased before an older normal one' — is correctness-critical for mixed load but is proven by NO test. The in-memory path has 4+ ordering tests (`ordered_pending_prompts_*`), but the durable path has none. A future refactor of `queue_sort_at` or the ORDER BY (e.g. someone 'simplifying' to observed_at) would silently invert priority with no failing test, and a 16-row window cap could let a starving urgent task fall outside the lease window unnoticed.
- **Risk:** Very low. Test-only; writes to test SQLite root per the operator guardrail.
- **Verifier guidance:** Keep the core test — it is a clean, valid hardening. Tighten the changeSketch in two ways. (1) Primary test: in a temp SQLite root, create three pending durable queue tasks out of insertion order with priorities low, normal, urgent via create_queue_task, then assert list_queue_tasks(root,&["pending"],16)[0] is urgent, [1] normal, [2] low (equivalently call maybe_lease_next_durable_queue_prompt_for_idle_dispatch and assert it returns the urgent task first). This directly pins the queue_sort_at folding + ORDER BY external_created_at ASC contract. (2) Drop or re-scope the "second test" as written — the proposed 'urgent behind 16 normals' starvation case is a strawman: because urgent folds to now-24h it always sorts ahead of any normal, so it can never fall outside a 16-row window that is otherwise filled by normals. The real window-cap risk is 16+ tasks of the SAME-or-higher sort_at ahead of a starving task; if you want to cover starvation, assert that an urgent task is still returned when 16+ OTHER urgent (or same-bucket) tasks precede it is NOT guaranteed by the current code — so either (a) drop the second test, or (b) make it a documented known-limitation test that asserts current behavior (the 17th-place task is NOT leased) rather than asserting an invariant the code does not provide. Recommend: ship test (1) only. Also add a tie-break assertion within one priority bucket (older observed_at first) to lock the secondary `m.observed_at ASC` clause.
- **Grounding caveat:** All anchors exist and the weakness is real. queue_sort_at (channels.rs:7872) folds priority into a shifted timestamp (urgent -24h, high -1h, normal 0, low +1h). Both callsites (2267, 2541) write sort_at into external_created_at (confirmed exact at 2322: `external_created_at: &sort_at`). list_queue_tasks_from_conn_with_statuses (7333) orders by route_status CASE then `m.external_created_at ASC` then `m.observed_at ASC`. maybe_lease_next_durable_queue_prompt_for_idle_dispatch (service.rs:9474) leases the first non-inflight row of list_queue_tasks(root,&["pending"],16) — hardcoded 16-row window confirmed. The finding's literal line cites (7872, 2322/2613) have minor drift but the named anchors and the 2322 ref are correct. No test pins durable-queue priority lease ordering: the only multi-priority test (queue_tasks_round_trip_through_channel_store, 8689) asserts stored `priority` value and single-row round-trip, not lease order; the 4 ordered_pending_prompts_* tests (service.rs:17546+) are the in-memory pending_prompts path; queue_priority_rank (service.rs:10269) is a separate ticket-self-work selection mechanism, not the durable lease path.


### `router-dispatch` · `router-6` — Inbound dispatch sort happens AFTER lease, so cross-source priority isn't an exclusivity invariant

🏷 Pass 1 · impact **medium** · effort **M** · verifier **revise**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** 🔵 **DEFER — audit/cosmetic, not hardening** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **marginal** — Grounded and accurately framed (after the Verifier-guidance correction): with limit=1 the Rust source-rank sort at service.rs:9221 is a verified no-op, take_messages SQL (channels.rs:6645/6739) has no source-rank term, and lease_pending_...

> ⚠️ **Canonical issue:** implement the **Canonical scope** + **Verifier guidance** below. (The stale original Fix/Change-sketch fields were removed in the live re-audit cleanup.)

- [ ] **open**
- **Canonical scope:** Implement the corrected scope in **Verifier guidance**. Treat the superseded original fix/sketch/test mapping as historical context, not instructions.
- **Canonical verification:** Use the Q10/test instructions in **Verifier guidance**; if they conflict with any superseded original field, Verifier guidance wins.
- **Anchors:** `src/core/service/service.rs::route_external_messages`, `src/core/service/service.rs::source_label_dispatch_rank`, `src/core/mission/channels.rs::lease_pending_inbound_messages`
- **Problem:** At service.rs:9128 the router leases up to `CHANNEL_ROUTER_SERIAL_LEASE_LIMIT=1` inbound messages and THEN sorts the returned vec by `source_label_dispatch_rank` (9133-9137). With limit 1 the sort is a no-op: `take_messages` already picked the single highest-ranked-per-thread row by its own SQL ordering (route_status, then channel-specific created_at), which does NOT encode founder/owner vs newsletter source rank. So which inbound message wins the single serial slot is decided by `take_messages`' SQL, not by `source_label_dispatch_rank` — the Rust-side priority sort only matters if limit>1. There is no test asserting that, given a founder email and a newsletter both pending, the founder email is the one leased. The intended priority is real (rank table at 9920) but it is applied to a 1-element list.
- **Risk:** Medium. The rank source lives in service settings, while the lease SQL lives in channels; the fix must keep those definitions consistent rather than copying a second role classifier. Persisted rank needs migration/backfill; threaded policy needs a clean API boundary.
- **Verifier guidance:** Real gap, but the finding overstates it as purely "decorative" and ignores the queued_prompt_dispatch_rank layer (service.rs:9904-9982) that DOES enforce founder>newsletter once both are leased. Tighten the framing and narrow the claim: the residual, unhardened gap is ONLY the first-selection-while-idle case — when the service is not busy, the single message pulled by take_messages this tick is chosen by recency, so an idle newsletter can be leased+dispatched before the founder is ever leased, costing the founder a full turn. The in-memory queue rank covers the busy-backlog case but not this one. Avoid window-lease-then-ack-losers-back-to-pending; it re-touches leases and is unnecessary if the lease ORDER BY can be made rank-aware. But the role rank source must be bridged explicitly: the service-side classification depends on email-role settings, while `take_messages` lives in channels. Preferred implementation is to persist a normalized source_rank/source_label at ingest and order on that field in both `take_messages` branches; acceptable alternative is to pass a rank policy/settings handle into the lease API. Do not duplicate a second founder/owner classifier in SQL. Required test: seed settings plus an owner/founder email and a newer generic/newsletter email as two distinct pending inbound threads, call lease_pending_inbound_messages(root,1,owner) on an idle root, assert the leased message_key is the founder's — this is what no current test covers (17396/17405/17435 only test the rank/label functions in isolation).
- **Grounding caveat:** Anchors verified at service.rs:9006/9128-9137/9915 and channels.rs:2008/6557/6739-6750; problem holds — limit=1 makes the Rust sort a no-op and take_messages SQL has no source-rank term; no founder-vs-newsletter lease-selection test exists.

- [x] **shipped** — `job.suggested_skill` is validated against the catalog once at the prompt-worker boundary (new pub `skill_store::skill_bundle_exists` over `ctox_skill_bundles`); on absence `record_skill_bound_missing_flow_event` emits exactly one `skill.bound_missing` harness-flow event chained on the leased message key + work item (same chaining as skills-5), with `{skill, source_label}` metadata. The dispatch hint still renders — a missing skill degrades, not aborts — and a catalog-lookup error surfaces a feed event instead of a false `bound_missing`. - **Canonical scope:** Implement the corrected scope in **Verifier guidance**. Treat the superseded original fix/sketch/test mapping as historical context, not instructions.

### `turn-loop-context` · `turnloop-5` — Exact-token overflow collapses to AgentOutcome::ExecutionError; empty-selection remains a retry-policy decision

- [x] **shipped** — `AgentOutcome::ContextRejected` (lcm.rs enum + as_str/from_token; `is_agent_failure` stays true) is a dedicated class for a deterministic exact-token context overflow. `classify_agent_failure` (service.rs) maps the `context_preflight_exact_overflow` marker to it before the `ExecutionError` fallthrough; `runtime_error_is_transient_api_failure` already excludes the marker (now pinned by a test). The AgentOutcome enum has no variant distinguishing a deterministic context/budget reject from a generic runtime crash, so process-mining and the agent_failure counter cannot tell 'we keep overflowing the context budget' apart from 'the backend crashed'. `context_selection_empty` is related, but existing code/tests currently treat it as a transient retry-policy case; include it only with an explicit policy/test update.

AgentOutcome (lcm.rs:91-102) has exactly 5 variants, none for a context/budget reject; as_str/from_token (lcm.rs:107-127) are the only exhaustive matches, and is_agent_failure is `!Success` so a new variant stays a failure automatically. - **Anchors:** `src/core/execution/agent/turn_loop.rs::detect_durable_state_transition`, `src/core/execution/agent/turn_loop.rs:662`
- **Problem:** detect_durable_state_transition runs three SQL probes (self-work closed, knowledge added, focus commits) and the caller wraps the whole thing in .unwrap_or(false) (turn_loop.rs:662). Inside, individual query_row failures are also .unwrap_or(0). The code comments record that a prior version had a wrong column/kind and 'the error was swallowed into no boundary' — i.e. this exact swallowing already shipped a regression where boundary refreshes silently stopped. Today any future schema drift (renamed table, changed kind casing) again degrades to 'never refresh on transition' with zero operator-visible signal, because the only trace is the absence of a continuity-refresh phase event.
- **Risk:** Low. Behavior-preserving for the happy path; only adds an event and changes an internal return type. The .unwrap_or(false) default is retained so a fresh install with missing tables still degrades gracefully.
- **Verifier guidance:** Keep the core change (return a struct carrying detected:bool + probe_errors so an errored query is distinguished from an empty one, retaining default-false graceful degradation), but fix two factual defects in the sketch:\n\n1) The proposed emit(\"boundary-detection-degraded ...\") does NOT create auditable / process-mining evidence. emit() flows to service.rs:3381 push_event, which lands in SharedState.recent_events — a 24-slot in-memory ring buffer (service.rs:14074-14079, pop_front at len>=24) plus the live status feed. It is ephemeral and is NOT consumed by process_mining.rs (that reads ctox_process_events triggers, not phase events). So delete the \"auditable evidence / Process-Mining can flag chronic detection faults\" framing in the opportunity and Q9. For a durable operator signal, route the degraded case to eprintln! (captured in service logs, the same channel already used at turn_loop.rs:606) and/or to the real audit/process-event sink if a durable record is actually wanted — do not claim auditability from the phase event alone.\n\n2) The test must assert on the FUNCTION'S RETURN VALUE, not on the volatile phase event. Tighten it: open an LCM/mission DB with ticket_self_work_items (or continuity_documents) absent, call the (newly struct-returning) detect_durable_state_transition, and assert probe_errors is non-empty while detected stays false. Asserting \"the degraded phase event fires\" (as the sketch proposes) would test an ephemeral ring-buffer entry and couple the unit test to service-layer wiring.\n\nWith those two corrections the finding is a clean, behavior-preserving observability hardening of the documented prior-regression site.
- **Grounding caveat:** Anchors verified exactly. detect_durable_state_transition is at turn_loop.rs:144-219; the caller wraps it in .unwrap_or(false) at line 662 (confirmed). All three probes use .unwrap_or(0) (lines 170, 180, 212), so an errored query (missing table/column, parse failure) is collapsed into the same "0 rows" path as a legitimate empty result, and the whole function further collapses any Err into false. The documented prior-regression comment is real (lines 199-202: a previous capitalized-kind query joining nonexistent d.id "errored and the error was swallowed into 'no boundary'"). The named test focus_commit_boundary_detection_compares_epoch_millis exists at line 1584. The weakness (future schema drift silently degrades to "never refresh on transition" with no operator signal) holds as stated.



### `compaction-internals` · `lcm-x2` — query_row(...).unwrap_or(1) masks DB errors; keep as cleanup under lcm-x1

🏷 Pass 2 · impact **low** · effort **S** · kind **concurrency** · verifier **revise**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** 🔵 **DEFER — audit/cosmetic, not hardening** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **marginal** — This ticket is unusual: it has already been adversarially re-scoped, and that re-scoping is itself accurate. Every anchor verified at the exact cited line (no drift). The core smell is real — query_row(...).unwrap_or(1) at lcm.rs:1103 an...

> ⚠️ **Canonical issue:** implement the **Canonical scope** + **Verifier guidance** below. (The stale original Fix/Change-sketch fields were removed in the live re-audit cleanup.)

- [x] **shipped** — `add_message_with_outcome` (lcm.rs:1118-1155) now wraps the seq-read + message + FTS + ordinal-read + context_items inserts in one `unchecked_transaction()`, and the seq/ordinal reads propagate via `?`/`.context(...)?` instead of `query_row(...).unwrap_or(1)` (the magic value masked a real busy/IO error as a spurious UNIQUE/PK violation). Regression test `add_message_with_outcome_rolls_back_on_partial_failure` (lcm.rs:7233) forces the context_items step to fail and asserts zero orphan `messages`/`messages_fts` rows.
- **Canonical scope:** Implement the corrected scope in **Verifier guidance**. Treat the superseded original fix/sketch/test mapping as historical context, not instructions.
- **Canonical verification:** Use the Q10/test instructions in **Verifier guidance**; if they conflict with any superseded original field, Verifier guidance wins.
- **Anchors:** `lcm.rs seq unwrap_or(1) (1096-1103)`, `lcm.rs::next_context_ordinal unwrap_or(1) (3070-3079)`, `idx_messages_conversation_seq UNIQUE (804), context_items PK (839)`
- **Problem:** MAX(seq)+1 and next_context_ordinal already use COALESCE for the empty-table case, so `.unwrap_or(1)` fires only on genuine DB errors (30s-exhausted lock, IO, schema/corruption). It masks that error with a magic value and may convert the real failure into a misleading UNIQUE/PK failure. The orphaned-row hazard is the separate `lcm-x1` transaction bug, not caused by this fallback.
- **Verifier guidance:** Real but the fix framing, severity, and mechanism are wrong. CORRECTED VERSION: The legitimate, narrow hardening is 'replace query_row(...).unwrap_or(1) with ? at lcm.rs:1103 and 3078' — propagating a genuine DB error is strictly better than substituting magic value 1, which derives a spurious UNIQUE/PK violation from a real busy/IO error and (for run_add_message) lets turn_loop.rs:759-778 retry on the wrong error class. That is a valid behavior-/persistence-preserving cleanup. BUT downgrade impact from high to low and effort to S: busy_timeout=30s (persistence.rs:34) absorbs ordinary cross-process contention, the only realistic Err is a 30s-stuck lock or true IO/corruption (rare), and the run_add_message path already retries. DROP the three overstated harm claims: 'recoverable lock' (it is a 30s-exhausted lock), the orphan attribution (caused by missing transaction, not by unwrap_or), and 'corrupts ordering' (unrealizable — no DELETE FROM messages). The SHARPER, properly-grounded finding hiding underneath is the actual gap: add_message_with_outcome inserts messages + messages_fts + context_items as separate auto-commit statements with NO transaction, so a failure at the ordinal/context_items step (1128-1133) leaves an orphaned message row (and a messages_fts row with no context item). The right fix is to wrap the message+FTS+ordinal+context_items inserts in a single self.conn.unchecked_transaction() (the same pattern already used at lcm.rs:1434/1499/1556) so the row set is atomic, AND swap the two unwrap_or(1) for ?. Fix the test sketch accordingly: assert that (a) a held write-lock exhausting busy_timeout causes add_message_with_outcome to return Err with NO partial row written (transaction rolled back), and (b) on success the message and its context_item are both present — not 'a row at MAX(seq)+1' under a lock, which cannot happen with ?.
- **Grounding caveat:** All anchors verified and accurate: lcm.rs:1096-1103 (seq = COALESCE(MAX(seq),0)+1 query .unwrap_or(1)), lcm.rs:3070-3079 (next_context_ordinal .unwrap_or(1)), schema UNIQUE idx_messages_conversation_seq at 804 and context_items PK at 839, mission_start_seq dependency at live_context.rs:870-875. The core smell is real: query_row(...).unwrap_or(1) masks a genuine DB error (busy/IO/corruption) with the magic value 1 instead of propagating it; COALESCE already covers empty-table so unwrap_or(1) fires ONLY on error. BUT the finding's harm mechanism is substantially overstated/misattributed: (1) the connection sets busy_timeout=30s (persistence.rs:34, lcm.rs:731) — a query_row error therefore reflects a 30s-EXHAUSTED lock, not a 'transient recoverable lock'; SQLite blocks/retries internally before returning Err. (2) The message-orphan claim is real but is a PRE-EXISTING no-transaction bug, NOT caused by unwrap_or(1): add_message_with_outcome runs the message INSERT (1110), FTS INSERT (1124), ordinal query (1128) and context_items INSERT (1129) as separate auto-commit statements (no unchecked_transaction wraps this region), so ANY ordinal-step failure — whether a propagated busy error via ? or a fabricated PK collision — orphans the already-committed message row equally. Replacing unwrap_or with ? does NOT close that orphan window. (3) The 'non-colliding seq=1 corrupts ordering' case requires an empty-conversation-with-error (where seq=1 is actually correct) or a deleted seq=1 gap; there is no DELETE FROM messages path, so this is effectively unrealizable.

### `spawn-liveness-subagents` · `liveness-6` — Agent-job worker spawn failures are per-item terminal; no bounded retry on transient spawn errors

🏷 Pass 1 · impact **low** · effort **M** · verifier **revise**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** 🔵 **DEFER — audit/cosmetic, not hardening** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **marginal** — All three anchors and the behavioral claim are verified true against live code: non-AgentLimitReached spawn errors mark the item Failed on the first occurrence (agent_jobs.rs:658-668) and the loop never reads item.attempt_count except fo...

> ⚠️ **Canonical issue:** implement the **Canonical scope** + **Verifier guidance** below. (The stale original Fix/Change-sketch fields were removed in the live re-audit cleanup.)

- [ ] **open**
- **Canonical scope:** Implement the corrected scope in **Verifier guidance**. Treat the superseded original fix/sketch/test mapping as historical context, not instructions.
- **Canonical verification:** Use the Q10/test instructions in **Verifier guidance**; if they conflict with any superseded original field, Verifier guidance wins.
- **Anchors:** `src/core/harness/core/src/tools/handlers/agent_jobs.rs:658 (Err(err) => mark_agent_job_item_failed)`, `src/core/harness/core/src/tools/handlers/agent_jobs.rs:649 (AgentLimitReached => mark pending, requeue)`, `src/core/harness/state/src/runtime/agent_jobs.rs (attempt_count column)`
- **Problem:** In run_agent_job_loop, AgentLimitReached correctly requeues the item as pending (agent_jobs.rs:649-657), but ANY other spawn error (agent_jobs.rs:658-668) immediately marks the item Failed and continues. The item carries an attempt_count (rendered to CSV at agent_jobs.rs:1178) but the loop never consults it — a single transient spawn error (e.g. a momentary thread-manager hiccup) terminally fails a row that a bounded retry would recover. The job-level contract is 'finite drain', and a bounded per-item retry on transient spawn failure would tighten that drain's robustness while staying finite (Q6: rework bounded to the same item).
- **Risk:** must cap strictly on attempt_count so a permanently-failing spawn cannot loop forever; the retry path must not reset attempt_count and must yield/back off rather than hammering spawn_agent in a tight loop.
- **Verifier guidance:** The weakness is real, but the proposed changeSketch is BROKEN and would introduce a worse bug — an infinite busy-loop — which is exactly the risk the finding itself flags. Two concrete defects when re-reading the code:

1. Wrong termination claim. The changeSketch asserts "mark_agent_job_item_running_with_thread already increments attempts on each assignment, so termination is guaranteed." False. In the for-loop (agent_jobs.rs:630-699) the item is read as Pending (list filter Some(Pending), line 626) and `mark_agent_job_item_running_with_thread` runs ONLY after a SUCCESSFUL spawn (line 670). On `Err(err)` (line 658) the spawn failed before line 670, so attempt_count is NEVER incremented for the spawn-failure case.

2. Proposed requeue is a no-op. `mark_agent_job_item_pending` (state/agent_jobs.rs:372-399) has `WHERE ... AND status = ?` bound to `Running` (line 395). The spawn-failed item is still `Pending`, so this UPDATE affects 0 rows and changes nothing. Result: the loop re-reads the same Pending item with the same attempt_count next iteration, spawn fails again, and with `progressed=true` it skips `wait_for_status_change` (guarded by `if !progressed` at line 727) — a tight busy-loop hammering spawn_agent with zero backoff, forever. This is precisely the "must cap strictly so a permanently-failing spawn cannot loop forever" risk the finding raises, triggered by its own fix.

Corrected, tighter version: (a) Add a state-layer mutation that operates on the CURRENTLY-Pending spawn-failed item and atomically bumps the retry counter AND records last_error — e.g. `mark_agent_job_item_spawn_retry(job_id, item_id, error_message)` with `UPDATE ... SET attempt_count = attempt_count + 1, last_error = ?, updated_at = ? WHERE job_id = ? AND item_id = ? AND status = 'pending'` (note WHERE status = Pending, not Running). (b) In the Err(err) arm read `item.attempt_count`; if `attempt_count + 1 < MAX_SPAWN_ATTEMPTS` (typed const, no env read) call the new retry mutation (which increments → guarantees the cap is reached), else call mark_agent_job_item_failed as today. (c) Do NOT set `progressed = true` on the retry branch, or add explicit backoff before re-spawn, so the loop yields via wait_for_status_change instead of busy-spinning. (d) Q10 test must assert BOTH: an item failing to spawn exactly MAX times ends Failed, AND attempt_count strictly monotonically increases across retries (proving termination) — write test fixtures to the SQLite runtime store, not std::env. Keep impact=low; the corrected effort is closer to M-but-careful because it requires a new audited state mutation, not reuse of the existing pending mutation.
- **Grounding caveat:** All three anchors verified against current code. agent_jobs.rs:658 is the `Err(err) =>` arm that calls `mark_agent_job_item_failed` and `continue` (handlers/agent_jobs.rs:658-668). agent_jobs.rs:649 is `Err(CodexErr::AgentLimitReached { .. })` which calls `mark_agent_job_item_pending` then `break` (649-657). state/src/runtime/agent_jobs.rs has the `attempt_count` column (lines 71/146/189) and it is incremented ONLY in `mark_agent_job_item_running` (line 326) and `mark_agent_job_item_running_with_thread` (line 355). The weakness is REAL: grep confirms the loop never reads `item.attempt_count` outside CSV rendering (only lines 1142/1178), so any non-limit transient spawn error terminally fails the row that a bounded retry could recover.

### `state-machine-guards` · `spawn-contract-entity-pin-1` — Spawn-contract entity strings are unaudited free-form vocabulary; typos fail closed but are not pinned

🏷 Pass 1 · impact **low** · effort **S** · verifier **revise**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** ⬜ **DROP — not worth doing** · grounded **partial** · stability **marginal** — Anchors all real and the mechanical observation is accurate: the spawn vocabulary is free-form &'static str with no proof-time membership check. But the original headline ("no consistency check against CoreEntityType" / silently disables...

> ⚠️ **Canonical issue:** implement the **Canonical scope** + **Verifier guidance** below. (The stale original Fix/Change-sketch fields were removed in the live re-audit cleanup.)

- [x] **shipped** — `SPAWN_ENTITY_TYPES` (core_transition_guard.rs) is the closed spawn vocabulary enumerated from the real contracts (not `CoreEntityType` — a deliberately separate, broader space), and `analyze_spawner_contracts` (split out of `analyze_core_spawn_model`) flags any contract parent/child entity-type outside it (allowing `"*"`) as `spawner_contract_unregistered_entity_type:<pattern>:<type>`. Test `spawn_contract_entity_types_are_a_closed_vocabulary` pins: live contracts stay healthy, a `"Workitem"` typo flips `report.ok` with the specific violation, and `"*"` stays allowed + healthy. Optional callsite-threading deferred (touches the parallel agent's `tickets.rs`).
- **Canonical scope:** Implement the corrected scope in **Verifier guidance**. Treat the superseded original fix/sketch/test mapping as historical context, not instructions.
- **Canonical verification:** Use the Q10/test instructions in **Verifier guidance**; if they conflict with any superseded original field, Verifier guidance wins.
- **Anchors:** `src/core/service/core_transition_guard.rs::core_spawner_contracts (line 715, e.g. parent_entity_types: &["WorkItem", "QueueTask", "Thread", ...])`, `src/core/service/core_transition_guard.rs::validate_core_spawn (parent/child membership check, lines 637-649)`, `src/core/service/core_transition_guard.rs::analyze_core_spawn_model (line 513)`
- **Problem:** core_spawner_contracts uses bare string literals ('WorkItem','QueueTask','Thread','Message','ControlPlane','IotAlarm','PlanStep','ScheduleTask','WebStackTask') for parent_entity_types/child_entity_type, and validate_core_spawn compares request strings to these. analyze_core_spawn_model checks that the lists are non-empty and the intervention skill is approved, but it never checks that the entity-type strings are members of a closed, known spawn vocabulary. A caller passing parent_entity_type="Workitem" (case/typo) or a contract literal drifting from the caller's literal yields spawn_parent_type_not_registered — a fail-closed wrong rejection, not a guard bypass — and nothing catches the mismatch at proof time.
- **Risk:** Low — additive static check; must enumerate the real vocabulary from current contracts and callsites so it does not flag a legitimate type.
- **Verifier guidance:** Real but the framing is wrong and must be corrected before keeping. Two fixes: (1) Drop the "CoreEntityType" framing entirely — the spawn vocabulary is deliberately a separate, broader space than the state-machine's CoreEntityType enum (QueueTask vs QueueItem; Thread/Message/ControlPlane/IotAlarm/PlanStep/ScheduleTask/WebStackTask have no CoreEntityType counterpart). Do NOT validate spawn strings against CoreEntityType or core_entity_types() — that would flag every legitimate contract. (2) Restate impact honestly: a typo fails CLOSED (spawn_parent_type_not_registered → rejected at validate_core_spawn:643/648), so this is a maintainability / wrong-rejection bug and an unaudited-vocabulary gap, NOT a guard bypass that "silently disables guarding." Tightened change: add `const SPAWN_ENTITY_TYPES: &[&str] = &["WorkItem","QueueTask","Thread","Message","ControlPlane","IotAlarm","PlanStep","ScheduleTask","WebStackTask"];` (enumerated from the real contracts at lines 722-814, NOT from CoreEntityType), and in analyze_core_spawn_model push a violation for any contract whose parent_entity_types/child_entity_type contains a string not in SPAWN_ENTITY_TYPES (allow "*"). Extend the existing core_spawn_model_proves_registered_interventions_are_bounded test with a deliberately-mistyped contract asserting report.ok becomes false. Optional but recommended given the cross-file re-typing at the callsites (channels.rs/tickets.rs/iot/conditions.rs/service.rs): expose the vocabulary as the single source so callsites reference it, otherwise the static check only covers contract literals and the callsite-vs-contract drift it cites remains uncaught. Scope this as S/low-impact maintainability hardening, not a security finding.
- **Grounding caveat:** Anchors all verified. core_spawner_contracts at core_transition_guard.rs:715 uses bare &'static str literals for parent_entity_types/child_entity_type (lines 722-814). validate_core_spawn parent/child membership check confirmed at lines 637-649 (string ==, with "*" wildcard). analyze_core_spawn_model at line 513 checks only: non-empty pattern/child/parent (520-535), budget range (536), intervention_skill in {queue-cleanup,harness-self-audit} (542) and its SKILL.md contract text (550-575) — it NEVER validates entity-type strings against any closed vocabulary. Callsites independently re-type the same literals (channels.rs:2404/2776/2866/2990, tickets.rs:2912, iot/conditions.rs:1077, service.rs:11923) so cross-side drift is genuinely possible; harness_spawn_liveness.rs even uses an entirely different string ("AgentJob") proving the space is unbounded/unaudited. BUT the finding's title/problem premise — "no consistency check against CoreEntityType" — is FALSE as stated: CoreEntityType (core_state_machine.rs:12) = {Service,Mission,Context,QueueItem,WorkItem,Ticket,Review,FounderCommunication,Commitment,Schedule,Knowledge,Repair} is a DIFFERENT, near-disjoint vocabulary from the spawn space {WorkItem,QueueTask,Thread,Message,ControlPlane,IotAlarm,PlanStep,ScheduleTask,WebStackTask} — only WorkItem overlaps; QueueItem≠QueueTask. Checking spawn strings against CoreEntityType would wrongly flag every legit contract. The mechanical weakness (unenumerated free-form spawn vocabulary, no proof-time membership check) is real; the CoreEntityType framing is wrong.


### `integration-metaguards` · `X3` — terminal_reaped_at on ctox_core_spawn_edges is a dead column with a misleading projection (no writer, ignored by budget count)

🏷 Pass 2 · impact **low** · effort **S** · kind **dead-code** · verifier **keep**/high-conf
🔎 **Live re-audit (3rd pass):** ⬜ **DROP — not worth doing** · grounded **confirmed** · stability **marginal** — Every factual claim is grounded in live code: the column is declared, never written (zero UPDATE statements; INSERT omits it from columns and the ON CONFLICT SET), ignored by the budget count (WHERE accepted=1 only), projected as always-...

- [ ] **open**
- **Anchors:** `src/core/service/core_transition_guard.rs:121 (ctox_core_spawn_edges.terminal_reaped_at TEXT)`, `src/core/service/core_transition_guard.rs:855 (accepted_spawn_budget_count — counts accepted edges, ignores terminal_reaped_at)`, `src/core/service/process_mining.rs:1102 (spawn-edges CLI SELECTs terminal_reaped_at)`, `src/core/service/process_mining.rs:1128 (projects terminal_reaped_at into spawn-edges JSON output)`, `src/apps/desktop/src/db_reader.rs:1695 (desktop reader struct field terminal_reaped_at)`
- **Problem:** ctox_core_spawn_edges.terminal_reaped_at is declared in the guard schema and projected into both the `ctox process-mining spawn-edges` CLI JSON and the desktop db_reader struct — advertising a reaping / budget-release lifecycle. But there is no UPDATE on ctox_core_spawn_edges anywhere in the tree (verified: zero `UPDATE ctox_core_spawn_edges` statements), so the column is always NULL, and the spawn-budget gate accepted_spawn_budget_count counts ALL accepted edges regardless of reaping. The column is pure dead schema that misrepresents the spawn-edge model to anyone reading the CLI/desktop output (it implies terminal edges can be reaped to free budget; they cannot). Pass-1's rejected 'spawn-reaper budget leak' note concerns the intended permanent liveness bound — this finding is narrower and orthogonal: a never-written column with a lying projection, not a budget-behavior change.
- **Fix:** Behavior- and persistence-preserving cleanup: keep the schema column in place, but remove the dead always-NULL field from the spawn-edges CLI SELECT/projection and desktop reader struct so no user-facing surface advertises a reaping lifecycle the guard does not honor. Do not add a writer and do not drop the column in this ticket.
- **Change sketch:** Remove `terminal_reaped_at` from the spawn-edges CLI SELECT/projection (process_mining.rs:1102/1128) and from SpawnEdgeRow/query_spawn_edges (db_reader.rs:1695/1921/1943). Leave `terminal_reaped_at TEXT` in the CREATE TABLE to avoid a schema migration. Add a guard test that the spawn-edges projection contains only fields with a defined writer. No transition/spawn/audit behavior changes.
- **Prüfsatz:** Hardens the ctox_core_spawn_edges projection surface and accepted_spawn_budget_count's documented contract; route_external_messages untouched; no new work/status/spawn paths; core SM and Core Spawn Guard behavior unchanged (budget math already ignores the column); no semantic equality; Skills untouched; this is Process-Mining/Audit surface honesty; a projection-vs-writer guard test proves no dead field is re-advertised.
- **Risk:** Low if done as projection-removal (no schema migration). A real DROP COLUMN needs the standard column-exists-tolerant migration; given the column is always NULL, removing it from projections is the zero-risk path. Do NOT add a writer — that would change the intended permanent spawn-budget bound.
- **Verifier guidance:** Real but low-value. Scope tightening: the user-visible "misleading projection" exists ONLY in the `ctox process-mining spawn-edges` CLI JSON (process_mining.rs:1102/1128), which emits `terminal_reaped_at: null` advertising a reaping lifecycle the guard never honors. The desktop side (db_reader.rs:1695/1921/1943 -> SpawnEdgeRow) is merely a dead struct field — forensics.rs render_spawn_edges never displays it, so there is no desktop-facing lie, just unused parsing. Preferred fix = the projection-removal path the finding already calls zero-risk: drop the column from the CLI SELECT+JSON (process_mining.rs:1102/1128) and from SpawnEdgeRow/query_spawn_edges (db_reader.rs:1695/1921/1943); leave the CREATE TABLE column in place to avoid any DROP COLUMN migration. Add the proposed guard test asserting the spawn-edges CLI projection contains only fields with a defined writer. Do NOT pursue the DROP COLUMN branch and do NOT add a writer. Keep, treating it as a small audit-surface honesty cleanup.
- **Grounding caveat:** All anchors verified. core_transition_guard.rs:121 declares `terminal_reaped_at TEXT`; the production INSERT at :448-454 omits it from both the column list and the `ON CONFLICT DO UPDATE SET` clause, so it is always NULL. `grep -rn "UPDATE ctox_core_spawn_edges"` returns zero hits — no writer exists. accepted_spawn_budget_count (:855) counts `WHERE accepted = 1` and never references the column. process_mining.rs:1102/1128 do SELECT and project it into the `ctox process-mining spawn-edges` JSON as an always-null field. db_reader.rs:1695/1921/1943 carry it into SpawnEdgeRow. Note: forensics.rs render_spawn_edges does NOT display it, so the desktop side is a dead struct field, not a user-visible projection; the only place it is actually advertised to a reader is the CLI JSON.
